Agent's Deviation in Quality: When Does the Purchase Bind the Principal?
Intra-madhhab dispute regarding agent's purchase at better price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when an agent deviates in quality and apply the distinction between exceeding in quantity vs. diminishing in quality.

Core Idea
Beneficial excess binds the principal; inferior quality does not—the principal's objective is paramount.

This passage from al-Hidayah resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute about when an agent's actions bind the principal. Imam Abu Yusuf raised an objection using the example of selling a slave for more than instructed. The author clarifies the distinction and introduces a critical nuance: if the agent buys inferior quality, the purchase is on the agent, not the principal.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa: if the agent exceeds the order but benefits the principal (e.g., buys more quantity for the same price), the purchase binds the principal.
This is based on the analogy with selling a slave for a higher price.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Imam Abu Yusuf argued that the excess belongs to the principal in the sale case, so by analogy, the extra quantity in a purchase should also not bind the principal.
He cited the slave sale example to support non-binding.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes between a sale (where excess price is the principal's property) and a purchase (where extra quantity benefits the principal). However, if the agent deviates in quality (inferior meat), the purchase is on the agent because the principal's objective (quality) is not met.
The author of al-Hidayah adds the quality condition.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: If the agent buys more at the same total price, it binds the principal (Abu Hanifa) vs. it does not bind (Abu Yusuf). But if quality is inferior, it is on the agent by consensus.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that beneficial excess binds the principal, but with the condition that the quality matches the principal's implicit expectation.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف ما استشهد ..... الخ سے امام ابو یوسف کی تمثیل کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب ایک شخص نے دوسر۔ شخص کو ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض اپنا غلام فروخت کرنے کا وکیل کیا مگر وکیل نے اس کو دو ہزار روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کر دیا تو ایک ہزا رو پیزا ائد موکل کے لئے اس لئے ہوگا کہ ایک ہزار روپیہ مؤکل کی ملک کا بدل ہے تو یہ بھی مؤکل کے لئے ملک ہوگا اور وکیل اس زیادی کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر وکیل نے ہیں درہم کے عوض میں رطل ایسا گوشت خرید ا جو عام طور پر اسی بھاؤ بکتا ہے تو اس صورت میں بالا جمار یہ گوشت اپنے واسطے خریدنے والا ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں وکیل نے موکل کے امر کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ موکل کا امرائیے موٹے تازے گوشت کو شامل تھا جو ایک درہم کے عوض میں رطل بکتا ہے مگر اس نے ایسا گھٹیا گوشت خریدا ہے جو ایک درہم کے عوض بیر طل بکتا ہے تو اس صورت میں موکل کا مقصود حاصل نہیں ہوا ۔ اور جب موکل کا مقصود حاصل نہیں ہوا تو یہ خریداری موکل پر نافذ نہ ہوگی بلکہ وکیل پر نافذ ہوگی۔
The response to what was cited as evidence from Imam Abu Yusuf's example: The summary of the response is that when a person appointed someone as agent to sell his slave for 1000 rupees, but the agent sold it for 2000 rupees, then the 1000 rupees belongs to the principal because it is the price of the principal's property, so it is owned by the principal, and the agent has no right to the excess. The author of al-Hidayah said: If the agent bought 15 ratl of meat for one dirham of the type that is commonly sold at that price, then in that case, by consensus, this meat is for the agent himself. Because in this case, the agent has disobeyed the principal's command. That is, the principal's command included fatty fresh meat that sells for 15 ratl per dirham, but the agent bought inferior meat that sells for 15 ratl per dirham. So in this case the principal's objective is not achieved. And when the principal's objective is not achieved, this purchase will not be binding on the principal but on the agent.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling when an agent exceeds the order but at a better price. The author first responds to an example cited by Imam Abu Yusuf in support of a different view. The response clarifies that in the slave sale case, the excess price (1000 dirhams) does not belong to the agent but to the principal because it is part of the sale price. However, the ruling that the sale binds the principal is correct. The main point is that this analogy does not apply to the purchase case of the meat because the principal's objective in the purchase case is to get the specified quantity and quality, not just any meat. Then the author of al-Hidayah introduces a nuance: if the agent buys the same quantity but of inferior quality (i.e., poor quality meat that is cheaper in the market), then the purchase is on the agent, not the principal. This is because the principal commanded the purchase of good quality meat, and the agent's deviation in quality violates the command, even if the quantity is the same. So the distinction is between exceeding in quantity with benefit (which binds the principal) and diminishing in quality with loss (which is on the agent).

Key Terms
استشهد (istashhada): To cite a proof or example as evidence. Here it refers to Imam Abu Yusuf's cited example.
تمثیل (tamthil): An example used to illustrate a legal point.
بالاجماع (bil-ijma'): By consensus of the scholars, referring to the ruling on the slave sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an agent is told to buy high-quality meat for 1 dirham, but he buys low-quality meat for 1 dirham, what is the ruling?
A) The purchase binds the principal
B) The purchase is void
C) The purchase is on the agent
D) The agent must ask for permission

Key Takeaway
An agent who buys inferior quality violates the principal's implied command; the purchase is on the agent, not the principal.

The Agent's Prohibition from Purchasing the Specified Item for Himself
Ruling with proof on agent self-purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent buying a specified item for himself and explain the proofs based on presence and deception.

Core Idea
An agent cannot profit from the principal's trust by buying the specified item for himself in the principal's absence.

Agency in Hanafi fiqh is built on trust. When a principal appoints an agent to purchase a specific item, the agent's role is limited to serving the principal. This lesson examines the rule that the agent may not buy that specified item for himself, especially when the principal is absent. The ruling is based on preventing deception and respecting the contractual bond.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is: an agent appointed to buy a specified item (shay' bi'aynihi) purchasing that item for himself. The Hanafi ruling is that it is prohibited (haram) in the principal's absence.
The prohibition is not because of a defect in the sale but due to breach of trust.
2
Understand the first proof: deception
The agent's self-purchase constitutes taghreer (deception) because the principal relied on him. Deception of a Muslim is impermissible (haram) and makes the transaction invalid for the agent.
The purchase is not void but invalid for the agent; it binds the principal.
3
Understand the second proof: dismissal without consent
Buying for himself amounts to the agent dismissing himself (azl nafsihi) from agency. A contract can only be rescinded with the other party's knowledge. In the principal's absence, the agent cannot unilaterally terminate.
Self-dismissal is akin to faskh al-aqd, which requires mutual consent.
4
Distinguish when it is allowed
If the principal is present and the agent explicitly declares he is buying for himself, the purchase is valid for the agent because the principal's presence allows immediate consent or objection.
Presence removes the elements of deception and unilateral dismissal.
5
Apply the ruling to exceptions
If the agent violates the principal's instructions (e.g., buys with different currency or appoints another agent), the purchase is considered for the agent himself because he contradicted the command.
Contradiction nullifies the agency for that transaction.

Source Text

ترجمہ اگر مؤکل نے وکیل کو کسی معین چیز کے خریدنے کا وکیل کیا ہوتو وکیل کیلئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ اس کو اپنی ذات کے واسطے خرید لے کیونکہ وکیل کا اپنے واسطے خریدنا موکل کا دھوکا دینے کا سبب ہے اسلئے کہ متوکل نے اس پر اعتماد کیا ہے۔ اور اسلئے کہ ایسا کرنے میں وکیل کا اپنے آپ کو معزول کرنا ہے حالانکہ وکیل بقول بعض علماء کے اس کا مالک نہیں ہے مگر مؤکل کی موجودگی میں ۔ پس اگر شمن بیان کر دیا گیا ہو پھر وکیل نے اس کے خلاف جنس کے عوض خریدا یا شمن بیان نہیں ہوا تھا لیکن وکیل نے غیر نقود کے عوض خرید ایا وکیل نے کسی دوسرے شخص کو اس کے خریدنے کا وکیل کیا پس دوسرے وکیل نے خرید لیا۔ حالانکہ وکیل اول غائب ہے تو ان صورتوں میں وکیل اول کیلئے ملک ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ وکیل نے ان صورتوں میں مؤکل کے امر کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ لہذا یہ خریداری اسی پر نافذ ہو جائے گی اور اگر دوسرے وکیل نے وکیل اول کی موجودگی میں خریدا تو خریداری مؤکل اول پر نافذ ہو گی۔ اسلئے کہ وکیل اول کی رائے موجود ہے۔ لہذا وکیل اول اپنے موکل کے حکم کے مخالف نہ ہوا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے کسی دوسرے شخص کو کسی معین چیز خریدنے کا وکیل کیا ہے تو وکیل کیلئے اس متعینہ چیز کو اپنے واسطے خرید نا جائز نہیں ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر وکیل نے اس متعینہ چیز کو اپنے واسطے خرید بھی لیا تو یہ خریداری مؤکل کیلئے ہوگی نہ کہ وکیل کیلئے خواه وکیل عقد شراء کے وقت اپنے واسطے خریدنے کی نیت کرے خواہ اپنے واسطے خریدنے کی صراحت کرے۔ مثلاً یہ کہے کہ لوگو! تم گواہ رہو میں نے یہ چیز اپنے واسطے خریدی ہے مگر یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ موکل عقد شراء کے وقت موجود نہ ہو اور اگر مؤکل عقد شراء کے وقت موجود ہو اور وکیل اپنے واسطے خریدنے کی صراحت کر دے تو اس صورت میں خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی۔ اصل مسئلہ پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ متعینہ شی ، کے خریدنے کے سلسلہ میں مؤکل نے وکیل پر اعتماد کیا ہے۔ مگر وکیل نے اس متعینہ شی ، کو اپنے واسطے خرید کر متوکل کو دھوکا دیا ہے۔ اور موکل ایک مسلمان ہے اور مسلمان کو دھوکا دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا وکیل کا اس متعینہ شی کو اپنے واسطے خریدنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب وکیل نے اس متعینہ شی ، کو اپنے واسطے خرید کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ بحکم وکالت مؤکل کے واسطے خریدنے پر مامور تھا تو گویا وہ اپنے آپ کو وکالت سے معزول کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ حالانکہ مؤکل کی عدم موجودگی میں وکیل اپنے آپ کو معزول کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہوتا جیسا کہ موکل ، وکیل کی عدم موجودگی میں اس کو معزول کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ معزول کرنا یا معزول ہونا فسخ عقد ہے اور فسخ عقد بغیر کسی دوسرے ساتھی سے علم کے درست نہیں ہوتا لہذا وکیل کا مؤکل کی عدم جودگی میں اپنے آپ کو معزول کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر مؤکل موجود ہو اور وکیل نے اس متعینہ شی کو اپنے واسطے خریدنے کی صراحت کر دی ہے تو اس صورت میں وکیل کا اپنے آپ کو معزول کرنا چونکہ مؤکل کی موجودگی میں ہے اسلئے یہ درست ہوگا اور اس متعینہ شی کی خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی نہ کہ مؤکل کیلئے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر موکل نے کسی کو متعینہ چیز خریدنے کا وکیل کیا ہو اور پھر اس نے مؤکل کی عدم موجودگی میں اس چیز کو
He said: If he appoints him agent to buy a specific thing, he may not buy it for himself, because it leads to deception of the principal since he relied on him, and because it involves dismissing himself, and he does not own it according to what is said except in the presence of the principal. So if the price was specified and he bought contrary to its type, or it was not specified and he bought with non-monetary goods, or he appointed another agent to buy it and the second bought while the first is absent, the ownership is established for the first agent in these cases because he contradicted the command, so it is valid for him. And if the second bought in the presence of the first agent, it is valid for the first principal because his opinion was present, so he was not contradictory. Translation: If the principal appointed an agent to buy a specific item, it is not permissible for the agent to buy it for himself, because the agent's buying for himself is a cause of deceiving the principal, as the principal relied upon him. And because in doing so, the agent dismisses himself, although, according to some scholars, he does not own it except in the presence of the principal. So if the price was specified and then the agent bought contrary to its type, or the price was not specified and the agent bought with non-monetary goods, or the agent appointed another person to buy it and the second bought while the first agent was absent, then in these cases ownership is established for the first agent, because he contradicted the principal's command, so the purchase is valid for him. And if the second agent bought in the presence of the first agent, the purchase is valid for the first principal, because the first agent's opinion was present, so he was not contradictory. Explanation of the issue: If a person appointed another as agent to buy a specific item, it is not permissible for the agent to buy that specified item for himself. Even if the agent bought that specified item for himself, this purchase is for the principal, not for the agent, whether the agent intended to buy for himself at the time of contract, or explicitly stated he is buying for himself. For example, he says, 'O people! Bear witness that I have bought this item for myself.' However, this ruling applies when the principal is not present at the time of contract. But if the principal is present at the time of contract and the agent explicitly says he is buying for himself, then in that case the purchase is for the agent. The proof for the original ruling is that the principal trusted the agent regarding the purchase of the specific item. But the agent deceived the principal by buying that item for himself. The principal is a Muslim, and deceiving a Muslim is not permissible. Therefore, the agent's buying that specific item for himself is not permissible. The second proof is that when the agent bought that specific item for himself, while he was commanded by the agency to buy for the principal, he effectively intends to dismiss himself from agency. However, in the absence of the principal, the agent is not authorized to dismiss himself, just as the principal is not authorized to dismiss the agent in the absence of the agent. Because dismissal or being dismissed is a rescission of the contract, and rescission is not valid without the knowledge of the other party. Therefore, the agent's dismissal of himself in the absence of the principal is not valid. Yes, if the principal is present and the agent explicitly states he is buying that specific item for himself, then in that case the agent's dismissal of himself is valid because it is in the presence of the principal, and the purchase of that specific item is for the agent, not for the principal. The author of al-Hidayah says: If the principal appointed someone as agent to buy a specific item, and then he bought that item in the absence of the principal...
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling from al-Hidayah regarding an agent appointed to buy a specific item. The passage type is a ruling with proof. The Arabic matn states: If a principal appoints an agent to buy a specific item, the agent may not buy it for himself. This is because it leads to deceiving the principal who relied on him, and because it involves dismissing himself from agency without the principal's knowledge. However, this only applies in the absence of the principal. If the principal is present and the agent explicitly states he is buying for himself, it is valid. Then the matn lists several cases where the agent's purchase is considered for himself due to contradiction of the command: (1) if the price was specified and he bought with a different currency, (2) if the price was not specified and he bought with non-monetary goods, (3) if he delegated another agent and that second agent bought while the first was absent. In all these cases, the purchase belongs to the first agent because he violated the command. But if the second agent buys in the presence of the first agent, it binds the original principal because the first agent's opinion (tacit approval) is present. The Urdu commentary expands on these points, providing reasons: the agent's self-purchase constitutes deception of a Muslim, which is impermissible, and it amounts to an invalid dismissal of oneself from agency. Finally, the author of al-Hidayah emphasizes that the ruling hinges on the principal's presence.

Key Terms
شيء بعينه (shay' bi'aynihi): A specific, identified item that the agent is appointed to purchase.
تعزير (taghreer): Deception or fraud, here referring to the agent deceiving the principal by buying for himself.
عزل نفسه (azl nafsihi): The agent's act of dismissing himself from agency without the principal's consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An agent is appointed to buy a specific car. In the principal's absence, the agent buys it for himself. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The agent owns the car
B) The principal owns the car
C) The sale is void
D) The agent must cancel

Key Takeaway
An agent appointed to buy a specific item cannot buy it for himself in the principal's absence; the purchase invalidly binds the principal.

12 min
When an Agent Buys a Specified Item for Himself: Rule and Exceptions
Ruling with rational proofs and three exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default Hanafi ruling when an agent purchases a specified item for himself and identify the three exceptional cases where ownership transfers to the agent.

Core Idea
An agent cannot buy a specified item for himself; the purchase belongs to the principal unless the agent clearly deviates from authority.

This lesson examines a key ruling from the Hanafi Book of Agency: what happens when an agent (wakīl), appointed to buy a specific item, purchases it for himself instead? The general rule is clear – the purchase is for the principal (muwakkil) – but there are important exceptions when the agent has opposed the principal's command. We will explore the legal proofs and the three specific scenarios where the agent becomes the owner.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
Read the opening part of the passage: the agent appointed to buy a specific item cannot buy it for himself. If he does, the purchase is for the principal, not the agent, even if the agent intended or declared otherwise.
This rule applies when the principal is absent at the time of purchase.
2
Understand the Rational Proofs
The passage provides two rational (ʿaqlī) proofs: (1) the agent's self-purchase deceives the principal who trusted him, and deceiving a Muslim is impermissible; (2) the agent is effectively dismissing himself from the agency, which is not allowed without the principal's knowledge in his absence.
These proofs are based on principles of trust (amāna) and contract rescission.
3
Note the Exception When Principal is Present
If the principal is present at the contract and the agent explicitly states he is buying for himself, then the purchase is for the agent. The agent's self-dismissal is valid because it happens in the principal's presence.
This shows that the principal's awareness changes the ruling.
4
Identify the Three Exceptions in the Principal's Absence
Even when the principal is absent, ownership goes to the agent in three cases: (1) the agent bought with a different species than the specified price (e.g., dirhams vs. dinars); (2) no price was specified but the agent bought with non-currency goods; (3) the first agent appointed a sub-agent (wakīl thānī) who bought the item while the first agent was absent.
In all three, the agent is deemed to have opposed the principal's command, so the contract is effective on him, not the principal.
5
Apply to the Sub-Agency Scenario
If the sub-agent buys in the presence of the first agent, the purchase goes to the original principal because the first agent's opinion was present. Absence triggers opposition.
This highlights the importance of the agent's direct oversight (ra'y).

Source Text

كتاب الوكالة ولم یکن مسمى فاشترى بغير النقود او وكل وكيلا بشرائه فاشترى الثانى وهو غائب يثبت الملك للوكيل الأول فى هذه الوجوه لانه خالف امر الأمر فنفذ عليه ولو اشترى الثانى بحضرة الوكيل الأول نفذ على المؤكل الأول لانه حضره رأيه فلم يكن مخالفا ترجمہ اگر مؤکل نے وکیل کو کسی معین چیز کے خریدنے کا وکیل کیا ہوتو وکیل کیلئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ اس کو اپنی ذات کے واسطے خرید لے کیونکہ وکیل کا اپنے واسطے خریدنا موکل کا دھوکا دینے کا سبب ہے اسلئے کہ متوکل نے اس پر اعتماد کیا ہے۔ اور اسلئے کہ ایسا کرنے میں وکیل کا اپنے آپ کو معزول کرنا ہے حالانکہ وکیل بقول بعض علماء کے اس کا مالک نہیں ہے مگر مؤکل کی موجودگی میں ۔ پس اگر شمن بیان کر دیا گیا ہو پھر وکیل نے اس کے خلاف جنس کے عوض خریدا یا شمن بیان نہیں ہوا تھا لیکن وکیل نے غیر نقود کے عوض خرید ایا وکیل نے کسی دوسرے شخص کو اس کے خریدنے کا وکیل کیا پس دوسرے وکیل نے خرید لیا۔ حالانکہ وکیل اول غائب ہے تو ان صورتوں میں وکیل اول کیلئے ملک ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ وکیل نے ان صورتوں میں مؤکل کے امر کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ لہذا یہ خریداری اسی پر نافذ ہو جائے گی اور اگر دوسرے وکیل نے وکیل اول کی موجودگی میں خریدا تو خریداری مؤکل اول پر نافذ ہو گی۔ اسلئے کہ وکیل اول کی رائے موجود ہے۔ لہذا وکیل اول اپنے موکل کے حکم کے مخالف نہ ہوا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے کسی دوسرے شخص کو کسی معین چیز خریدنے کا وکیل کیا ہے تو وکیل کیلئے اس متعینہ چیز کو اپنے واسطے خرید نا جائز نہیں ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر وکیل نے اس متعینہ چیز کو اپنے واسطے خرید بھی لیا تو یہ خریداری مؤکل کیلئے ہوگی نہ کہ وکیل کیلئے خواه وکیل عقد شراء کے وقت اپنے واسطے خریدنے کی نیت کرے خواہ اپنے واسطے خریدنے کی صراحت کرے۔ مثلاً یہ کہے کہ لوگو! تم گواہ رہو میں نے یہ چیز اپنے واسطے خریدی ہے مگر یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ موکل عقد شراء کے وقت موجود نہ ہو اور اگر مؤکل عقد شراء کے وقت موجود ہو اور وکیل اپنے واسطے خریدنے کی صراحت کر دے تو اس صورت میں خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی۔ اصل مسئلہ پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ متعینہ شی ، کے خریدنے کے سلسلہ میں مؤکل نے وکیل پر اعتماد کیا ہے۔ مگر وکیل نے اس متعینہ شی ، کو اپنے واسطے خرید کر متوکل کو دھوکا دیا ہے۔ اور موکل ایک مسلمان ہے اور مسلمان کو دھوکا دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا وکیل کا اس متعینہ شی کو اپنے واسطے خریدنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب وکیل نے اس متعینہ شی ، کو اپنے واسطے خرید کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ بحکم وکالت مؤکل کے واسطے خریدنے پر مامور تھا تو گویا وہ اپنے آپ کو وکالت سے معزول کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ حالانکہ مؤکل کی عدم موجودگی میں وکیل اپنے آپ کو معزول کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہوتا جیسا کہ موکل ، وکیل کی عدم موجودگی میں اس کو معزول کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ معزول کرنا یا معزول ہونا فسخ عقد ہے اور فسخ عقد بغیر کسی دوسرے ساتھی سے علم کے درست نہیں ہوتا لہذا وکیل کا مؤکل کی عدم جودگی میں اپنے آپ کو معزول کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر مؤکل موجود ہو اور وکیل نے اس متعینہ شی کو اپنے واسطے خریدنے کی صراحت کر دی ہے تو اس صورت میں وکیل کا اپنے آپ کو معزول کرنا چونکہ مؤکل کی موجودگی میں ہے اسلئے یہ درست ہوگا اور اس متعینہ شی کی خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی نہ کہ مؤکل کیلئے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر موکل نے کسی کو متعینہ چیز خریدنے کا وکیل کیا ہو اور پھر اس نے مؤکل کی عدم موجودگی میں اس چیز کو اپنے واسطے خرید لیا ہو تو سابق میں گذر چکا کہ یہ خریداری مؤکل کیلئے ہوگی اور مؤکل ہی اس متعینہ شی کا مالک ہوگا۔ وکیل مالک نہ ہوگا۔ مگر تین صورتیں اس سے مستثنیٰ ہیں۔ یعنی تین صورتیں ایسی ہیں جن میں خریداری وکیل کیلئے واقع ہو گی۔ اور وکیل ہی اس شی کا مالک ہوگا۔ - اگر مؤکل نے شمن مسمی کے عوض خریدنے کا وکیل کیا ہے کمل نے اس شمن مسمی کی جنس کے خلاف کے عوض خرید کیا۔ مثلا مؤکل نے در اہم کا ذکر کیا اور وکیل نے دنا میز کے عوض خریدا تو اس صورت میں یہ خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں وکیل نے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ جیسا کہ ظاہر ہے اور موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کرنے سے عقد وکیل پر نافذ ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل پر لند یہ عقد شراء وکیل پر نافذ ہوگا ۔ اور وکیل ہی اس متعینہ شی ء کا مالک ہوگا۔ - یہ کہ مؤکل نے شمن بیان نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ وکیل سے یہ کہہ دیا کہ فلاں متعینہ چیز خرید کر لاؤ مگر وکیل نے نقود یعنی در اہم، دنانیر کے علاوہ دوسری کسی ملیلی یا موزونی چیز کے عوض خریداری کی تو اس صورت میں بھی یہ خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی اور وکیل ہی خریدی ہوئی چیز کا مالک ہوگا۔ موکل مالک نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی وکیل نے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ متوکل کے شمن بیان نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے ثمن متعارف کی طرف لوٹے گا اور متعارف نقد بلد ہے یعنی شہر کا مروجہ سکہ متعارف ہے۔ لہذا موکل امراسی نقد بلد کی طرف راجع ہوگا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہوگا گویا موکل نے یوں کہا کہ فلاں متعینہ چیز نقد بلد کے عوض خرید کر لاؤ مگر وکیل ۔ غیر نقود کے عوض خریدا تو وکیل مونک کمی کی میں نے ان خیالات کی صورت میں عقد شرا، وکیل کیلئے ہوتا ہے اور خرید کی ہوئی چیز کا مالک وکیل ہی ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل۔ الہند اند کورہ صورت میں بھی خریدی ہوئی چیز وکیل کیلئے ہوگی۔ -۳- یہ ہے کہ مؤکل نے ایک شخص کو ایک متعینہ چیز خریدنے کا وکیل کیا۔ پھر اس وکیل نے دوسرے شخص کو وکیل کیا۔ پھر وکیل ثانی ۔ وکیل اول کی عدم موجودگی میں اس متعینہ شی کوخریدا تو اس صورت میں بھی یہ خریداری وکیل اول کیلئے ہوگی ۔ اور وہی اس شئی کا مالکہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی وکیل اول نے اپنے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ جب مؤکل نے اس کو وکیل بنایا تو تو گویا یہ حکم دیا تھا کہ اس متعینہ شی کوخرید کرنے کے وقت تیری رائے موجود رہنی چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ اس صورت میں وکیل اول کی عد موجودگی کی وجہ سے وکیل اول کی رائے نہیں پائی گئی۔ اور جب وکیل اول کی رائے نہیں پائی گئی تو وکیل اول کی طرف سے مؤکل ۔ حکم کی مخالفت پائی گئی اور وکیل کے اپنے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کرنے سے چونکہ عقد وکیل پر نافذ ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل پر ۔ اسلئے اس صورت میں خریداری وکیل اول کیلئے ہوگی نہ کہ اس کے متوکل کیلئے اور اگر وکیل ثانی نے وکیل ارل کی موجودگی میں خریداری کی تو خریداری مؤکل اول پر نافذ ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں خریداری کرتے وقت وکیل اول کی رائے متحقق ہو گئی ہے اور جس وکیل اول کی رائے متحقق ہوگئی تو وکیل اول اپنے مؤکل کی مخالفت کرنے والا نہ ہوا۔ اور جب وکیل اول اپنے موکل کی مخالف کرنے والا نہیں ہوا تو یہ خریداری اس کے مؤکل پر ہی نافذ ہوگی نہ کہ وکیل اول پر۔
Book of Agency. If (the price) was not specified and he bought with other than currency, or he appointed an agent to purchase it and the second purchased while he (the first) was absent, ownership is established for the first agent in these cases because he opposed the command, so it is effective upon him. And if the second purchased in the presence of the first agent, it is effective upon the first principal because his (the first agent's) opinion was present, so he was not opposed. Translation: If the principal appointed an agent to purchase a specific item, it is not permissible for the agent to buy it for himself because the agent's buying for himself is a cause for deceiving the principal, since the principal trusted him. And because in doing so the agent is dismissing himself, although the agent, according to some scholars, is not the owner of it except in the presence of the principal. So if the price was specified and the agent bought with a different species, or the price was not specified but the agent bought with non-currency, or the agent appointed another person to purchase it and the second bought while the first agent was absent — in these cases ownership is established for the first agent because he opposed the principal's command. Therefore this purchase is effective upon him. If the second agent bought in the presence of the first agent, then the purchase is effective upon the first principal because the first agent's opinion was present, so he was not opposed to the principal's command. Explanation: The issue is that if a person appoints another as agent to purchase a specific item, it is not permissible for the agent to buy that specific item for himself. Even if he buys it for himself, the purchase is for the principal, not for the agent, whether the agent intended to buy for himself or explicitly stated it. For example, he says, 'O people, bear witness that I have bought this item for myself.' But this ruling applies when the principal is not present at the time of the contract. If the principal is present and the agent explicitly states that he is buying for himself, then the purchase is for the agent. The proof for the original ruling is that the principal trusted the agent regarding the purchase of the specific item, but the agent deceived the principal by buying it for himself. A Muslim is not to be deceived, so it is not permissible. Another proof is that when the agent bought the specific item for himself, while he was commanded to buy it for the principal by virtue of agency, it is as if he wants to dismiss himself from the agency. But in the absence of the principal, the agent is not authorized to dismiss himself, just as the principal is not authorized to dismiss the agent in the agent's absence. Dismissal is a rescission of contract, and rescission is not valid without the knowledge of the other party. Therefore, the agent's dismissal of himself in the principal's absence is not valid. Yes, if the principal is present and the agent explicitly states that he is buying for himself, then the agent's dismissal of himself is in the presence of the principal, so it is valid, and the purchase of the specific item is for the agent, not the principal. The author of Al-Hidayah says: If the principal appoints someone as agent to buy a specific item, and then the agent buys it for himself in the principal's absence, as previously mentioned, the purchase is for the principal, and the principal is the owner of that specific item. The agent is not the owner. However, three cases are excepted from this. That is, three cases in which the purchase is valid for the agent, and the agent is the owner of that item. (1) If the principal appointed him to buy with a specified price, and the agent bought with a different species of that price. For example, the principal mentioned dirhams and the agent bought with dinars. In this case, the purchase is for the agent because the agent opposed the principal's command. When the principal's command is opposed, the contract is effective upon the agent, not the principal. So the purchase contract is effective upon the agent, and he is the owner of that specific item. (2) That the principal did not specify the price but just said, 'Bring this specific item,' and the agent bought it with something other than currency (dirhams and dinars), like a weighed or measured item. In this case as well, the purchase is for the agent, and he is the owner, not the principal. Because in this case also the agent opposed the principal's command. Since the principal did not specify the price, one refers to the customary price, and the customary price is the currency of the city. So the principal's command is implicitly to buy with the city's currency. So it is as if the principal said, 'Buy this specific item with the city's currency,' but the agent bought with non-currency, so he opposed. Therefore, in this case too, the purchase is for the agent. (3) That the principal appointed a person as agent to buy a specific item, then that agent appointed another person as agent, and the second agent bought that specific item in the absence of the first agent. In this case, the purchase is for the first agent, and he is the owner. Because here too, the first agent opposed his principal's command. When the principal appointed him, it was as if he commanded that his (the first agent's) opinion should be present at the time of purchase. But in this case, due to the first agent's absence, his opinion was not present. Since his opinion was not present, there was opposition to the principal's command from the first agent. And when the agent opposes his principal's command, the contract is effective upon the agent, not the principal. So in this case the purchase is for the first agent, not for his principal. If the second agent bought in the presence of the first agent, then the purchase is effective upon the first principal, because the first agent's opinion was realized, so he was not in opposition. And since he was not in opposition, the purchase is effective upon his principal, not upon the first agent.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the Book of Agency. It begins by stating the general rule: an agent appointed to buy a specific item cannot buy it for himself. If he does, the purchase is attributed to the principal (muwakkil), not the agent. The commentary provides two rational proofs: first, the principal relied on the agent, and buying for himself is a deception, which is impermissible in Islam; second, by doing so the agent is effectively dismissing himself from the agency, which is not valid without the principal's knowledge in his absence. The text then clarifies an exception: if the principal is present at the contract and the agent explicitly declares he is buying for himself, then the purchase is for the agent. The main ruling has three exceptions where the purchase goes to the agent even in the principal's absence: (1) when the principal specified a price (thaman musamma) and the agent bought with a different species (e.g., dirhams vs. dinars); (2) when the principal did not specify the price, so the customary local currency is implied, but the agent bought with non-currency goods; (3) when the first agent appointed a sub-agent, and the sub-agent bought the item while the first agent was absent. In all three, the agent is deemed to have opposed the principal's command, so the purchase is effective upon the agent. If the sub-agent buys in the first agent's presence, the purchase goes to the original principal because the first agent had the opportunity to oversee. The commentary follows the order of the matn, first explaining the rule, then the proofs, then the exceptions, and ends with the sub-agency case. No inter-madhhab disputes are mentioned; the positions are consistent Hanafi.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakīl): The agent appointed by the principal (muwakkil) to perform a specific legal act, here purchasing a specified item.
موکل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent (wakīl) to act on his behalf.
شمن مسمی (thaman musammā): A specific price mentioned and agreed upon for the purchase.
نقود (nuqūd): Currency, specifically dirhams and dinars (silver and gold coins) that serve as customary money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if an agent appointed to buy a specific item buys it for himself in the principal's absence without any deviation, who owns the item?
A) The agent, because he made the purchase.
B) The principal, because the agent was acting on his behalf.
C) The agent, if he explicitly stated he was buying for himself.
D) The principal, unless one of three exceptions applies.

Key Takeaway
An agent's self-purchase of a specified item belongs to the principal unless the agent opposes the command by using a different price species, non-currency payment, or sub-agency in his absence—in those cases, ownership transfers to the agent.

Ruling on Agent's Purchase of an Unspecified Slave
States the default ownership rule in unspecified agency purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ownership when an agent buys an unspecified slave and identify the two exceptions that transfer ownership to the principal.

Core Idea
Default: agent owns the slave; only explicit intention or using principal's money transfers ownership.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a key issue in the contract of agency (wakalah): when a principal authorizes an agent to buy a slave without specifying which one, and the agent performs the purchase, who owns the slave? The ruling establishes a default presumption of agent ownership, with two clear exceptions. Understanding this default is essential for determining the rights and obligations of both parties in agency transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The principal says 'buy a slave' but does not specify which slave, granting general authority to purchase any slave.
This is a general agency, not specific to a particular slave.
2
State the default ruling
By default, the purchased slave belongs to the agent (wakeel), not the principal (muwakkil).
The agent's ownership is established because the principal did not limit the choice.
3
List the two exceptions
(1) If the agent explicitly states that he intended the purchase for the principal. (2) If the agent uses the principal's money to buy the slave.
These exceptions indicate the agent's intention to buy on behalf of the principal.
4
Understand the commentary on disagreement
The commentator notes that there is detail and some disagreement among scholars, but the default rule is established by consensus.
The default is strong and relied upon for fatwa.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
If the agent buys with his own money and says nothing, the slave is his. The principal cannot claim it without proof of the exceptions.
This shows practical application of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا وكله بشراء عبد بغير عينه فاشترى عبدا فهو للوكيل الا ان يقول نويت الشراء للمؤكل او يشتري بمال المؤكل قال رضى الله عنه هذه المسألة على وجوه ان اضاف العقد الى دراهم الأمر كان للآمر وهـ المراد عندى بقوله او يشتريه بمال المؤكل دون النقد من ماله لان فيه تفصيلا وخلافا وهذا بالاجماع وه ترجمہ مؤکل نے غیر معین غلام خرید نے پر وکیل بنایا وکیل نے ایک غلام خرید اوہ وکیل کا ہوگا ، مؤکل کا کب ہوگا
And if he (the principal) appoints him as agent to buy a slave without specification (of a particular slave), and he buys a slave, then it is for the agent unless he says 'I intended the purchase for the principal' or he buys with the principal's money. He (the commentator) said, may Allah be pleased with him: This issue has aspects: if he attributes the contract to the dirhams of the commander (principal), it is for the commander. And this is what is meant by his statement 'or he buys with the principal's money' without the currency from his own money, because there is detail and disagreement in it, and this is by consensus... Translation: The principal appointed an agent to buy an unspecified slave. The agent bought a slave. It will belong to the agent. When will it be the principal's?
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents a new ruling: when an agent is appointed to buy a slave without specifying which slave (i.e., a general authorization to purchase a slave), and the agent buys a slave, the default ruling is that the slave belongs to the agent (wakeel), not the principal. However, there are two exceptions: (1) if the agent explicitly states that he intended the purchase for the principal (nawaytu al-shira'a lil-muwakkil), or (2) if he buys using the principal's property (mal al-muwakkil). The commentary by the author (likely 'Ala' al-Din al-Haskafi or the commentator of Ashraf al-Hidayah) explains that this issue has multiple aspects. If the agent attributes the contract to the principal's dirhams, the purchase is for the principal. The phrase 'or he buys with the principal's money' means using the principal's actual funds, not just the currency from his own money. This distinction is made because there is detail and some disagreement, but the ruling as stated is by consensus (bil-ijma'). The Urdu translation that follows is incomplete but conveys the same: the agent appointed to buy an unspecified slave; when he buys a slave, it is for the agent; when will it be for the principal? The commentary is cut off, but the central ruling is clear. This is a ruling statement with no explicit dalil provided in the available text, though the comment about consensus indicates it is a well-established position.

Key Terms
عبد بغير عينه (abd bi-ghayri 'aynihi): An unspecified slave; the agent is authorized to buy any slave, not a particular one.
بمال المؤكل (bi-māli al-muwakkil): Using the principal's property (money) to make the purchase, as opposed to the agent's own money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when an agent is appointed to buy an unspecified slave and buys with his own money without stating intention, who owns the slave?
A) The principal
B) The agent
C) Both jointly
D) The seller

Key Takeaway
In an unspecified agency purchase of a slave, the default ownership is with the agent; only explicit intention or use of the principal's funds transfers ownership.

Exception 1: Agent Buys with Different Currency than Specified
First exception in agency: agent uses different currency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an agent buys with a different currency than the principal specified, and identify that the purchase belongs to the agent.

Core Idea
If the agent uses a different currency than specified, the purchase is for the agent, not the principal.

In agency, the agent must follow the principal's instructions. One key instruction is the price. This lesson covers the first exception: when the principal specifies a currency (e.g., dirhams) and the agent uses a different currency (e.g., dinars). The purchase then belongs to the agent, because deviation invalidates the agency for that transaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal's instruction
Determine what the principal specified as the price and its currency. The principal must have explicitly named a specific currency (e.g., dirhams).
If the principal did not specify a price, this exception may not apply; see Exception 2.
2
Compare the agent's action
Check what the agent actually paid. If the agent used a different currency (e.g., dinars instead of dirhams), that is a deviation from the principal's command.
The deviation must be in the genus of the price, not just a different amount of the same currency.
3
Determine the ruling
Since the agent opposed the principal's command, the contract takes effect on the agent. The agent becomes the owner of the purchased item, and the principal is not bound.
This ruling applies regardless of whether the agent made a profit or loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة
مگر تين صورتيں اس سے مستثنیٰ ہيں۔ يعنی تين صورتيں ايسی ہيں جن ميں خريداری وکيل کيلئے واقع ہو گی۔ اور وکيل ہی اس شی کا مالک ہوگا۔ - اگر مؤکل نے شمن مسمی کے عوض خر ينے کا وکيل کيا ہے کمل نے اس شمن مسمی کی جنس کے خلاف کے عوض خرید کيا۔ مثلاً مؤکل نے در اہم کا ذکر کيا اور وکيل نے دنا میز کے عوض خریدا تو اس صورت ميں يہ خريداری وکيل کيلئے ہوگی۔ کيونکہ اس صورت ميں وکيل نے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ جيسا کہ ظاہر ہے اور موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کرنے سے عقد وکيل پر نافذ ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل پر لند يہ عقد شراء وکيل پر نافذ ہوگا۔ اور وکيل ہی اس متعينہ شیء کا مالک ہوگا۔ - يہ کہ مؤکل نے شمن بيان نہيں کيا ہے بلکہ وکيل سے يہ کہہ ديا کہ فلاں متعينہ چيز خرید کر لاؤ مگر وکيل نے نقود يعنی در اہم، دنانير کے علاوہ دوسری کسی [مليلی؟] يا [موزونی؟] چيز کے عوض خريداری کی تو اس صورت ميں بھی يہ خريداری وکيل کيلئے ہوگی اور وکيل ہی خريد ہوئی چيز کا مالک ہوگا۔ موکل مالک نہ ہوگا۔ کيونکہ اس صورت ميں بھی وکيل نے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ متوکل کے شمن بيان نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے ثمن متعارف کی طرف لوٹے گا اور متعارف نقد بلد ہے يعنی شہر کا مروجہ سکہ متعارف ہے۔ لہذا موکل امراسی نقد بلد کی طرف راجع ہوگا۔ اور يہ ايسا ہوگا گويا موکل نے يوں کہا کہ فلاں متعينہ چيز نقد بلد کے عوض خرید کر لاؤ مگر وکيل غير نقود کے عوض خریدا تو وکيل [؟] کی اس صورت ميں عقد شراء وکيل کيلئے ہوتا ہے اور خرید کی ہوئی چيز کا مالک وکيل ہی ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل۔ -۳- يہ ہے کہ مؤکل نے ايک شخص کو ايک متعينہ چيز خر ينے کا وکيل کيا۔ پھر اس وکيل نے دوسرے شخص کو وکيل کيا۔ پھر وکيل ثانی وکيل اول کی عدم موجودگی ميں اس متعينہ شی کو خریدا تو اس صورت ميں بھی يہ خريداری وکيل اول کيلئے ہوگی۔ اور وہی اس شی کا مالک ہوگا کيونکہ اس صورت ميں بھی وکيل اول نے اپنے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ جب مؤکل نے اس کو وکيل بنايا تو گويا يہ حکم ديا تھا کہ اس متعينہ شی کو خرید نے کے وقت تيری رائے موجود رہنی چاہئے۔ حالانکہ اس صورت ميں وکيل اول کی عدم موجودگی کی وجہ سے وکيل اول کی رائے نہيں پائی گئی۔ اور جب وکيل اول کی رائے نہيں پائی گئی تو وکيل اول کی طرف سے مؤکل کے حکم کی مخالفت پائی گئی اور وکيل کے اپنے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کرنے سے چونکہ عقد وکيل پر نافذ ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل پر۔ اسلئے اس صورت ميں خريداری وکيل اول کيلئے ہوگی نہ کہ اس کے موکل کيلئے۔ اور اگر وکيل ثانی نے وکيل اول کی موجودگی ميں خريداری کی تو خريداری مؤکل اول پر نافذ ہو جائے گی۔ کيونکہ اس صورت ميں خريداری کرتے وقت وکيل اول کی رائے متحقق ہو گئی ہے اور جس وکيل اول کی رائے متحقق ہوگئی تو وکيل اول اپنے مؤکل کی مخالفت کرنے والا نہ ہوا۔ اور جب وکيل اول اپنے موکل کی مخالفت کرنے والا نہيں ہوا تو يہ خريداری اس کے مؤکل پر ہی نافذ ہوگی نہ کہ وکيل اول پر۔
Book of Agency: There are three exceptions to this, i.e. three cases in which the purchase is effected for the agent, and the agent will be the owner of that thing. (1) If the principal appointed him as agent to buy for a specified price, and the agent bought for a price contrary to the genus of that specified price – for example, the principal mentioned dirhams and the agent bought for dinars – then in this case the purchase is for the agent, because the agent has opposed the command of the principal, as is apparent. And by opposing the principal's command, the contract takes effect on the agent, not the principal; thus the contract of purchase will take effect on the agent and the agent will be the owner of that specified thing. (2) That the principal did not state the price, but told the agent, 'Go buy that specified thing', but the agent bought it in exchange for something other than currency, i.e. dirhams or dinars, i.e. some other measurable or weighable item. In this case too, the purchase is for the agent and the agent is the owner of the purchased item, the principal is not the owner. Because in this case also, the agent opposed the command of the principal. The reason is that when the principal did not state the price, the price defaults to the customary price, and the customary price is the currency of the land, i.e. the prevailing coin of the city. Therefore, the principal's order refers to the local currency. It is as if the principal said, 'Buy that specific thing for the local currency', but the agent bought for something other than currency. So in this case, the contract of purchase is for the agent and the owner of the purchased item is the agent, not the principal. (3) That the principal appointed someone as agent to buy a specific thing; then that agent appointed another person as agent; then the second agent bought that specific thing in the absence of the first agent. In this case too, the purchase is for the first agent, and he will be the owner of that thing. Because in this case too, the first agent opposed the command of his principal. The reasoning is that when the principal appointed him as agent, it was as if he commanded that at the time of buying that specific thing, your personal judgment must be present. But in this case, due to the absence of the first agent, his judgment was not present. And since his judgment was not present, opposition to the principal's command occurred on the part of the first agent. And when the agent opposes his principal's command, the contract takes effect on the agent, not the principal. Therefore, in this case, the purchase is for the first agent, not for his principal. But if the second agent bought in the presence of the first agent, then the purchase takes effect on the original principal, because at the time of purchase, the first agent's judgment was realized, so the first agent did not become an opponent of his principal. And when the first agent did not oppose his principal, this purchase takes effect on his principal, not on the first agent.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah lists three specific exceptions to the general rule that an agent's purchase goes to the principal. The general rule is that when an agent acts within his authority, the contract binds the principal. However, when the agent deviates from the principal's instructions in these three ways, the purchase is considered the agent's own. The first exception is when the principal specifies a price (e.g. in dirhams) and the agent buys using a different currency (e.g. dinars). The second exception is when the principal does not mention a price, so the default is the local currency, but the agent buys with a non-currency item (like grain). The third exception is when the principal appoints an agent to buy a specific item, that agent sub-delegates, and the sub-agent buys without the first agent's presence. In all three cases, the agent's deviation from the principal's implied or explicit instructions invalidates the agency for that transaction, making the agent personally liable and owner of the purchased item.

Key Terms
شمن مسمى (thaman musamma): The specified price explicitly stated by the principal, often including the type of currency.
نقد بلد (naqd al-balad): The local currency or coinage commonly used in the city – not directly applicable here but relevant for Exception 2.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a principal tells an agent to buy a commodity for 100 dirhams, and the agent buys it for 100 dinars?
A) The purchase is for the principal, because the amount is the same
B) The purchase is for the agent, because the agent changed the currency type
C) The purchase is void because the price is different
D) The agent must pay the difference to the principal

Key Takeaway
An agent who buys with a different currency than specified by the principal becomes the owner of the purchased item.

Exception 2: Agent Buys with Non-Currency When Principal Did Not Specify Price
Second exception: agent uses non-currency when no price specified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the second exception: when the principal does not specify a price, the agent must use the local currency; otherwise, the purchase is for the agent.

Core Idea
If the principal does not state a price, the default is the local currency; buying with a non-currency item makes the agent the owner.

Sometimes a principal tells an agent to buy a specific item without mentioning the price. In such cases, the implied price is the local currency (naqd al-balad). If the agent instead pays with a measurable or weighable commodity (like grain or cloth), he has deviated, and the purchase belongs to him. This lesson explains that second exception.

Guided Path
1
Check if the principal stated a price
If the principal did not mention any price for the purchase, the default price according to custom is the local currency.
The local currency (naqd al-balad) is the prevailing coinage in the city.
2
Identify what the agent paid
Determine whether the agent paid with currency (dirhams/dinars) or with a non-currency item (e.g., grain, cloth, animals).
Non-currency items include measurable (mikyal) or weighable (mawzun) goods.
3
Determine the ruling
If the agent used a non-currency item, he deviated from the principal's implied command, so the purchase is for the agent.
If the agent used the local currency, the purchase is for the principal.

Source Text

(1) If the principal appointed him as agent to buy for a specified price, and the agent bought for a price contrary to the genus of that specified price – for example, the principal mentioned dirhams and the agent bought for dinars – then in this case the purchase is for the agent, because the agent has opposed the command of the principal, as is apparent. (2) That the principal did not state the price, but told the agent, 'Go buy that specified thing', but the agent bought it in exchange for something other than currency, i.e. dirhams or dinars, i.e. some other measurable or weighable item. So in this case, the contract of purchase is for the agent and the owner of the purchased item is the agent, not the principal. The reasoning is that when the principal appointed him as agent, it was as if he commanded that at the time of buying that specific thing, your personal judgment must be present. But in this case, due to the absence of the first agent, his judgment was not present. And since his judgment was not present, opposition to the principal's command occurred on the part of the first agent. Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah lists three specific exceptions to the general rule that an agent's purchase goes to the principal. The general rule is that when an agent acts within his authority, the contract binds the principal. However, when the agent deviates from the principal's instructions in these three ways, the purchase is considered the agent's own. The first exception is when the principal specifies a price (e.g. in dirhams) and the agent buys using a different currency (e.g. dinars). The second exception is when the principal does not mention a price, so the default is the local currency, but the agent buys with a non-currency item (like grain). In all three cases, the agent's deviation from the principal's implied or explicit instructions invalidates the agency for that transaction, making the agent personally liable and owner of the purchased item.

Key Terms
نقد بلد (naqd al-balad): The local currency or coinage commonly used in the city; the default price when no price is specified.
متعارف (muta'arif): Customary; here, the customary price defaults to the local currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A principal tells his agent to buy a cow without specifying the price. The agent buys the cow by trading his bicycle. Who owns the cow?
A) The principal, because he asked for it
B) The agent, because he used a non-currency item instead of the local currency
C) The cow remains with the seller because payment was improper
D) Both share ownership

Key Takeaway
When no price is specified, the agent must use the local currency; using a non-currency item makes the agent the owner of the purchase.

Exception 3: Agent Sub-Delegates and Sub-Agent Buys in First Agent's Absence
Third exception: sub-agency and absence of first agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the third exception: when an agent sub-delegates and the sub-agent buys the item in the first agent's absence, the purchase belongs to the first agent, not the principal.

Core Idea
If a sub-agent buys the specific item without the first agent present, the purchase is for the first agent, due to lack of his judgment.

An agent may sometimes delegate the purchase to another person (sub-agent). This lesson covers the third exception: when the principal appoints an agent to buy a specific item, that agent appoints a sub-agent, and the sub-agent buys the item while the first agent is absent. In that case, the purchase is for the first agent, because the principal's command required the first agent's personal judgment at the time of purchase.

Guided Path
1
Identify the chain of delegation
Principal appoints Agent A to buy a specific thing. Agent A then appoints Agent B (sub-agent) to do the purchase.
Sub-delegation is permitted in Hanafi law, but the first agent remains responsible.
2
Check the first agent's presence at the time of purchase
Determine whether Agent A was present when Agent B made the purchase.
If present, the first agent's judgment is considered exercised.
3
Determine the ruling
If Agent A was absent, the purchase is for Agent A (the first agent), because the principal's command implied that Agent A's judgment should be involved. If Agent A was present, the purchase is for the original principal.
Presence means the first agent could have exercised his discretion; absence means he did not, so his action is voided.

Source Text

كتاب الوكالة
مگر تين صورتيں اس سے مستثنیٰ ہيں۔ يعنی تين صورتيں ايسی ہيں جن ميں خريداری وکيل کيلئے واقع ہو گی۔ اور وکيل ہی اس شی کا مالک ہوگا۔ - اگر مؤکل نے شمن مسمی کے عوض خر ينے کا وکيل کيا ہے کمل نے اس شمن مسمی کی جنس کے خلاف کے عوض خرید کيا۔ مثلاً مؤکل نے در اہم کا ذکر کيا اور وکيل نے دنا میز کے عوض خریدا تو اس صورت ميں يہ خريداری وکيل کيلئے ہوگی۔ کيونکہ اس صورت ميں وکيل نے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ جيسا کہ ظاہر ہے اور موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کرنے سے عقد وکيل پر نافذ ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل پر لند يہ عقد شراء وکيل پر نافذ ہوگا۔ اور وکيل ہی اس متعينہ شیء کا مالک ہوگا۔ - يہ کہ مؤکل نے شمن بيان نہيں کيا ہے بلکہ وکيل سے يہ کہہ ديا کہ فلاں متعينہ چيز خرید کر لاؤ مگر وکيل نے نقود يعنی در اہم، دنانير کے علاوہ دوسری کسی [مليلی؟] يا [موزونی؟] چيز کے عوض خريداری کی تو اس صورت ميں بھی يہ خريداری وکيل کيلئے ہوگی اور وکيل ہی خريد ہوئی چيز کا مالک ہوگا۔ موکل مالک نہ ہوگا۔ کيونکہ اس صورت ميں بھی وکيل نے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ متوکل کے شمن بيان نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے ثمن متعارف کی طرف لوٹے گا اور متعارف نقد بلد ہے يعنی شہر کا مروجہ سکہ متعارف ہے۔ لہذا موکل امراسی نقد بلد کی طرف راجع ہوگا۔ اور يہ ايسا ہوگا گويا موکل نے يوں کہا کہ فلاں متعينہ چيز نقد بلد کے عوض خرید کر لاؤ مگر وکيل غير نقود کے عوض خریدا تو وکيل [؟] کی اس صورت ميں عقد شراء وکيل کيلئے ہوتا ہے اور خرید کی ہوئی چيز کا مالک وکيل ہی ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل۔ -۳- يہ ہے کہ مؤکل نے ايک شخص کو ايک متعينہ چيز خر ينے کا وکيل کيا۔ پھر اس وکيل نے دوسرے شخص کو وکيل کيا۔ پھر وکيل ثانی وکيل اول کی عدم موجودگی ميں اس متعينہ شی کو خریدا تو اس صورت ميں بھی يہ خريداری وکيل اول کيلئے ہوگی۔ اور وہی اس شی کا مالک ہوگا کيونکہ اس صورت ميں بھی وکيل اول نے اپنے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ جب مؤکل نے اس کو وکيل بنايا تو گويا يہ حکم ديا تھا کہ اس متعينہ شی کو خرید نے کے وقت تيری رائے موجود رہنی چاہئے۔ حالانکہ اس صورت ميں وکيل اول کی عدم موجودگی کی وجہ سے وکيل اول کی رائے نہيں پائی گئی۔ اور جب وکيل اول کی رائے نہيں پائی گئی تو وکيل اول کی طرف سے مؤکل کے حکم کی مخالفت پائی گئی اور وکيل کے اپنے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کرنے سے چونکہ عقد وکيل پر نافذ ہوتا ہے نہ کہ موکل پر۔ اسلئے اس صورت ميں خريداری وکيل اول کيلئے ہوگی نہ کہ اس کے موکل کيلئے۔ اور اگر وکيل ثانی نے وکيل اول کی موجودگی ميں خريداری کی تو خريداری مؤکل اول پر نافذ ہو جائے گی۔ کيونکہ اس صورت ميں خريداری کرتے وقت وکيل اول کی رائے متحقق ہو گئی ہے اور جس وکيل اول کی رائے متحقق ہوگئی تو وکيل اول اپنے مؤکل کی مخالفت کرنے والا نہ ہوا۔ اور جب وکيل اول اپنے موکل کی مخالفت کرنے والا نہيں ہوا تو يہ خريداری اس کے مؤکل پر ہی نافذ ہوگی نہ کہ وکيل اول پر۔
Book of Agency: There are three exceptions to this, i.e. three cases in which the purchase is effected for the agent, and the agent will be the owner of that thing. (1) If the principal appointed him as agent to buy for a specified price, and the agent bought for a price contrary to the genus of that specified price – for example, the principal mentioned dirhams and the agent bought for dinars – then in this case the purchase is for the agent, because the agent has opposed the command of the principal, as is apparent. And by opposing the principal's command, the contract takes effect on the agent, not the principal; thus the contract of purchase will take effect on the agent and the agent will be the owner of that specified thing. (2) That the principal did not state the price, but told the agent, 'Go buy that specified thing', but the agent bought it in exchange for something other than currency, i.e. dirhams or dinars, i.e. some other measurable or weighable item. In this case too, the purchase is for the agent and the agent is the owner of the purchased item, the principal is not the owner. Because in this case also, the agent opposed the command of the principal. The reason is that when the principal did not state the price, the price defaults to the customary price, and the customary price is the currency of the land, i.e. the prevailing coin of the city. Therefore, the principal's order refers to the local currency. It is as if the principal said, 'Buy that specific thing for the local currency', but the agent bought for something other than currency. So in this case, the contract of purchase is for the agent and the owner of the purchased item is the agent, not the principal. (3) That the principal appointed someone as agent to buy a specific thing; then that agent appointed another person as agent; then the second agent bought that specific thing in the absence of the first agent. In this case too, the purchase is for the first agent, and he will be the owner of that thing. Because in this case too, the first agent opposed the command of his principal. The reasoning is that when the principal appointed him as agent, it was as if he commanded that at the time of buying that specific thing, your personal judgment must be present. But in this case, due to the absence of the first agent, his judgment was not present. And since his judgment was not present, opposition to the principal's command occurred on the part of the first agent. And when the agent opposes his principal's command, the contract takes effect on the agent, not the principal. Therefore, in this case, the purchase is for the first agent, not for his principal. But if the second agent bought in the presence of the first agent, then the purchase takes effect on the original principal, because at the time of purchase, the first agent's judgment was realized, so the first agent did not become an opponent of his principal. And when the first agent did not oppose his principal, this purchase takes effect on his principal, not on the first agent.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah lists three specific exceptions to the general rule that an agent's purchase goes to the principal. The general rule is that when an agent acts within his authority, the contract binds the principal. However, when the agent deviates from the principal's instructions in these three ways, the purchase is considered the agent's own. The first exception is when the principal specifies a price (e.g. in dirhams) and the agent buys using a different currency (e.g. dinars). The second exception is when the principal does not mention a price, so the default is the local currency, but the agent buys with a non-currency item (like grain). The third exception is when the principal appoints an agent to buy a specific item, that agent sub-delegates, and the sub-agent buys without the first agent's presence. In all three cases, the agent's deviation from the principal's implied or explicit instructions invalidates the agency for that transaction, making the agent personally liable and owner of the purchased item.

Key Terms
وکيل اول (wakil awwal): The first agent appointed by the principal, who then sub-delegates.
وکيل ثانی (wakil thani): The second agent (sub-agent) appointed by the first agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a principal appoints an agent to buy a specific item, the agent appoints a sub-agent, and the sub-agent buys the item while the first agent is abroad?
A) The purchase is for the principal, because the sub-agent acted on his behalf
B) The purchase is for the first agent, because his judgment was not present
C) The purchase is for the sub-agent, because he executed the contract
D) The purchase is void because of unauthorized sub-delegation

Key Takeaway
When a sub-agent buys the item without the first agent being present, the first agent becomes the owner, not the principal.

Agent Buying Unspecified Slave: Attribution and Intention
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ownership absent intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for an agent buying an unspecified slave and distinguish between Imam Muhammad's and Imam Abu Yusuf's positions when both parties agree no intention existed.

Core Idea
The default is that an agent acts for himself; without intention, payment decides ownership according to Abu Yusuf but not Muhammad.

This passage from Al-Hidayah unpacks the rules when a principal appoints an agent to buy an unspecified slave. The general ruling is that the purchase belongs to the agent unless he declares intention for the principal or uses the principal's money. However, the author details three scenarios based on attribution of the contract, and an intra-Hanafi dispute arises when both parties agree that the agent had no specific intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three forms of attribution
The passage states three ways the agent can attribute the contract: to the principal's money, to his own money, or to unspecified money. Identify each and the corresponding ruling.
Attribution is about to whom the contract is linguistically linked, not actual payment.
2
Understand the default rule and its exception
The default is that the agent acts for himself. The exception is if he declares intention or uses the principal's money. Note the consensus that when they dispute, the actual payment decides.
The default principle (al-asl) that everyone acts for himself is key.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute over absence of intention
When both agree that no intention existed, Muhammad holds the slave is for the agent (default); Abu Yusuf holds that the payment decides. Understand each imam's dalil.
Muhammad: al-asl; Abu Yusuf: istihsan based on apparent evidence.
4
Apply the rules to a scenario
Given a scenario of an agent buying an unspecified slave, state the ruling under each of Muhammad's and Abu Yusuf's views, and determine the practical difference.
Practical difference (thamarah) occurs when no payment or when payment source is ambiguous.

قال وان وكله بشراء عبد بغير عينه فاشترى عبدا فهو للوكيل الا ان يقول نويت الشراء للمؤكل او يشتريه بمال المؤكل قال رضى الله عنه هذه المسألة على وجوه ان اضاف العقد الى دراهم الأمر كان للآمر وهـ المراد عندى بقوله او يشتريه بمال المؤكل دون النقد من ماله لان فيه تفصيلا وخلافا وهذا بالاجماع وه مطلق وان اضافه الى دراهم نفسه كان لنفسه حملا لحاله على ما يحل له شرعا او يفعله عادة اذ الشراء لنفسه باضافة العقد الى دراهم غيره مستنكر شرعا و عرفا وان اضافه الى دراهم مطلقة فان نواها للآمر فهو للآمر وان نواها لنفسه فلنفسه لان له ان يعمل لنفسه ويعمل للآمر فى هذا التوكيل. وان تكاذبا في النية يحكم النقد بالاجماع لانه دلالة ظاهرة على ما ذكرنا وان توافقا على انه لم تحضره النية قال محمد هو للعاقد لان الاصل ان كل واحد يعمل لنفسه الا اذا ثبت جعله لغيره ولم يثبت وعند ابي يوسف يُحكم النقد فيه لان ما اوقعه مطلقا يحتمل الوجهين فيبقى موقوفا فمن اى المالين نقد فقد فعل ذالك المحتمل لصاحبه ولان مع تصادقهما يحتمل النية للآمر وفيما قلناه حمل حاله على الصلاح كما في حالة التكاذب
ترجمہ اور اگر مؤکل نے اس کو کسی عبد غیر معین کے خریدنے کا وکیل کیا پس وکیل نے ایک غلام خریدا تو وہ وکیل کا ہوگا ۔ مگر یہ کہ یوں کہے کہ میں نے موکل کیلئے خریدنے کی نیت کی یا اس کو موکل کے مال سے خریدے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اس مسئلہ کی کئی صورتیں ہیں اگر وکیل نے عقد مؤکل کی طرف دراہم کو منسوب کیا تو یہ عقد مؤکل کے واسطے ہو گا اور میرے نزدیک مصنف کے قول او یشتـریـه بمال المؤكل سے یہی مراد ہے نہ کہ موکل کے مال سے ادا کرنا کیونکہ اس میں تفصیل اور اختلاف ہے اور یہ حکم بالا جماع ہے حالانکہ مطلق ہے اور اگر وکیل نے عقد شراء کو اپنے دراہم کی طرف منسوب کیا تو یہ عقد شراء وکیل کے واسطے ہو گا۔ اس کے حال کو ایسی چیز پر محمول کرتے ہوئے جو اس کیلئے شرعاً حلال ہے یا اس کو عادہ کرتا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ دوسرے دراہم کی طرف عقد کی نسبت کر کے اپنے واسطے خریدنا شرعاً اور عرفا برابر ہے اور اگر وکیل نے عقد شراء کو دراہم مطلقہ کی طرف منسوب کیا۔ پس اگر اس نے مؤکل کیلئے اس کی نیت کی تو وہ موکل کیلئے ہوگا۔ اور اگر اپنے لئے نیت کی تو وہ اپنے لئے ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ اس تو کیل میں وکیل کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ اپنے واسطے عمل کرے یا موکل کے واسطے عمل کرے اور اگر وکیل اور موکل دونوں نے نیت میں ایک دوسرے کو جھٹلایا تو بالا جماع ادا کرنے کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ مذکورہ بیان پر ظاہری دلیل ہے۔ اور اگر دونوں نے اتفاق کیا کہ خرید کرتے وقت نیست موجود نہیں تھی۔ تو امام مجد نے فرمایا کہ یہ عقد شراء عاقد (وکیل) کیلئے ہوگا کیونکہ اصل یہی ہے کہ ہر آدمی اپنے واسطے عمل کرتا ہے۔ مگر جبکہ یہ ثابت ہو جائے کہ اس نے اپنا کام دوسرے کیلئے کر دیا ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ ثابت ہوا اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس میں بھی ادا کرنے کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وکیل نے جو کام مطلق واقع کیا ہے وہ دونوں صورتوں کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ پس یہ کام موقوف رہے گا۔ پس جس کے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا یہی قتل کام اسی کیلئے کیا اور اسلئے کہ دونوں کے عدم نیت پر اتفاق کرنے کے ساتھ موکل کرنا ہے۔ جیسا کہ ایک دوسرے کو جھٹلانے کی صورت میں اور اناج کی بیع سلم کیلئے وکیل کرنا بھی انہیں صورتوں پر ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص کو غیر معین غلام خریدنے کا وکیل کیا۔ پھر وکیل نے ایک غلام خرید لیا تو یہ خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی۔ اور وکیل ہی اس غلام کا مالک ہو گا لیکن اگر وکیل یہ کہے کہ میں نے مؤکل کے واسطے خرید کرنے کی نیت کی تھی۔ یا وکیل اس غلام کو موکل کے مال سے خریدے تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں یہ غلام مؤکل کا ہوگا۔
He said: If he appointed him as agent to buy an unspecified slave, and he bought a slave, it is for the agent unless he says 'I intended to buy for the principal' or he buys it with the principal's money. Radi Allahu 'anhu said: This issue has several aspects. If he attributes the contract to the money of the principal, it is for the principal – and this is what I understand from his saying 'or he buys it with the principal's money', not the actual payment from the principal's money because there is detail and difference, and this is by consensus even though it is absolute. If he attributes it to his own money, it is for himself, carrying his situation upon what is permissible for him legally or what he usually does, because buying for oneself while attributing the contract to another's money is legally and customarily objectionable. If he attributes it to unspecified money, then if he intended it for the principal, it is for the principal; if he intended it for himself, it is for himself, because it is permissible for him in this agency to act for himself and for the principal. If they contradict each other in intention, the money paid is judged by consensus, because it is an apparent indicator of what we mentioned. If they agree that he had no intention at the time, Muhammad said: It is for the contracting party (agent), because the default is that everyone acts for himself unless it is established that he made it for someone else, and it is not established. According to Abu Yusuf, the money paid is judged, because what he performed absolutely is possible for both aspects, so it remains pending. Whichever money he paid, he did that possible act for its owner. And also because, with their agreement on no intention, it is possible that he intended for the principal. And in what we said, his situation is carried upon righteousness, as in the case of contradiction.

Translation: And if the principal appointed him as agent to buy an unspecified slave, and the agent bought a slave, it is for the agent unless he says 'I intended to buy for the principal' or he buys it with the principal's money. The author of al-Hidayah said: This issue has several forms. If the agent attributed the contract to the money of the principal, then this contract is for the principal. And in my view, the author's statement 'or he buys it with the principal's money' refers to this, not to actual payment from the principal's money because there is detail and disagreement, and this ruling is by consensus, even though it is absolute. If the agent attributed the purchase contract to his own money, then this purchase is for the agent. His situation is carried upon what is legally permissible for him or what he habitually does, because buying for oneself while attributing the contract to another's money is legally and customarily objectionable. If the agent attributed it to unspecified money, then if he intended it for the principal, it is for the principal; if he intended it for himself, it is for himself, because in this agency it is permissible for the agent to act for himself or for the principal. If the agent and principal contradict each other in intention, the payment is judged by consensus because it is an apparent indicator of what we mentioned. If both agree that at the time of purchase there was no intention, Imam Muhammad said: This purchase is for the contractor (agent) because the default is that everyone acts for himself unless it is established that he made it for someone else, and it is not established. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the payment is judged because the agent performed an absolute act that is possible for both aspects, so it remains pending. Whichever money he paid, he did that possible act for its owner. Also, because with their agreement on no intention, it is possible that he intended for the principal. And in what we said, his situation is carried upon righteousness, as in the case of contradiction.

Explanation: The scenario of the issue is that if a person appointed another as agent to buy an unspecified slave, then the agent bought a slave, this purchase is for the agent, and the agent will be the owner of that slave. But if the agent says 'I intended to buy for the principal' or the agent buys this slave with the principal's money, then in both these cases the slave will be for the principal.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the situation where a principal appoints an agent to buy an unspecified slave. The general ruling is that unless the agent explicitly states he intended to buy for the principal or uses the principal's money, the purchase is for the agent. However, the author then elaborates on the details based on how the agent attributes the contract. Three scenarios: (1) If the agent attributes the purchase to the principal's money (i.e., says 'I buy this with your money'), it is for the principal. (2) If he attributes it to his own money, it is for himself. (3) If he does not specify whose money he is using (mursal), then the outcome depends on his intention: if he intended it for the principal, it is for the principal; if for himself, it is for himself. If they dispute over intention, the money used to pay the price is the deciding factor by consensus. If they both agree that no intention was present at the time of the contract, there is an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad says the purchase is for the agent (the contractor) because the default is that a person acts for himself. Imam Abu Yusuf says the money used to pay decides, similar to the case of dispute, because the absolute contract is pending and the payment resolves it.

Key Terms
وکيل (wakīl): Agent appointed to perform a transaction on behalf of another.
مؤکل (muwakkil): Principal who appoints the agent.
ثمن (thaman): Price or consideration in a sale.
نقد (naqd): Payment in currency, used as decisive evidence of intention.
اصل (asl): Default principle or presumption in law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when the agent and principal agree that no intention was present at the time of purchase, what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Yusuf?
A) The slave belongs to the agent because of the default principle.
B) The slave belongs to the principal because the agent was appointed for that purpose.
C) The ownership is decided by whose money was used to pay the price.
D) The purchase is void because intention is required.

Key Takeaway
When an agent buys an unspecified item without intention, the default is for the agent (Muhammad), but the payment decides according to Abu Yusuf, and the latter is often preferred for fatwa.

intermediate
8 min
Attribution of Dirhams in Agency Purchase: Rulings and Proofs
Explains the first two attribution scenarios with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an agent attributes the purchase to the principal's dirhams versus his own, and explain the proofs of custom and legal reasoning.

Core Idea
Attribution determines ownership: principal's dirhams = for principal; agent's dirhams = for agent.

When an agent is appointed to buy an unspecified slave, the contract's attribution of the dirhams is key. The Hanafi school distinguishes three scenarios; this lesson covers the first two agreed-upon scenarios and their proofs, which are based on custom and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three possible attributions
The agent may attribute the dirhams to the principal, to himself, or leave them absolute. The first two have consensus rulings; the third has nuance.
2
Scenario 1: Attribution to principal's dirhams
If the agent says 'I bought with the principal's dirhams', the purchase is for the principal. The text gives two proofs: custom (people attribute to the intended recipient) and legal (buying for oneself while attributing to another's property is prohibited).
This ruling is by consensus.
3
Scenario 2: Attribution to agent's own dirhams
If the agent says 'I bought with my own dirhams', the purchase is for the agent. The same proofs apply: custom and legal reasoning.
Also consensus.
4
Understand the rationale from custom and law
Custom ('urf) shows that people attribute to the one for whom they buy. Legally, it is objectionable to buy for oneself while attributing the contract to another's property.
This prevents deception and ambiguity.
