Slave's Absolute Self-Purchase: The Third Scenario
Third scenario of slave's purchase of himself as wakeel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a slave says 'sell my person into my hand' without specifying for whom, and explain why the absolute wording creates doubt leading to the slave's freedom.

Core Idea
Absolute wording creates doubt; doubt prevents compliance, so the transaction is for the slave himself.

We have previously examined two scenarios where a slave appointed as wakeel to purchase himself explicitly states for whom he is buying. In this third scenario, the slave uses absolute wording: 'sell my person into my hand' without adding 'for so-and-so'. The Hanafi school rules that this ambiguity leads to the slave's freedom. Let us analyze the proof and reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and ruling
Identify what the slave says and the legal consequence. The slave says 'sell my person into my hand' without specifying for whom; the ruling is that the slave becomes free.
2
Identify the dalil (proof)
The proof is the absolute wording 'myself' which bears two possibilities: for himself or for his principal. This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
The Arabic phrase: 'لان المطلق يحتمل الوجهين فلا يقع امتثالا بالشك'.
3
Apply the principle of doubt
Because of the ambiguity, the slave's speech cannot be considered as compliance with the principal's order. The act is therefore attributed to the slave himself.
Doubt (shakk) prevents the act from being attributed to the principal.
4
Connect to the consequence
When a slave purchases himself, he becomes free. Hence, in this scenario, the slave is free. The rule that a person transacts for himself, especially when it leads to emancipation, supports this.
This is consistent with earlier rulings on slave self-purchase.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام نے کہا تو میرے ہاتھ میری ذات فروخت کر دے اور یہ نہیں کہا کہ فلاں کے واسطے آزاد کر تو یہ غلام آزاد ہے وكذا الوقال بعني نفسي ولم يقل لفلان فهو حر لان المطلق يحتمل الوجهين فلا يقع امتثالا بالشك فيبقى التصرف واقعاً لنفسه ترجمہ اور اسی طرح اگر غلام نے کہا کہ تو میرے ہاتھ میری ذات فروخت کر دے اور یوں نہیں کہا کہ فلاں کے واسطے تو آزاد ہے۔ اسلئے کہ مطلق کلام دونوں صورتوں کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ لہذا شک کی وجہ سے یہ تمیل حکم نہ ہوگا۔ اور تصرف اپنی ذات کے واسطے باقی رہ جائے گا۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں مذکورہ تین صورتوں میں سے تیسری صورت مذکور ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ غلام نے عقد کو مطلق رکھا۔ یعنی نہ اپنی طرف منسوب کیا اور نہ اپنے مؤکل کی طرف منسوب کیا بلکہ غلام نے اپنے مولیٰ سے یوں کہا کہ تو میری ذات کو میرے ہاتھ فروخت کر دے اور اس پر کوئی اضافہ نہیں کیا تو اس صورت میں بھی غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غلام کا یہ کلام یعنی نفسی مطلق ہے۔ دونوں صورتوں کا احتمال ہے یعنی یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ غلام نے اپنی ذات کو اپنے واسطے خریدا ہوا اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ اپنے موکل کے واسطے خریدا ہو۔ پس جب دونوں احتمال بی تو غلام کا یہ کلام مشکوک ہوا۔ اور کلام مشکوک چونکہ حکم کی تعمیل قرار نہیں دیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اسلئے شک کی وجہ سے غلام کا یہ کلام موکل کے حکم کی تعمیل واقع نہ ہوگا۔ یعنی یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا کہ غلام نے موکل کے حکم کی تعمیل کی ہے اور اپنی ذات کو موکل کے واسطے خریدا ہے۔ اور جب غلام کا یہ کلام مؤکل کے حکم کی تعمیل واقع نہیں ہوا تو غلام کا یہ تصرف یعنی اپنی ذات کو خریدنا خود غلام کیو اسطے واقع ہوگا ۔ اور اس تصرف سے غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کیونکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ انسان اپنے واسطے تصرف کرے۔ خاص طور پر ایسا تصرف جس سے اعتاق حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال ثابت ہو گیا کہ غلام اس تیسری صورت میں بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
And similarly if the slave said, 'Sell my person into my hand' and did not say 'for so-and-so', then this slave is free. And likewise the agent said 'with myself' and did not say 'for someone', then he is free because the absolute wording bears both possibilities, so it does not constitute compliance due to doubt, so the transaction remains for himself. Commentary: This passage mentions the third of the three scenarios, the gist of which is that the slave left the contract absolute—he neither attributed it to himself nor to his principal—but he said to his master, 'Sell my person into my hand,' without adding anything. In this case too the slave becomes free. The proof is that the slave's speech, i.e. 'with myself', is absolute, bearing both possibilities: it is possible that the slave bought himself for himself, and possible that he bought for his principal. When both possibilities exist, the slave's speech becomes doubtful, and doubtful speech cannot be considered compliance with an order. Therefore, due to doubt, the slave's speech is not compliance with the principal's order, meaning it will not be said that he complied and bought himself for the principal. And since it is not compliance, the transaction of buying himself occurs for himself, and through this transaction the slave becomes free, as has passed earlier, because the apparent principle is that a person transacts for himself, especially a transaction that results in emancipation. In any case, it is established that the slave becomes free in this third scenario as well.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling for the third scenario in the discussion of a slave appointed as a wakeel to purchase himself. The scenario is when the slave says, 'Sell my person into my hand' without specifying for whom. The author explains that this absolute wording creates doubt—it could be for himself or for his principal. Due to this doubt, it cannot be considered compliance with the principal's order, and therefore the transaction is deemed for the slave himself. According to the earlier ruling, when a slave buys himself, he becomes free. The commentary also clarifies that the word 'myself' is absolute and ambiguous. The ruling is based on the principle that in case of doubt, the act is attributed to the one performing it, especially when it leads to emancipation, which is a favorable outcome.

Key Terms
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute wording that does not specify a particular person (e.g., 'myself' without indicating for whom).
شک (shakk): Doubt regarding the intention or compliance with an order, which prevents the act from being attributed to the principal.
تصرف (tasarruf): The legal act or transaction (here, the purchase of the slave's person).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the slave explicitly bought himself for himself.
B) Because the absolute wording creates doubt, so the act is attributed to himself, leading to emancipation.
C) Because the master's order was to buy for the principal, but the slave bought for himself, making the transaction valid for the slave.
D) Because the slave had permission to free himself.

Key Takeaway
When a slave says 'sell my person into my hand' without specifying for whom, he becomes free because the absolute wording creates doubt, preventing the act from being attributed to the principal.

Wakeel's Sale to Father/Grandparent: Dispute Between Imam Abu Hanifah and Sahibayn
Exposition of ruling and ikhtilaf on wakeel selling to close relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning behind Imam Abu Hanifah's and the Sahibayn's positions on a wakeel selling to close relatives, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A wakeel cannot sell to himself; Imam Abu Hanifah extends this to close relatives via tuhmah, but the Sahibayn do not.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over the validity of a wakeel (agent) selling the principal's property to his own father or grandfather. The source passage presents the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn, and extends the same disagreement to contracts of ijarah, sarf, and salam. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle of tuhmah in agency law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is a wakeel selling the principal's property to his own father or grandfather. What is the central question? Is it permissible?
Imam Abu Hanifah says no; Sahibayn say yes.
2
Understand the underlying principle: a wakeel cannot sell to himself
The text first establishes that a wakeel selling to his own slave or mukatab is impermissible because their possessions are effectively his. This sets the baseline: selling to oneself is invalid.
This is based on the inability of one person to be both offeror and acceptor.
3
Trace Imam Abu Hanifah's extension using tuhmah
Imam Abu Hanifah argues that selling to a father or grandfather is akin to selling to oneself because of tuhmah (suspicion). Evidence: testimony between them is rejected, and their benefits are interconnected (munafa' muttasil).
Thus the sale is a 'place of suspicion' and not permitted.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn hold that the wakeel has absolute authority (wakeel mutlaq) and tuhmah does not apply because the relative is a separate legal entity. The wakeel can contract with any third party unless specifically prohibited.
The sale is valid according to them.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and extension to other contracts
The practical difference: if the wakeel sells to his father, the sale is valid (Sahibayn) or invalid (Imam Abu Hanifah). The same disagreement applies to contracts of ijarah, sarf, and salam.
The passage does not state a tarjih (preferred view).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متہم بھی نہیں ہے تو ان لوگوں کے ساتھ عقد کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ بھی نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں وکیل کا اپنے اس غیر مدیون غلام کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا جس کے ذمہ کوئی قرضہ نہ ہو جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وکیل کا اپنے غیر مدیون غلام کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا خود اپنے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ غلام اور جو کچھ غلام کے قبضہ میں ہوتا ہے وہ سب مولیٰ کی ملک ہوتا ہے اس میں دوسرے کا کوئی حق نہیں ہوا۔ پس جب غلام اور غلام کے قبضہ کی تمام چیزیں مولی (وکیل) کی ملک ہیں تو وکیل کا اپنے غلام کے ہاتھ کسی چیز کو فروخت کرنا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ وکیل کا خود اپنے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں وکیل عقد بیچ کی دونوں طرفوں یعنی ایجاب و قبول کا متولی ہو جائے گا۔ حالانکہ ایک شخص عقد بیع کی دونوں طرفوں کا متولی نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس کی تفصیل کتاب النکاح کے اول میں گزر چکی ہے۔
اسی طرح وکیل کا اپنے مکاتب کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مولی کا اپنے مکاتب کی کمائی میں حق ہوتا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ مکاتب اپنی کمائی میں سے نہ کسی پر تبرع کرنے کا مجاز ہوتا ہے اور نہ اپنے غلام کا نکاح کر سکتا ہے اور جب مکاتب بدل کتابت ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہو جاتا ہے تو مولی کا یہ حق ، حقیقت ملک سے بدل جاتا ہے یعنی کا تب کے بدل کتابت ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہونے کی صورت میں مکاتب کو بدستور مولی کا غلام کر دیا جاتا ہے۔ اور جو کچھ اس کے پاس کمائی ہوتی ہے وہ سب مولیٰ کی ملک ہو جاتی ہے۔ بہر حال جب مکاتب کی کمائی میں مولیٰ کا حق ہے تو مولی (وکیل) کا اپنے مکاتب کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا بھی خود اپنے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا ہے اور پہلے گذر چکا ہے کہ اپنے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا وکیل کا اپنے مکاتب کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ بات تو تسلیم ہے کہ تو کیل مطلق ہے۔ لیکن تہمت کی جگہیں وکالتوں سے مستفی ہوتی دلیل ہیں یعنی وکیل جس شخص کے ساتھ معاملہ کرنے سے متہم ہوتا ہے۔ مؤکل کی جانب سے اس کے ساتھ معاملہ کرنے کی اس کو اجازت نہیں ہوتی۔
اور مسئلہ مذکورہ میں بھی یہ مقام تہمت کا ہے یعنی باپ دادا کے ساتھ معاملہ کرنے میں وکیل متہم ہے۔
ایک تو اسلئے کہ باپ، دادا، اور بیٹے کے درمیان ایک کی دوسرے کے حق میں گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ دوم... اسلئے کہ ان کے درمیان منافع باہم متصل ہیں۔ کیونکہ عاد باپ، بیٹے کے مال سے اور بیٹا، باپ کے مال سے نفع اٹھاتا ہے۔ پس باپ کا مال من وجہ بیٹے کا مال ہوا اور بیٹے کا مال من وجہ باپ کا مال ہوا۔ اور جب ایسا ہے تو وکیل کا اپنے باپ دادا و غیرہ کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا من وجہ اپنے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا ہوگا اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ اپنے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا نا جائز ہے۔ لہذا وکیل کا اپنے باپ، دادا وغیرہ کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا بھی نا جائز ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ عقد اجارہ اور عقد صرف میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہے اور یہی اختلاف عقد سلم میں ہے۔ یعنی اگر کسی شخص نے اجارہ کیلئے کسی کو وکیل کیا۔ مثلا یہ کہا کہ تو میرا یہ مکان کرایہ پر دے دے یا میرا یہ سونا سونے کے عوض فروخت کر دے۔ پس اگر وکیل نے یا یا اپنے باپ دادا یا ایسے شخص کے ساتھ عقد اجارہ کیا یا عقد صرف یا عقد سلم کیا جس کی گواہی اس کے حق میں جائز نہیں ہے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ عقد جائز ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔
He is not suspected either, then there is no harm in contracting with those people. Yes, the wakeel's selling through his own non-debtor slave who has no debt upon him is not permissible. Because the wakeel's selling through his own non-debtor slave is like selling through himself. Because the slave and whatever is in the slave's possession are all the property of the master; no one else has a right in it. So when the slave and all things in the slave's possession are the property of the master (the wakeel), then the wakeel's selling something through his own slave is like the wakeel selling through himself, which is not permissible. Because in that case the wakeel becomes the administrator of both sides of the sale contract, i.e., offer and acceptance, whereas one person cannot be the administrator of both sides of a sale contract. Its detail has passed at the beginning of Kitab al-Nikah. Similarly, the wakeel's selling through his own mukatab is not permissible. Because the master has a right in the earnings of his mukatab; for this reason the mukatab is not allowed to make a gift from his earnings nor can he marry his slave, and when the mukatab becomes unable to pay the kitabah instalments, the master's right changes from the reality of ownership, i.e., in the case of the mukatab's inability to pay the kitabah, the mukatab is made a slave of the master again, and whatever earnings he has become the master's property. In any case, when the master has a right in the mukatab's earnings, then the master (wakeel)'s selling through his own mukatab is also selling through himself, and it has passed before that selling through oneself is not permissible. Therefore the wakeel's selling through his own mukatab will also not be permissible. The proof of Hadrat Imam Abu Hanifah is that it is conceded that the wakeel is absolute. But the places of suspicion are deduced from agency contracts, meaning that the wakeel is suspected of the person with whom he transacts; he does not have permission from the principal to transact with that person. And in the mentioned issue, this is also a place of suspicion, i.e., the wakeel is suspected in transacting with his father and grandfather. First, because between father, grandfather, and son, testimony of one for the other is not accepted. Second, because benefits are interconnected between them, for usually a father benefits from his son's wealth and a son benefits from his father's wealth. So the father's wealth is in some respect the son's wealth, and the son's wealth is in some respect the father's wealth. And when this is the case, the wakeel's selling through his father, grandfather, etc. is in some respect selling through himself, and it has passed before that selling through oneself is impermissible. Therefore the wakeel's selling through his father, grandfather, etc. will also be impermissible. The author of Hidayah said that the same disagreement is in the contract of ijarah and the contract of sarf, and the same disagreement is in the contract of salam. That is, if a person appointed someone as wakeel for ijarah, for example, he said: 'You rent out this house of mine' or 'You sell this gold of mine for gold.' Then if the wakeel made a contract of ijarah, or sarf, or salam with his father, grandfather, or with such a person whose testimony is not permissible in his favour, then according to the Sahibayn this contract is permissible, and according to Imam Abu Hanifah it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a wakeel (agent) selling the principal's property to certain close relatives. The text first establishes that a wakeel cannot sell to himself because he would be both offeror and acceptor. It then extends this reasoning to selling through his own slave or mukatab because their possessions are effectively his. Then it transitions to the core issue: selling to one's father, grandfather, or similar relatives. Imam Abu Hanifah holds it impermissible due to tuhmah (suspicion of partiality) because the financial interests of these relatives are interconnected with the wakeel's own—testimony between them is rejected in court, and they mutually benefit from each other's wealth. Thus such a sale is akin to selling to oneself. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider the sale valid because the wakeel's authority is absolute and these relatives are not like the wakeel himself. The text notes that this same disagreement applies to contracts of ijarah (hire), sarf (currency exchange), and salam (advance sale). The commentary follows the author's order: first discussing the slave/mukatab cases, then the father/grandfather case, then the extension to other contracts. No tarjih (preference) is given in this passage.

Key Terms
تہمت (tuhmah): Suspicion of partiality or self-dealing that would compromise the agent's duty to act in the principal's best interest.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah (manumission by payment) with his master, thereby gaining limited rights over his earnings and person.
غیر مدیون (ghayr madyoon): A slave who is not indebted (i.e., owes no debt to anyone). In this context, a slave over whom the master has full ownership rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifah, why is a wakeel not allowed to sell the principal's property to his own father?
A) Because the father is not a Muslim.
B) Because the father's testimony is not accepted for the son, and their benefits are interconnected, creating suspicion of partiality.
C) Because the father is a minor.
D) Because the father is already a partner in the property.

Key Takeaway
A wakeel selling to his father is a place of tuhmah for Imam Abu Hanifah, making the sale invalid; the Sahibayn consider it valid based on absolute authority.

Wakeel's Sale for Low Price or Goods: Dispute Between Imam Abu Hanifah and Sahibayn
Exposition of ruling and ikhtilaf on wakeel selling below market value or for goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding the scope of a wakeel's authority to sell below market value or for goods, and explain the rationale behind each position.

Core Idea
A wakeel's authority is absolute according to Abu Hanifah, but restricted by custom according to the Sahibayn.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the limits of a sales agent's authority. When a principal appoints an agent (wakeel) to sell property, may the agent sell at a price far below market value or accept goods instead of cash? Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ on this question, and their reasoning sheds light on how custom and the nature of a transaction qualify an absolute command.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifah)
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifah permits: selling for a little or much, and for goods. Note that he considers the agency absolute.
2
Identify the opposing view (Sahibayn)
State that the Sahibayn restrict the agent to selling at the market price (thaman al-mithl) and for cash only. They prohibit ghabn fahish and barter.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
Understand their dalil: the absolute command is qualified by custom ('urf). Custom dictates sale at equivalent price and for cash. Also, ghabn fahish is partly a gift, and barter is partly a purchase, so the term 'sale' does not fully apply.
They analogize to the father and executor, who also lack such authority.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response (Abu Hanifah)
Abu Hanifah argues that the agency is absolute and should run except in cases of suspicion. Such sales are genuine sales (oath example) and customary in need. He distinguishes the ordinary wakeel from a father/executor, whose guardianship is advisory.
The dispute is about whether custom restricts the absolute language or not.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the wakeel sells at a gross loss or for goods, the sale is valid according to Abu Hanifah and invalid according to the Sahibayn.
This affects the principal's remedy if the agent acts against his interests.

He said: The agent for sale, selling for little and much and for goods is permissible according to Abu Hanifah, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: His selling at a deficiency that people do not overlook is not permissible, and it is not permissible except with dirhams and dinars. Because the absolute command is restricted by what is customary, because transactions are to fulfill needs, so they are restricted by their contexts, and the customary is sale at the equivalent price and with currency. For this reason, agency to buy coal, ice, and the sacrificial animal is restricted to the time of need. And because sale at a gross loss is in one respect a sale and in one respect a gift; likewise barter is in one respect a sale and in one respect a purchase, so the absolute name 'sale' does not include it. For this reason, the father and the executor do not have the power to do it. And his proof: that the agency for sale is absolute, so it proceeds on its absoluteness in other than a place of suspicion, and sale at a gross loss or for goods is customary when there is severe need for the price and boredom with the goods. And the issues are rejected according to Abu Hanifah's statement as is narrated from him, and it is a sale in every respect, so much so that if someone swears that he will not sell, he breaks his oath by it, except that the father and the executor do not have the power to do it even though it is a sale in every respect, because their guardianship is advisory and there is no consideration (nazar) in a sale at a gross loss. And barter is in every respect a purchase and in every respect a sale, because the definition of each one exists. Translation: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: According to Imam Abu Hanifah, it is permissible for the agent for sale to sell for little and much and for goods. And the two (Sahibayn) said: He cannot sell at such a loss that people do not tolerate, and he cannot sell except for dirhams and dinars. Because the absolute command in agency is restricted by custom. Because transactions are for fulfilling needs, so they are restricted to the contexts of needs, and the customary is sale at the equivalent price and sale for currency. For this reason, agency to buy coal, ice, and the sacrificial animal is restricted to the time of need. And because a sale at a gross loss is in one respect a sale and in one respect a gift; similarly, sale of goods for goods is in one respect a sale and in one respect a purchase. Therefore the absolute term 'sale' does not include it, and for this reason the father and the executor are not authorized to sell at a gross loss. The proof of Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifah) is that the agency for sale is absolute, so it proceeds on its absoluteness except in a place of suspicion. And selling at a gross loss or for goods is customary when the need for the price is severe and one is bored with the goods. And the issues are restricted according to the statement of Abu Hanifah as is narrated from him. And selling at a gross loss is completely a sale, even if someone swears that he will not sell, he breaks his oath by selling at a gross loss, except that the father and the executor do not have the power to do it, even though it is in every way a sale, because their guardianship is advisory and there is no consideration in selling at a gross loss. And sale of goods for goods is in every way a purchase and in every way a sale, because the definition of each exists. Explanation: The scenario is that if a person appointed another as agent for sale, e.g., he made him an agent to sell his slave, then according to Imam Abu Hanifah it is permissible for the agent to sell that slave for a small price or for a large price or for some goods such as grain or animal. And the Sahibayn said: For the agent, selling at a gross loss is not permissible, nor is selling for any goods other than dirhams and dinars permissible.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scope of authority of a wakeel bil-bay' (agent for sale). The core issue is whether the agent can sell the principal's property at a price significantly below market value (ghabn fahish) or in exchange for goods ('ard) instead of cash. Imam Abu Hanifah holds that the agent may sell for little or much, and for goods, because the agency is absolute (mutlaq) and such transactions are customary when necessity demands. The Sahibayn restrict the agent to selling at the market price and for cash (dirhams and dinars), arguing that the absolute command in agency is qualified by custom ('urf): people normally sell at the equivalent price for cash. A sale at a gross loss is partly a gift, and barter is partly a purchase, so the pure term 'sale' does not encompass them. They analogize to a father or executor, who are also restricted in such sales due to their advisory role (wilayah nazariyyah). Abu Hanifah counters that the sale at a gross loss is still a genuine sale in every respect, as evidenced by the fact that a person who swears not to sell would break his oath by such a sale; however, he concedes that a father and executor are restricted because their guardianship is advisory. The passage concludes by clarifying the scenario: if A appoints B as agent to sell his slave, Abu Hanifah allows B to sell for a low price, high price, or for goods; the Sahibayn forbid selling at a gross loss or for non-cash items. The text does not give a definitive tarjih.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): A sale at a price significantly below the market value such that people would not ordinarily accept such a loss. It is a technical term in Hanafi fiqh for excessive disadvantage.
سامان (saman): Goods or commodities used as payment instead of currency (cash). In this context, it refers to in-kind exchange (barter).
متعارف (muta'arif): Customary practice; what is conventionally accepted in society. In Hanafi usul, muta'arif is a source for restricting muhlaq commands in agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), why is a wakeel not allowed to sell the principal's property for goods instead of cash?
A) Because goods are not considered valid payment in Islamic law.
B) Because barter is partly a purchase and partly a sale, so it is not fully covered by the absolute term 'sale'.
C) Because the wakeel would be committing a sin.
D) Because the principal clearly specified cash only.

Key Takeaway
The scope of an agent's authority is determined by custom; the Hanafi school is divided on whether an absolute agency permits selling at a gross loss or for goods.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Agent's Authority for Ghabn Fahish and Barter
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's authority for ghabn fahish and barter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the scope of an absolute agent's authority to sell according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding ghabn fahish and barter.

Core Idea
An absolute agent may sell at any valid price or barter unless the principal explicitly restricts – Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn restrict by custom.

In this lesson, we examine an important intra-Hanafi disagreement on the limits of an agent's authority. The Sahibayn argue that an absolute agency is implicitly restricted by customary practice, while Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it covers all valid sales. The dispute turns on the nature of absolute commands and the role of custom in interpreting them.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and identify the two positions
The issue is whether an agent for sale can sell at a gross loss (ghabn fahish) or barter. Abu Hanifa permits; Sahibayn forbid.
The dispute is internal to the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's first proof: absolute command restricted by custom
The Sahibayn argue that the principal's absolute command to sell is restricted by customary practice (selling at market price for cash). They support this with the principle that transactions are legislated for needs, and custom determines the scope.
They give examples of seasonal agencies.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's second proof: ghabn fahish is partly a gift, barter partly a purchase
Since sale with gross fraud is partly a gift, it exceeds the agent's authority to sell only. Similarly, barter is partly a purchase.
Cite the father/minor and terminally ill patient rulings.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's counter-proofs
Abu Hanifa argues that an absolute agency includes all valid sales unless there is suspicion. He refutes the custom argument by noting need-based exceptions, and rejects the gift/purchase characterization using the oath example.
The oath example shows these are fully sales (min kulli wajh).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the practical consequence
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's. Practically, the agent's sale at a loss or barter binds the principal, and the agent is not liable.
This is the operative rule for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة
ہے۔ غبن فاحش یہ ہے کہ جس میں عام طور پر لوگ دھوکا نہ کھاتے ہوں اور جسمیں عام طور پر لوگ دخردہ کھا جاتے ہوں ۔ وہ مبین پیر ہے نہیں صاحبین کے نزدیک اس قدر کم دام میں بیچنا جس کے عوض عام لوگ نہ بیچتے ہوں جائز نہیں ہے۔ البتہ غین یسیر یعنی تھوڑے سے نقصان کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مؤکل کی طرف سے وکیل بالبیع کیلئے بیچنے کا امر مطلق ہے اور امر مطلق متعارف کے ساتھ مقید ہوتا یعنی جو طریقہ لوگوں میں متعارف ہوتا ہے امر مطلق اس کے ساتھ مقید ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ تصرفات ضرورتوں اور حاجتوں کو دور کرنے کیلئے مشروع کئے گئے ہیں اور جب تصرفات ، ضرورتوں اور حاجتوں کو دور کرنے کیلئے مشروع ہیں تو تصرفات انہیں ضرورتوں کے مواقع کے ساتھ مقید ہوں گے اور متعارف یعنی مروج یہ ہے کہ بیع میں شمن برابر کا ہو اور بیع ، نقد یعنی در اہم ودنا نیر کے عوض ہو ۔ پس مؤکل کا امر مطلق کے ساتھ بیچنے کا امرکر نا متعارف طریقہ پر یعنی شمن مثل اور نقود کے عوض بیچنے کا امر کرنا ہے اور جب مؤکل کا یہ امرشمن مثل اور نقود کے عوض بیچنے کا امر کرنا ہوا تو وکیل کیلئے اس امر کے خلاف تین فاحش کے ساتھ یا سامان کے عوض بیچنا جائز نہ ہوگا ۔ چونکہ تصرفات ضرورتوں کے مواقع کے ساتھ مقید ہوتے ہیں۔ اسلئے اگر کسی شخص نے کسی کوکوئلہ یا برف یا قربانی کا جانور خریدنے کا وکیل کیا تو یہ تو وکیل ضرورت کے زمانہ کے ساتھ مقید ہوگی۔ یعنی کوئلہ خریدنے کی توکیل اسی سال کے سردی کے زمانہ کے ساتھ مقید ہوگی اور برف خریدنے کی توکیل اسی سال کے گرمی کے زمانہ کے ساتھ مقید ہوگی اور قربانی کا جانور خریدنے کی توکیل اسی سال کے ایام اضحیہ کے ساتھ یا اس سے پہلے ایام کے ساتھ مقید ہو گی ۔ حتی کہ اگر وکیل نے ان چیزوں کو آئندہ سال خریدا تو موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی وجہت سی خریداری موکل پر لازم نہ ہو گی ۔ بلکہ خود وکیل پر لازم ہوگی ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ منین فاحش کے ساتھ بیع من وجہ توسیع ہے مگر من وجہ ہبہ ہے۔ کیونکہ جب ایک ہزار روپیہ کی چیز کو پانی سورہ بیہ کے عوض بیچا گیا تو گویا بائع نے آدھی چیز کوفروخت کیا اور آدھی کو ہبہ کیا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر مرض وفات میں مبتلا بیمار نے نہین فاحش کے ساتھ کوئی چیز فروخت کی تو اس کا اعتبار نٹ مال سے ہوگا۔ یعنی اگر یہ شی ، اس کے مال کا نمث یا ثلث سے کم ہو تو اس بی کو نافذ کردی جائے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ غبن فاحش کے ساتھ من وجہ بیج ہے اور من وجہ ہبہ ہے۔ اسی لئے صغیر کا باپ صغیر کے سامان کو اور میت کا وصی میت کی نا بالغ اولاد کے سامان کو شین فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ باپ اور وصی ، نابالغ کے سامان کو ہبہ کرنے کے مجاز نہیں : وتے ہیں۔ بہر حال مین فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا من وجہ ہبہ ہے اور وکیل با لبیع فروخت کرنے کا وکیل ہوتا ہے نہ کہ ہبہ کرنے گا ۔ ہیں جب وکیل بالسمیع فروخت کرنے کا وکیل ہوتا ہے اور ہبہ کرنے کا وکیل نہیں ہوتا تو فقط مبیع ، بیع بین الفاحش کو شامل نہ ہوگا اور وکیل کانین فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا مؤکل کے حکم کی مخالفت ہو گا اور وکیل کیلئے مؤکل کے حکم کمخالفت چونکہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے نہین فائش کے ساتھ وکیل بالبیع کا فروخت کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔
اسی طرح مقابضہ یعنی سامان کو سامان کے عوض فروخت کرنا من وجہ بیج ہے۔ اور من وجہ شراء ہے۔ بیع تو اسلئے ہے کہ بائع نے اپنے ملک سے سامان خارج کیا ہے اور شراء اسلئے ہے کہ سامان اس کی ملک میں داخل ہوا ہے۔ پس جب مقابضہ من وجہ بیج ہے اور من مسجد شراء ہے تو لفظ بیچ بیچ مقا بیضہ کو شامل نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب لفظ بیچ بیچ مقابضہ کو شامل نہیں ہے تو وکیل کی مقایضہ کے طور پر مؤکل کے سامان کو مامان کے عوض فروخت کرنا مؤکل کیلئے حکم کی مخالفت ہوگا اور مؤکل کے حکم کی مخالفت چونکہ وکیل کیلئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے وکیل کے واسطے مؤکل کے سامان کو سامان کے عوض فروخت کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔
حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے دلیل یہ ہے کہ تو کیل بالمیچ مطلق ہے۔ یعنی کسی چیز کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے اور مطلق موضع تہمت کے علاوہ میں اپنے اطلاق پر جاری ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا یہاں بھی تو کیل بالبیع اپنے اطلاق پر جاری ہوگی۔ یعنی جس پر بھی بیچ کا اطلاق درست ہوگا یہ تو کیل اس کو شامل ہوگی ۔ پس غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بھیج اور سامان کے عوض بیع بھی ایک گونہ بیچ ہے یہ تو کیل ان بیوع کو بھی شامل ہو گی ۔ اور جب تو کیل ان بیوع کو شامل ہے تو نین فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنا اور سامان کے عوض بیچ کرنا وکیل کا اپنے مؤکل کی مخالفت کرنا نہیں ہوگا اور جب نین فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنے اور سامان کے عوض بیچ کرنے سے مؤکل کے حکم کی مخالفت نہیں ہوتی تو وکیل کیلئے نین فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اور سامان کے عوض بیع کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ والبيع بالغبن او بالعين متعارف .... الخ سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہ تو تعلیم ہے کہ مطلق متعارف کیساتھ مقید ہوتا ہے لیکن صاحبین کا یہ کہنا کہ بیچ میں متعارف یہ ہے کہ ثمن مثل کے عوض ہو اور نقود ( در اہم و دنانیر ) کے عوض ہو غلط ہے کیونکہ اگر شمن کی شدید ضرورت ہو تو غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنا بھی متعارف ہے۔
اسی طرح اگر آدمی کسی سامان سے اکتا جائے تو وہ اس کو بہر صورت بیچنا چاہتا ہے خواہ سامان کے عوض ہی کیوں نہ فروخت ہو۔ بہر حال اس صورت میں سامان کے عوض بیچنا بھی متعارف ہے۔
والمسائل ممنوعة ... الخ سے صاحبین کی طرف سے پیش کردہ استشہاد کا جواب دیا گیا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ کوئلہ، برف اور قربانی کا جانور خریدنے کی تو کیل حاجت کے زمانہ کے ساتھ مقید ہونا حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول کی بناء پر تسلیم نہیں ہے۔ یعنی حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک ان چیزوں کی توکیل بھی مطلق ہے۔ زمانہ حاجت کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے۔ وکیل ہر زمانہ میں خریدنے کا مجاز ہے پس جب امام صاحب کے نزدیک ان چیزوں کو خریدنے کی تو کیل بھی مطلق ہے اور کسی زمانہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے تو ان مسائل کے ذریعہ حضرت امام صاحب کے خلاف استشہاد کرنا کس طرح درست ہوگا۔ وانه بيع من كل وجه ...... الخ سے صاحبین کی دوسری دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کی یہ بات کہ غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیچ اور سامان کے عوض بیع من وجہ بیج ہے اور من وجہ بیع نہیں ہے ۔ ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ دونوں من کل وجہ بیع ہیں۔
اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ میں بیچ نہیں کروں گا۔ اور یوں کہا والله لا ابيع اور پھر اس نے غبن فاحش کے ساتھ کوئی چیز فروخت کی یا سامان کے عوض کوئی چیز فروخت کی تو یہ شخص حانث ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس اگر غبن فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا اور سامان کے عوض فروخت کرنا من کل وجہ بیج نہ ہوتا تو یہ شخص حانث نہ ہوتا۔ اس شخص کا اپنی قسم میں حانث ہو جاتا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ دونوں من کل وجہ بیع ہیں اور جب یہ دونوں یعنی نین فاحش کیسا تھ فروخت کرنا اور سامان کے عوض فروخت کرنا باب پین میں من کل وجہ بیع ہیں تو باب وکالت میں بھی من کل وجہ بیچ ہوں گے۔
Book of Agency. Ghabn fahish (gross fraud) is that in which people generally do not get deceived, and that in which people generally do get deceived. That is not [acceptable] in the view of the Sahibayn; selling at such a low price that people generally do not sell for is not permissible. However, selling with ghabn yasir (slight loss) is permissible. The proof of the Sahibayn is that the principal's command to the agent for sale is absolute, and an absolute command is restricted by custom – that is, the absolute command is restricted to the customary practice. Because transactions are legislated to fulfill necessities and needs, and when transactions are legislated for necessities and needs, they are restricted to the occasions of those necessities. Customary practice is that in a sale the price is equivalent (thaman mithl) and the sale is for cash (dirhams and dinars). So the principal's absolute command to sell is a command to sell according to custom, i.e., for the equivalent price and for currency. And when the principal's command is to sell for equivalent price and currency, then for the agent to sell contrary to this command with ghabn fahish or in exchange for goods is not permissible. Since transactions are restricted to the occasions of needs, therefore if someone appoints an agent to buy coal, ice, or a sacrificial animal, this agency is restricted to the time of need. That is, agency to buy coal is restricted to the winter of that year, agency to buy ice is restricted to the summer of that year, and agency to buy a sacrificial animal is restricted to the days of sacrifice of that year or the days before. So much so that if the agent buys these things in the following year, the purchase is not binding on the principal due to contravening his command; rather it is binding on the agent himself. The second proof is that sale with ghabn fahish is in one aspect a sale but in another aspect a gift. Because when an item worth one thousand rupees is sold for five hundred, it is as if the seller sold half the item and gave half as a gift. This is why if a terminally ill patient sells something with ghabn fahish, its validity depends on the total wealth. That is, if this item is less than a third or a half of his wealth, the sale is enforced; otherwise not. Sale with ghabn fahish is in one aspect a sale and in one aspect a gift. Therefore, a father of a minor cannot sell the minor's property with ghabn fahish, and the executor of the deceased cannot sell the property of the minor children with ghabn fahish, because the father and executor are not authorized to give gifts from the minor's property. In any case, selling with ghabn fahish is in one aspect a gift, and the agent for sale is an agent for sale, not for gift. When the agent is an agent for sale and not for gift, then the absolute agency (tawkil) does not include sale with ghabn fahish, and the agent selling with ghabn fahish would be contravening the principal's command. And since contravening the principal's command is not permissible for the agent, therefore selling with ghabn fahish by the agent for sale is also not permissible. Similarly, muqabadah (exchange) – i.e., selling goods for goods – is in one aspect a sale and in one aspect a purchase. It is a sale because the seller has removed goods from his ownership, and a purchase because goods have entered his ownership. So when muqabadah is in one aspect a sale and in one aspect a purchase, the word 'sale' does not include muqabadah. And when the word 'sale' does not include muqabadah, then the agent's selling the principal's goods in exchange for goods is a contravention of the principal's command, and since contravention is not permissible, it is not permissible for the agent to sell the principal's goods in exchange for goods. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the agency for sale is absolute – i.e., not restricted to anything – and an absolute (muthlaq) operates on its generality except where there is suspicion (tuhma). Therefore, here the agency for sale operates on its generality. That is, whatever constitutes a valid sale, this agency includes it. So sale with ghabn fahish and sale in exchange for goods are also types of sale, and the agency includes these sales. And when the agency includes these sales, then selling with ghabn fahish and selling in exchange for goods is not contravening the principal's command. And when there is no contravention, then it is permissible for the agent to sell with ghabn fahish and in exchange for goods. The phrase 'wal-bay'u bil-ghabni aw bil-'ayni muta'arif...' is the answer to the Sahibayn's proof. The summary of the answer is that it is acknowledged that an absolute is restricted by custom, but the Sahibayn's claim that the custom in sale is that it must be for an equivalent price and for currency (dirhams and dinars) is wrong, because if there is severe need for money, then selling with ghabn fahish is also customary. Similarly, if a person is fed up with goods, he wants to sell them at any cost, even if in exchange for goods. In that case, selling in exchange for goods is also customary. The phrase 'wal-masa'ilu mamnu'ah...' is an answer to the istishhad (example) presented by the Sahibayn. The summary is that the restriction of agency to buy coal, ice, and sacrificial animal to the time of need is not accepted on the basis of Imam Abu Hanifa's saying. That is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the agency for these things is also absolute, not restricted to the time of need. The agent is authorized to buy at any time. So when according to Imam Abu Hanifa the agency for these things is absolute and not restricted to any time, how can it be correct to use these examples as evidence against him? The phrase 'wa annahu bay'un min kulli wajh...' is an answer to the Sahibayn's second proof. The summary is that the Sahibayn's claim that sale with ghabn fahish and sale in exchange for goods is a sale in one aspect and not a sale in another aspect is not accepted. Rather, both are sales from every aspect (min kulli wajh). And the proof is that if someone swears 'By Allah, I will not sell' (wa'llahi la abi') and then sells with ghabn fahish or sells in exchange for goods, he becomes a breaker of his oath (hanith). So if selling with ghabn fahish and selling in exchange for goods were not sales from every aspect, he would not be a breaker of his oath. The fact that he becomes a breaker proves that both are sales from every aspect. And when both – selling with ghabn fahish and selling in exchange for goods – are sales from every aspect in the chapter of oaths, then in the chapter of agency they are also sales from every aspect.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scope of authority of an agent appointed for sale (wakil bil-bay'). The central question is whether an absolute agency to sell permits the agent to sell at a price involving gross fraud (ghabn fahish) or to barter goods (muqabadah) instead of selling for cash at the market price.

The passage first defines ghabn fahish (gross fraud) as a sale at a price so low that the public would not normally deceive each other with such a price, distinguishing it from ghabn yasir (slight loss) which is permissible. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that such sales are not permissible for the agent. Their first proof relies on the principle that an absolute command (amr mutlaq) is restricted by custom ('urf). Since transactions are legislated to fulfill needs, they are tied to the occasions of those needs. Custom in sales requires the price to be equivalent (thaman mithl) and to be in currency (dirhams/dinars). Therefore, the principal's absolute command to sell is inherently a command to sell according to this custom, and any departure — such as selling at a gross loss or in exchange for goods — violates the command. To illustrate, they give examples of agency to buy coal, ice, or a sacrificial animal, which are implicitly restricted to the relevant season/year.

The Sahibayn's second proof argues that sale with ghabn fahish is partly a sale and partly a gift (hibah), because the seller gives away part of the value. Since the agent is only authorized to sell, not to give gifts, such a transaction exceeds the agent's authority. Similarly, muqabadah (barter) is partly a sale and partly a purchase, so the agent, who is appointed to sell, cannot engage in a transaction that also involves buying.

Imam Abu Hanifa counters that the agency for sale is absolute and unrestricted. An absolute command operates on its full scope except where there is suspicion of misconduct (tuhma). Since both ghabn fahish and barter are valid forms of sale, they are included in the agency. He refutes the Sahibayn's custom argument by noting that custom can vary; if there is a pressing need for cash or if the owner is fed up with the goods, selling at a loss or for goods becomes customary. He also rejects the analogy of seasonal items, maintaining that such agencies are also absolute according to him. Finally, he uses the example of an oath: if someone swears 'I will not sell' and then engages in a ghabn fahish or barter sale, they break the oath, proving that these are fully considered sales (min kulli wajh) in Islamic law.

The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as indicated by the text's defense of his view. Thus, an agent with absolute authority may sell at any valid price, including below market value, or in exchange for goods, unless the principal explicitly restricts these.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): A sale at a price significantly below market value such that people would generally not deceive each other with it; gross fraud.
وکیل بالبیع (wakil bil-bay'): An agent appointed to sell the principal's property.
مقابضہ / مقابضۃ (muqabadah): A barter transaction, exchanging goods for goods rather than for cash.
امر مطلق (amr mutlaq): An absolute command without any qualification or restriction.
من کل وجہ (min kulli wajh): From every aspect; fully and completely (a type of sale).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if an agent for sale sells the principal's property at a price significantly below market value (ghabn fahish), what is the legal status of this sale?
A) The sale is void and the agent is liable for the loss.
B) The sale is valid and binding on the principal.
C) The sale is valid only if the principal had explicitly permitted it.
D) The sale is considered a gift, not a sale.

Key Takeaway
An absolute agent for sale may sell at any valid price or barter unless the principal explicitly restricts, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on General Agent's Authority to Sell with Gross Disparity or Barter
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of general agency in sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether a general agent may sell with gross disparity or barter, and distinguish the evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa from that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
An absolute agency includes all valid sales unless suspicion or restriction is proven.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about the scope of a general agent's authority when the principal simply says 'sell my property.' The two sides, Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Sahibayn), disagree on whether the agent can sell at a gross loss or in exchange for goods. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school balances absolute authorization with customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Dispute
Note that the act in question is a sale executed by a general agent (wakil bi al-bay') without explicit restriction. The dispute is whether such an agent may sell: (a) with gross disparity (ghaban fahish) or (b) by barter (muqayada).
The principal's instruction is assumed to be general, e.g., 'Sell this property.'
2
State Each Side's Position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the agent is authorized to sell with gross disparity and by barter because the agency is absolute. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the agent is restricted to customary sales for a similar cash price; disparity and barter are not included without explicit permission.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both are respected mujtahids within the school.
3
Examine the Evidence for Each
Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence: (1) The agency is mutlaq, and the absolute operates generally absent suspicion. (2) In oaths, such sales are considered full sales (min kulli wajh), proving they are true sales. (3) Custom varies: in need, disparity and barter become customary. The Sahibayn's evidence: (1) Custom (urf) restricts the absolute; sale is normally for cash at a fair price. (2) Precedents like buying coal, ice, and sacrificial animals are restricted to times of need. (3) Such sales are only partial sales (min wajh). (4) Barter is partially a purchase, so an agent for sale cannot do it.
The oath analogy is crucial: if one swears not to sell and then sells with disparity or by barter, he breaks his oath — proof that these are full sales.
4
Analyze the Responses and Rebuttals
Imam Abu Hanifa responds to each Sahibayn argument: (1) Custom is not static; in urgent need, these sales become customary. (2) The precedents are themselves absolute in his view — they do not prove restriction. (3) Oath cases confirm they are full sales, so they fall under the absolute agency. (4) Barter satisfies the definitions of both sale and purchase fully, hence it is included in an agency for sale.
The Sahibayn also raise an objection regarding the father and executor: if selling with disparity is a full sale, then they should be able to do it for minors, but they cannot. The response: their guardianship is based on compassion, and selling with disparity shows no compassion.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and the Mufta Bihi
Practical consequence: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale is valid, but the agent may be liable for loss if it was not beneficial. According to the Sahibayn, the sale is invalid without explicit permission. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Imam Abu Hanifa's, as it protects transaction validity and ease of business.
The commentator (Ashraf al-Hidaya) defends Abu Hanifa's view through detailed rebuttals.

کتاب الوكالة
اشرف البدایہ جلد دہم کے عوض فروخت کرنا مؤکل کیلئے حکم کی مخالفت ہوگا اور مؤکل کے حکم کی مخالفت چونکہ وکیل کیلئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے وکیل کے واسطے مؤکل کے سامان کو سامان کے عوض فروخت کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔
حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے دلیل یہ ہے کہ توکیل بالبیع مطلق ہے۔ یعنی کسی چیز کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے اور مطلق موضع تہمت کے علاوہ میں اپنے اطلاق پر جاری ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا یہاں بھی توکیل بالبیع اپنے اطلاق پر جاری ہوگی۔ یعنی جس پر بھی بیع کا اطلاق درست ہوگا یہ توکیل اس کو شامل ہوگی ۔ پس غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع اور سامان کے عوض بیع بھی ایک گونہ بیع ہے یہ توکیل ان بیوع کو بھی شامل ہو گی ۔ اور جب توکیل ان بیوع کو شامل ہے تو غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنا اور سامان کے عوض بیع کرنا وکیل کا اپنے مؤکل کی مخالفت کرنا نہیں ہوگا اور جب غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنے اور سامان کے عوض بیع کرنے سے مؤکل کے حکم کی مخالفت نہیں ہوتی تو وکیل کیلئے غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اور سامان کے عوض بیع کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ والبيع بالغبن او بالعين متعارف .... الخ سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہ تو تعلیم ہے کہ مطلق متعارف کیساتھ مقید ہوتا ہے لیکن صاحبین کا یہ کہنا کہ بیع میں متعارف یہ ہے کہ ثمن مثل کے عوض ہو اور نقود ( دراہم و دنانیر ) کے عوض ہو غلط ہے کیونکہ اگر ثمن کی شدید ضرورت ہو تو غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنا بھی متعارف ہے۔
اسی طرح اگر آدمی کسی سامان سے اکتا جائے تو وہ اس کو بہر صورت بیچنا چاہتا ہے خواہ سامان کے عوض ہی کیوں نہ فروخت ہو۔ بہر حال اس صورت میں سامان کے عوض بیچنا بھی متعارف ہے۔
والمسائل ممنوعة ... الخ سے صاحبین کی طرف سے پیش کردہ استشہاد کا جواب دیا گیا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ کوئلہ، برف اور قربانی کا جانور خریدنے کی توکیل حاجت کے زمانہ کے ساتھ مقید ہونا حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول کی بناء پر تسلیم نہیں ہے۔ یعنی حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک ان چیزوں کی توکیل بھی مطلق ہے۔ زمانہ حاجت کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے۔ وکیل ہر زمانہ میں خریدنے کا مجاز ہے پس جب امام صاحب کے نزدیک ان چیزوں کو خریدنے کی توکیل بھی مطلق ہے اور کسی زمانہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے تو ان مسائل کے ذریعہ حضرت امام صاحب کے خلاف استشہاد کرنا کس طرح درست ہوگا۔ وانه بيع من كل وجه ...... الخ سے صاحبین کی دوسری دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کی یہ بات کہ غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع اور سامان کے عوض بیع من وجہ بیع ہے اور من وجہ بیع نہیں ہے ۔ ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ دونوں من کل وجہ بیع ہیں۔
اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ میں بیع نہیں کروں گا۔ اور یوں کہا والله لا ابيع اور پھر اس نے غبن فاحش کے ساتھ کوئی چیز فروخت کی یا سامان کے عوض کوئی چیز فروخت کی تو یہ شخص حانث ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس اگر غبن فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا اور سامان کے عوض فروخت کرنا من کل وجہ بیع نہ ہوتا تو یہ شخص حانث نہ ہوتا۔ اس شخص کا اپنی قسم میں حانث ہو جاتا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ دونوں من کل وجہ بیع ہیں اور جب یہ دونوں یعنی غبن فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا اور سامان کے عوض فروخت کرنا باب یمین میں من کل وجہ بیع ہیں تو باب وکالت میں بھی من کل وجہ بیع ہوں گے۔

غير ان الاب والوصى ... الخ سے سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع اگر من کل وجہ بیع ہے تو باپ اور وصی کو صغیر کا مال غبن فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنے کا اختیار ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ ان کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے۔
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صغیر پر باپ اور وصی کی ولایت نظری ہے۔ یعنی صغیر پر ولایت حاصل ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ ولی صغیر پر شفقت کرے اور اسکے حق میں خیر اندیش ہو مگر غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنے میں باپ اور وصی کی طرف سے چونکہ صغیر کے حق میں کوئی شفقت کا مظاہرہ نہیں ہوا۔ اسلئے باپ اور وصی کو صغیر کا مال غبن فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنے کی قطعا ولایت حاصل نہ ہو گی۔ والمقايضة شراء من كل وجه .... الخ سے صاحبین کی دوسری دلیل کے دوسرے جز کا جواب ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کا یہ فرمانا کہ مقایضہ یعنی سامان کے عوض بیچنا من وجہ بیع ہے اور من وجہ شراء ہے۔ ہمیں تسلیم نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ من کل وجہ بیع بھی ہے اور من کل وجہ شراء بھی ہے کیونکہ اس پر بیع اور شراء دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی تعریف صادق آتی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بیع کہتے ہیں اپنی ملک سے کسی چیز کو نکال کر دوسرے کی چیز کو اپنی ملک میں داخل کرنا۔ اور شراء کہتے ہیں دوسرے کی چیز اپنی ملک میں داخل کرنے کیلئے اپنی ملک سے کسی چیز کو نکالنا۔ بیع مقایضہ پر چونکہ یہ دونوں تعریفین صادق آتی ہیں۔ اسلئے بیع مقایضہ من کل وجہ بیع بھی ہے اور من کل وجہ شراء بھی ہے۔ اور جب بیع مقایضہ من کل وجہ بیع ہے تو وکیل بالبیع کو موکل کی طرف سے بیع مقایضہ کرنے کا پورا پورا حق ہوگا۔ اور جب وکیل بالبیع کو بیع مقایضہ کرنے کا حق ہے تو وکیل بالبیع کیلئے موکل کے مال کو سامان کے عوض فروخت کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔
Book of Agency. Selling in exchange for [the book] Ashraf al-Hidaya volume ten would be a violation of the principal's order, and since violating the principal's order is not permissible for the agent, therefore it is not permissible for the agent to sell the principal's goods in exchange for goods. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the agency for sale is absolute, i.e., not restricted to any particular thing, and the absolute in the absence of suspicion operates according to its generality. Therefore here the agency for sale will operate according to its generality, meaning it will include whatever sale is validly applicable. Thus sale with gross disparity and sale in exchange for goods are also a type of sale, and this agency will include these sales. And when the agency includes these sales, selling with gross disparity and selling in exchange for goods would not be a violation of the principal by the agent, and when these do not violate the principal's order, then selling with gross disparity and selling in exchange for goods are permissible for the agent. 'And the sale with disparity or for goods is customary... etc.' is the response to the Sahibayn's evidence. The gist of the response is that this is a specification that the absolute is restricted by the customary, but the Sahibayn's statement that in sale the customary is in exchange for a similar price and in exchange for currency (dirhams and dinars) is incorrect, because if there is severe need for price, then selling with gross disparity is also customary. Similarly, if a person becomes bored with some goods, he wants to sell it by any means, even if it be in exchange for goods; in any case, selling in exchange for goods is also customary. 'And the issues are prevented... etc.' is the response to the istishhad (citation of precedents) presented by the Sahibayn. The gist is that the agency for buying charcoal, ice, and sacrificial animal being restricted to the time of need is not accepted based on Imam Abu Hanifa's statement; that is, according to Imam Sahib, agency for these things is also absolute, not restricted to the time of need. The agent is authorized to buy at any time. So when according to Imam Sahib agency for buying these things is absolute and not restricted to any time, how can istishhad be correct against Imam Sahib through these issues? 'And that it is a sale from every aspect... etc.' is the response to the Sahibayn's second evidence. The gist is that the Sahibayn's statement that sale with gross disparity and sale in exchange for goods are sale from one aspect and not sale from all aspects is not accepted by us; rather both are sale from every aspect. And the evidence is that if someone swore that 'I will not sell' and said 'By Allah, I will not sell', and then he sold something with gross disparity or in exchange for goods, then this person becomes sinful (hanith). So if selling with gross disparity and selling in exchange for goods were not sale from every aspect, then this person would not be sinful. That this person becomes sinful in his oath is evidence that both are sale from every aspect. And when both – selling with gross disparity and selling in exchange for goods – are sale from every aspect in the chapter of oaths, then in the chapter of agency they will also be sale from every aspect. 'Except that the father and executor... etc.' is the response to an implied question. The question is: if sale with gross disparity is sale from every aspect, then the father and executor should have the authority to sell the minor's property with gross disparity, whereas they do not have this authority. The answer to this is that the father and executor have guardianship of consideration (wilayat nazari) over the minor, i.e., the condition for having guardianship over the minor is that the guardian treat the minor with compassion and seek his benefit, but in selling with gross disparity, since there is no manifestation of compassion from the father and executor towards the minor, they absolutely do not have guardianship to sell the minor's property with gross disparity. 'And muqayada (barter) is purchase from every aspect... etc.' is the response to the second part of the Sahibayn's second evidence. The gist is that the Sahibayn's statement that muqayada, i.e., selling in exchange for goods, is sale from one aspect and purchase from one aspect, is not accepted by us; rather it is sale from every aspect and purchase from every aspect, because both definitions of sale and purchase apply to it. Because sale is called taking something out of one's ownership and bringing something else into one's ownership, and purchase is called taking something out of one's ownership to bring something else into one's ownership. Since both definitions apply to sale by muqayada, therefore muqayada is both sale from every aspect and purchase from every aspect. And when muqayada is sale from every aspect, then an agent for sale has complete right to do muqayada on behalf of the principal. And when the agent for sale has the right to do muqayada, then selling the principal's goods in exchange for goods is also permissible for the agent for sale.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the scope of a general agent's authority to sell. The discussion begins by stating the Sahibayn's position: if an agent is appointed to sell a specific item, selling it in exchange for goods (barter) violates the principal's order, so it is impermissible. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that an agency for sale (wakalah bil-bay') is absolute (mutlaq), not restricted to any particular type of sale. In the absence of suspicion (tuhmah), the absolute operates according to its generality, including all valid sales such as sale with gross disparity or barter. The Sahibayn argue that the customary practice (urf) restricts the absolute; here the custom is sale for a similar price in cash, so barter and disparity are not included. Imam Abu Hanifa responds that custom varies: in times of need, selling with disparity is customary, and if someone is fed up with goods, barter is also customary. The Sahibayn cite precedents (istishhad) of buying charcoal, ice, and sacrificial animals being restricted to times of need. Imam Abu Hanifa rejects this because those are also absolute in his view. The Sahibayn then argue that such sales are only partially sales (min wajh). Imam Abu Hanifa proves they are full sales (min kulli wajh) by oath: if one swears not to sell and then makes such a sale, he breaks his oath, showing they are considered full sales. An objection arises: if they are full sales, then a father and executor should also have authority to sell the minor's property with gross disparity, but they do not. The response is that their guardianship is based on compassion, and selling at a loss shows no compassion. Finally, the Sahibayn claim barter is sale from one aspect and purchase from another. Imam Abu Hanifa defines sale as transferring ownership of one's property for another's property, and purchase as acquiring property by giving something; barter satisfies both definitions fully. Therefore, a general agent has full authority to barter or sell with gross disparity. This dispute follows the Hanafi principle that an absolute authorization is interpreted broadly unless there is clear evidence of restriction or suspicion of misconduct.

Key Terms
توکیل بالبیع (tawkil bi al-bay'): Agency for sale; granting authority to another to sell one's property. In this text, it is considered absolute (mutlaq) unless explicitly restricted.
غبن فاحش (ghaban fāḥish): Gross disparity; a difference between the price and the market value that is not ordinarily tolerated by custom. In this text, it is a type of sale that is permissible for a general agent according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
مقایضہ (muqāyaḍah): Barter; exchanging goods for goods without cash. In this text, it is considered a full sale (bay' min kulli wajh) and also a full purchase (shira' min kulli wajh) because the definitions of both apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider selling with gross disparity or barter to be included in a general agency for sale?
A) Because the agent has explicit permission to do so in the contract
B) Because the agency is absolute and includes all types of sale, and such transactions are considered full sales (min kulli wajh)
C) Because the principal always intends the agent to act in his best interest
D) Because the Sahibayn agreed with Imam Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position is that an absolute agency for sale includes all valid sale types, including barter and selling with disparity, unless there is evidence of restriction or suspicion.

Price Limits for an Agent for Purchase
Ruling on permissible price range for an agent authorized to purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible price range for an agent authorized to purchase and distinguish between permissible slight disparity (ghaban yasir) and prohibited gross disparity (ghaban fahish) based on the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
An agent for purchase may buy at market value or with slight disparity; gross disparity invalidates the purchase due to suspicion of self-dealing.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common question in agency: within what price limits may an agent buy? The Hanafi school establishes a clear distinction based on custom and the presence of suspicion (tuhmah). Understanding this ruling is essential for anyone acting as a purchasing agent or advising on agency contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the agent for purchase (wakīl bi al-shirā') making a purchase contract. The ruling is that it is permissible at market value or with slight disparity, and impermissible with gross disparity.
2
Understand the basis: suspicion (tuhmah)
The prohibition is due to the strong suspicion that the agent may be buying for himself and then attributing the purchase to the principal. Gross disparity triggers this suspicion.
3
Distinguish slight vs. gross disparity
Slight disparity (ghaban yasīr) is what people ordinarily tolerate; gross disparity (ghaban fāḥish) is not tolerated. Custom ('urf) determines the threshold, which varies by commodity and time.
4
Note the exceptions
For purchase of a specific item (shay' mu'ayan), the agent's purchase binds the principal because the agent cannot buy it for himself. For marriage agency, the contract must be attributed to the principal, so no suspicion arises.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, an agent must stay within the customarily acceptable price range. If the agent buys at a grossly inflated price, the principal may reject the purchase and hold the agent liable for the excess.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وکیل بالشراء کا مثل قیمت کے ساتھ اور اتنے ثمن کے ساتھ جس کے مثل لوگ دھوکہ کھا جاتے ہیں عقد کرنا جائز ہے

قال والوكيل بالشراء يجوز عقده بمثل القيمة وزيادة يتغابن الناس فى مثلها ولا يجوز بما لا يتغابن الناس في مثله لان التهمة فيه متحققة فلعله اشتراه لنفسه فاذا لم يوافقه الحقه بغيره على مامر حتى لو كان وكيلا بشراء شيء بعينه قالوا ينفذ على الأمر لانه لا يملك شراءه لنفسه وكذا الوكيل بالنكاح اذا زوجه امرأة باكثر من مهر مثلها جاز عنده لانه لا بد من الاضافة الى المؤكل فى العقد فلا تتمكن هذه التهمة ولا كذا الوكيل بالشراء لانه يطلق العقد

ترجمہ اور وکیل بالشراء کا مثل قیمت کے عوض اور ایسی زیادتی کے عوض جس کے مثل میں لوگ دھوکا کھا جاتے ہوں عقد کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور ایسی زیادتی کے عوض جس کے مثل میں لوگ دھوکا نہ کھاتے ہوں جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ غبن فاحش کے ساتھ خریدنے میں تہمت متحقق ہے۔ چنانچہ ممکن ہے کہ وکیل نے اس کو اپنے واسطے خریدا ہو۔ مگر جب اسکے موافق نہ ہوئی تو اس نے اس کو دوسرے کے ذمہ ڈال دیا۔ چنانچہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر وکیل خرید شی معین کا ہو تو مشائخ نے کہا کہ اس کو موکل پر نافذ کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وکیل نے اس کو اپنے واسطے خریدنے کا مالک نہیں کیا ہے۔ اسی طرح وکیل بالنکاح نے جب مہر مثل سے زیادہ کے عوض کسی عورت کے ساتھ عقد نکاح کیا تو وہ جائز ہے اسکے نزدیک کیونکہ عقد میں موکل کی طرف اضافہ ضروری ہے، اس لئے یہ تہمت متحقق نہیں ہوتی۔ اور ایسا ہی وکیل بالشراء میں نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ عقد کو مطلق کرتا ہے۔
The agent for purchase may make a contract at the equivalent price and with an increase in the like of which people are deceived, and it is not permissible with an increase in the like of which people are not deceived.

He said: The agent for purchase may make a contract at the market value and with an increase the like of which people are deceived (i.e., slight disparity), and it is not permissible with an increase the like of which people are not deceived (i.e., gross disparity), because the suspicion (tuhmah) is realized in it; perhaps he bought it for himself, and when it did not suit him, he attributed it to someone else as has been mentioned. Even if he was an agent for the purchase of a specific item, they said it will be executed upon the principal because he does not own the purchase for himself. Similarly, the agent for marriage, when he marries a woman to his principal with more than her proper dower (mahr mithl), it is permissible according to him (Imam Abu Hanifa) because attribution to the principal in the contract is essential, so this suspicion is not realized. It is not the same for the agent for purchase because he concludes the contract absolutely.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on the scope of an agent authorized to purchase (wakil bi al-shira'). The agent may buy at the market value (mithl al-qeema) or with a slight increase that people ordinarily tolerate (ghaban yasir). However, the agent may not buy at a price with gross disparity (ghaban fahish) because there is a strong suspicion (tuhmah) that the agent is acting for his own benefit: he might buy the item for himself, and if it does not suit him, he attributes it to the principal. The text then mentions an exception: if the agent is authorized to purchase a specific item (shay' mu'ayan), the purchase is binding on the principal even if the price is high, because the agent cannot purchase that specific item for himself (since it is designated for the principal). Similarly, an agent for marriage (wakil bi al-nikah) can give more than the proper dower because the contract must be explicitly attributed to the principal, leaving no room for suspicion of the agent acting for himself. The ruling is based on the principle of preventing conflict of interest. The key distinction is that in an absolute purchase agency, the agent has discretion over what to buy, creating a risk of self-dealing when the price is excessive, whereas with a specific item or marriage agency, the agent's role is merely to execute the transaction, and there is no risk of the agent taking the benefit for himself.

Key Terms
غبن یسیر (ghaban yasīr): Slight disparity in price that people ordinarily tolerate in transactions; it is permissible for an agent to buy with such disparity.
تہمت (tuhmah): Suspicion or presumption of wrongdoing; in this context, the suspicion that the agent may be acting for his own benefit rather than the principal's.
وکیل بالنکاح (wakil bi al-nikāḥ): Agent for marriage; one authorized to contract a marriage on behalf of the principal. The ruling here is that such an agent may agree to a dower higher than the proper dower without suspicion, because the contract explicitly names the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is it permissible for an agent for marriage (wakil bi al-nikah) to give more than the proper dower, but not permissible for an agent for purchase to pay a grossly inflated price?
A) Because the agent for marriage is not subject to suspicion (tuhmah) since the contract must be attributed to the principal, whereas the agent for purchase can buy for himself
B) Because the agent for marriage has more authority than the agent for purchase
C) Because the proper dower is not defined, unlike market price
D) Because the agent for purchase has a duty to get the best deal

Key Takeaway
An agent for purchase is restricted to market value or slight disparity; gross disparity raises suspicion of self-dealing and is invalid unless the principal ratifies.

Guardian's Prohibition from Selling Minor's Property with Ghaban Fahish
Explaining why father/guardian cannot sell with ghaban fahish

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a father or guardian is prohibited from selling a minor's property with ghaban fahish by identifying the conditional nature of wilayat nazari.

Core Idea
Guardianship over a minor is conditional on care; selling at a gross loss violates that condition.

This passage addresses a subtle question: if a sale with gross undervalue is technically a valid contract, why can't a guardian execute it? The answer lies in the nature of their authority—it is not absolute but conditioned on acting in the minor's best interest. We will unpack the concept of wilayat nazari and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the implicit objection
The author anticipates a question: if a sale with ghaban fahish is still a valid contract, why can't a guardian do it? Identify this dialectical context.
The objection is based on the validity of the sale itself, but the response distinguishes between contract validity and the guardian's authority.
2
State the ruling and its basis
The father/guardian is prohibited from selling with ghaban fahish because his guardianship (wilayah) is conditional on care (wilayat nazari).
The ruling is derived from the purpose of guardianship, not from the contract's essential elements.
3
Identify the condition of wilayat nazari
The guardian must act with shafaqah (kindness) and seek benefit for the minor. Selling at a gross loss contradicts this condition.
The condition is inherent in the definition of this type of guardianship; it is not an external requirement.
4
Understand the legal consequence
Since the condition is not met, the guardian lacks the authority (wilayah) entirely for that transaction. The sale is not merely invalid but beyond his power.
This implies the sale is not enforceable, and the guardian may be liable.
5
Appreciate the rational proof
The ruling is derived from the purpose of guardianship: to protect, not harm. This is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
The proof is not a text but a logical necessity based on the objective of wilayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير ان الاب والوصى ... الخ سے سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع اگر من کل وجہ بیج ہے تو باپ اور وصی کو صغیر کا مال غبن فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنے کا اختیار ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ ان کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صغیر پر باپ اور وصی کی ولایت نظری ہے۔ یعنی صغیر پر ولایت حاصل ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ ولی صفیہ پر شفقت کرے اور اسکے حق میں خیر اندیش ہو مگر غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیع کرنے میں باپ اور وصی کی طرف سے چونکہ صغیر کے حق میں کوئی شفقت کا مظاہر ہ نہیں ہوا۔ اسلئے باپ اور وصی کو صغیر کا مال غبن فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کرنے کی قطعا ولایت حاصل نہ ہو گی۔
Except that the father and guardian... this is the answer to an implied question. The question is: If selling with ghaban fahish is a sale from every aspect, then the father and guardian should have the authority to sell the minor's property with ghaban fahish, while they do not have this authority. The answer: The guardianship of the father and guardian over the minor is supervisory. That is, the condition for guardianship over the minor is that the guardian shows kindness and seeks good for him. But in selling with ghaban fahish, since there is no manifestation of kindness towards the minor from the father and guardian, therefore the father and guardian absolutely do not have the authority to sell the minor's property with ghaban fahish.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage addresses a question about why a father or guardian cannot sell a minor's property at a gross undervalue (ghaban fahish) even though such a sale is technically a valid sale. The answer is that their guardianship (wilayah) is conditional upon care and benefit (shafaqah) for the minor. Since selling at a gross loss contradicts this condition, they lack the authority to do so. This is a ruling based on rational reasoning (dalil aqli) that the purpose of guardianship is protection, not harm.

Key Terms
ولایت نظری (wilayah nazari): Guardianship that is conditional upon the guardian acting with care and seeking benefit for the ward.
غبن فاحش (ghaban fahish): A gross disparity in price that people would not normally accept; here defined as undermining care.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A guardian's authority to sell a minor's property is not absolute; it is conditioned on the duty to act with care and avoid gross exploitation.

Definition of Ghaban Fahish and Yasir in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining ghaban fahish and yasir with their amounts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of ghaban fahish and ghaban yasir, and list the specific dirham amounts for goods, animals, and land.

Core Idea
Ghaban fahish exceeds expert tolerance; ghaban yasir does not. The Hanafi school specifies amounts per trade frequency.

This lesson clarifies the key terms ghaban fahish and ghaban yasir as used in Hanafi agency sales. Understanding these definitions is crucial because they determine whether the sale is binding on the principal or the agent. We will also learn the specific dirham thresholds set by the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general definition of ghaban fahish and yasir
From the text, ghaban fahish is loss that expert valuers would not overlook (la yadkhulu tahta taqwim al-muqawwimin), while ghaban yasir is the opposite.
The definition uses the concept of 'taqwim al-muqawwimin' (valuation by experts).
2
List the specific amounts mentioned in the text
For goods: a ten-dirham item sold at ten and a half (loss 0.5 dirham). For animals: a ten-dirham animal at eleven (loss 1 dirham). For land: ten dirhams' worth at twelve (loss 2 dirhams).
These amounts are relative to a base of ten dirhams, the nisab for theft.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Quduri's apparent view considered these amounts as ghaban fahish. However, the majority (Fath al-Qadir, al-Nihayah) consider them as ghaban yasir. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
The ikhtilaf is about designation, not the amounts themselves.
4
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
If the loss is within these amounts (ghaban yasir), the sale is binding on the principal. If it exceeds (ghaban fahish), the sale is binding on the agent.
The contract remains valid; only the binding party changes.

Source Text
