دلیل: اس کی دلیل کہ مذکورہ مقدار غبن یسیر اور اس سے زائد غبن فاحش ہے یہ ہے کہ غبن اس وقت زیادہ ہوتا ہے جب آدمی کو تجربہ کم ہو اور جب تجربہ زیادہ ہو غبن کم ہوتا ہے اور تجربہ کی قلت اور کثرت تصرف کی قلت اور کثرت سے ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی تصرف اور وقوع تجارت کی زیادتی سے تجربہ زیادہ ہوگا اور تصرف اور وقوع تجارت کی کمی سے تجربہ کم ہوگا اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ سامان میں تجارت کا وقوع زیادہ ہوتا ہے اور زمین وغیرہ غیر منقول جائداد میں تجارت کا وقوع کم ہوتا ہے اور جانوروں میں تجارت کا وقوع اوسط درجہ کا ہوتا ہے۔ پھر چونکہ دس درہم ایسا نصاب ہے جس کے سرقہ سے قطع ید ہو جاتا ہے اسلئے غبن یسیر کی تفسیر میں دس درہم کو اصل قرار دیا گیا ہے اور ایک درہم ایسا مال ہے جس کی وجہ سے انسان کو قید خانہ میں ڈال دیا جاتا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ تنگی اور بل [?] کے مواقع تجارت میں ایک درہم کے ساتھ چشم پوشی نہیں کی جاتی ہے۔ یعنی بائع ثمن ٹھہر جانے کے بعد ایک درہم چھوڑنے کا روادار نہیں ہوتا ہے اور نہ ہی مشتری ایک درہم زائد دینے کا روادار ہوتا ہے۔ بہرحال جب ایسا ہے تو سامان جس میں تجارت کا وقوع کثیر ہے اس میں ایک درہم کو غبن یسیر نہیں سمجھا جائے گا۔ ہاں نصف درہم چونکہ اس درجہ اہم نہیں ہے اسلئے سامان کی تجارت میں نصف درہم غبن یسیر شمار ہوگا اور جانوروں کی تجارت چونکہ سامان کی تجارت کے وقوع سے کم ہے اسلئے جانوروں کی تجارت میں نصف درہم کا دو چند یعنی ایک درہم غبن یسیر شمار ہوگا اور زمین وغیرہ کی تجارت کا وقوع چونکہ جانوروں کی تجارت کے وقوع سے بھی کم ہے اسلئے زمین کی تجارت میں ایک درہم کا دو چند یعنی دو درہم غبن یسیر شمار ہوں گے۔
Translation: And the loss that people do not bear is that which does not fall within the estimation of the valuers. And it was said: in goods, a ten-dirham item (sold) at ten and a half; in animals, a ten-dirham animal at eleven; and in land etc. immovable property, ten at twelve. Because the occurrence of transactions is high in the first, low in the last, and medium in the middle, and the increase of ghaban (loss) is due to the scarcity of transactions. Explanation: The author of Quduri interpreted ghaban fahish from 'la yataghaban al-nasu fihi' (that over which people do not overlook loss) and defined ghaban fahish as a loss that does not enter the estimation of trade experts, i.e., no person among those who own trade would estimate that amount as compensation. In any case, when 'la yataghaban al-nasu fihi' is ghaban fahish, then its opposite 'ma yataghaban al-nasu fihi' is ghaban yasir. And when ghaban fahish is defined as 'ma la yadkhulu tahta taqwimi al-muqawwimin', then ghaban yasir is defined as 'ma yadkhulu tahta taqwimi al-muqawwimin', i.e., a loss that enters the estimation of trade experts, and that is ghaban yasir. The apparent statement of Imam Quduri 'wa qila fi al-urud 'ashara niṣf' etc. indicates that this is an interpretation of ghaban fahish: in goods, ghaban fahish is that a ten-dirham item is (sold) at ten and a half dirhams; in animals, ghaban fahish is that a ten-dirham animal is at eleven dirhams; and in immovable property like land and houses, ghaban fahish is that a ten-dirham land is at twelve dirhams. However, the author of Fath al-Qadir said that in my view the truth is that this is an interpretation of ghaban yasir, because it matches the statement narrated by the majority of jurists and most of the mashayikh. And the author of al-Nihayah also wrote this. So if the ghaban matches the mentioned amount, it is called ghaban yasir, and the purchase contract is binding and effective on the principal; if it exceeds this amount, it is called ghaban fahish, and the purchase contract is binding and effective on the agent.
Proof: The proof that the mentioned amount is ghaban yasir and beyond it is ghaban fahish is that ghaban is greater when a person has little experience, and when experience is great, ghaban is little, and the scarcity and abundance of experience come from scarcity and abundance of transactions. That is, the increase of transactions and occurrence of trade will increase experience, and the decrease of transactions and occurrence of trade will decrease experience. And it is obvious that trade occurs frequently in goods, less frequently in land and other immovable property, and in animals its occurrence is of medium level. Then, since ten dirhams is a nisab for which the hand is cut off for theft, ten dirhams was taken as the basis in interpreting ghaban yasir. And one dirham is property for which a person is imprisoned. For this reason, in the context of hardship and property? (?) in trade, one dirham is not overlooked. That is, the seller, after the price is fixed, is not willing to forgo one dirham, nor is the buyer willing to pay one dirham extra. In any case, when this is so, then in goods, where trade occurrence is abundant, one dirham will not be considered ghaban yasir. Yes, half a dirham, since it is not of such importance, will be considered ghaban yasir in goods trade. And in animal trade, since it is less than the occurrence of goods trade, double of half a dirham, i.e., one dirham, will be considered ghaban yasir. And in land etc. trade, since its occurrence is even less than animal trade, double of one dirham, i.e., two dirhams, will be considered ghaban yasir.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on ghaban (loss/deception) in sales by an agent. It begins by defining ghaban fahish (excessive loss) as a loss that expert valuers would not overlook, and ghaban yasir (minor loss) as a loss they would overlook. The text then presents two interpretations: the apparent view of Imam Quduri (in the matn) that the stated amounts (10.5 for goods, 11 for animals, 12 for land) define ghaban fahish; but the correct view according to Fath al-Qadir and al-Nihayah is that these amounts define ghaban yasir. The practical effect: if the loss is within these amounts (ghaban yasir), the sale is binding on the principal (muwakkil); if it exceeds (ghaban fahish), the sale is binding on the agent (wakil). The text then provides a rational proof: the amount of tolerable loss varies with the frequency of trade transactions. Goods are traded most frequently, so the tolerable loss is smallest (half dirham). Animals are traded less, so the tolerable loss is one dirham. Land is traded least, so the tolerable loss is two dirhams. The basis of ten dirhams is taken because it is the nisab for theft, and one dirham is significant enough to cause imprisonment. This shows the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from custom and rational analysis.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghaban fahish): Loss that expert valuers would not overlook; exceeding the amounts specified (for goods: half dirham per ten; for animals: one dirham per ten; for land: two dirhams per ten).
غبن یسیر (ghaban yasir): Loss that expert valuers would overlook; the amounts within the specified limits.
تقویم المقومین (taqwim al-muqawwimin): The estimation made by professional valuers or experts in trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the amount of ghaban yasir for the sale of land (immovable property) per ten dirhams?
A) Half a dirham
B) One dirham
C) Two dirhams
D) Three dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines ghaban yasir by fixed dirham amounts per ten dirhams based on trade frequency; losses within these amounts bind the principal, while excess binds the agent.

The Rational Proof for Ghaban Amounts
Rational proof for ghaban amounts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rational evidence (dalil aqli) used by Hanafi scholars to determine the specific amounts of ghaban yasir for goods, animals, and land.

Core Idea
The frequency of trade determines tolerance: more trade means smaller acceptable loss.

This lesson examines the rational proof behind the specific thresholds for ghaban yasir. The Hanafi scholars derived these amounts not from a scriptural text but from rational observation of trade practices. Understanding this proof helps you appreciate how custom and experience inform legal rulings in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of the proof
The proof is a rational (aqlī) argument linking the amount of tolerable loss to the frequency of transactions in a given property type.
This is not based on Quran or hadith but on common practice and experience.
2
Trace the relationship between experience and loss tolerance
The proof states that when transactions are frequent, traders gain experience and tolerate smaller losses. When transactions are rare, traders are less experienced and tolerate larger losses.
This inverse relationship is the core of the proof.
3
Apply to the three property types
Goods are traded most frequently, so experience is highest and tolerable loss is smallest (0.5 dirham per ten). Animals are traded less, so tolerable loss is medium (1 dirham per ten). Land is traded least, so tolerable loss is largest (2 dirhams per ten).
The amounts increase as frequency decreases.
4
Note the basis of ten dirhams
The base of ten dirhams is chosen because it is the nisab for theft (had penalty). One dirham is the minimum amount for which imprisonment is imposed, showing its significance.
Thus the proof integrates established legal standards (had, ta'zir) with custom.

ترجمہ اور وہ خسارہ جس کو لوگ نہیں اٹھاتے ہیں وہ ہے جو اندازہ لگانے والوں کے اندازے کے تحت داخل نہ ہو۔ اور کہا گیا کہ سامان میں دس کی چیز ساڑھے دس میں ہو اور جانوروں میں دس کا جانور گیارہ کا ہو اور زمین وغیرہ غیر منقول جائداد میں دس کے بارہ ہوں۔ کیونکہ تصرف کا وجود اول میں زیادہ ہے اور اخیر میں کم ہے اور اوسط میں درمیانی ہے اور غبن کی زیادتی قلت تصرف کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح: صاحب قدری نے لَا يَتَغَابَنُ النَّاسُ فِيهِ سے غبن فاحش کو تعبیر کیا ہے اور غبن فاحش کی تعریف کی ہے کہ غبن فاحش ایسے خسارہ کا نام ہے جو ماہرین تجارت کے اندازے میں داخل نہ ہو یعنی جو لوگ تجارت کے مالک ہیں ان میں سے کوئی شخص اس قدر مال کے عوض اندازہ نہ کرے۔ بہرحال جب لَا يَتَغَابَنُ النَّاسُ فِيهِ غبن فاحش ہے تو اس کا مقابل مَا يَتَغَابَنُ النَّاسُ فِيهِ غبن یسیر ہو گا اور جب غبن فاحش کی تعریف مَا لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ تَقْوِيمِ الْمُقَوِّمِينَ ہے تو غبن یسیر کی تعریف مَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ تَقْوِيمِ الْمُقَوِّمِينَ ہوگی۔ یعنی ایسا خسارہ جو ماہرین تجارت کے اندازے میں نہ آئے اور وہ غبن یسیر ہے۔ مصنف قدوری کا ظاہر کلام و قيل في العروض دہ نیم الخ اس پر دال ہے کہ یہ غبن فاحش کی تفسیر ہے یعنی سامان میں غبن فاحش یہ ہے کہ دس درہم کی چیز ساڑھے دس درہم میں ہو، جانوروں میں غبن فاحش یہ ہے کہ دس درہم کا جانور گیارہ درہم میں ہو، اور غیر منقولہ جائداد زمین، مکان وغیرہ میں غبن فاحش یہ ہے کہ دس درہم کی زمین بارہ درہم میں ہو۔ مگر صاحب فتح القدیر نے کہا کہ میرے نزدیک حق یہ ہے کہ یہ غبن یسیر کی تفسیر ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بات جمہور فقہاء اور عامتہ المشائخ کے ذکر کردہ بیان کے مطابق ہے۔ اور یہی صاحب نہایہ نے تحریر فرمایا ہے۔ پس غبن اگر مذکورہ مقدار کے مطابق ہو تو وہ غبن یسیر کہلائے گا اور عقد شراء موکل پر لازم اور نافذ ہوگا اور اگر اس مقدار سے زائد ہو تو وہ غبن فاحش کہلائے گا اور عقد شراء وکیل پر لازم اور نافذ ہوگا۔
دلیل: اس کی دلیل کہ مذکورہ مقدار غبن یسیر اور اس سے زائد غبن فاحش ہے یہ ہے کہ غبن اس وقت زیادہ ہوتا ہے جب آدمی کو تجربہ کم ہو اور جب تجربہ زیادہ ہو غبن کم ہوتا ہے اور تجربہ کی قلت اور کثرت تصرف کی قلت اور کثرت سے ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی تصرف اور وقوع تجارت کی زیادتی سے تجربہ زیادہ ہوگا اور تصرف اور وقوع تجارت کی کمی سے تجربہ کم ہوگا اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ سامان میں تجارت کا وقوع زیادہ ہوتا ہے اور زمین وغیرہ غیر منقول جائداد میں تجارت کا وقوع کم ہوتا ہے اور جانوروں میں تجارت کا وقوع اوسط درجہ کا ہوتا ہے۔ پھر چونکہ دس درہم ایسا نصاب ہے جس کے سرقہ سے قطع ید ہو جاتا ہے اسلئے غبن یسیر کی تفسیر میں دس درہم کو اصل قرار دیا گیا ہے اور ایک درہم ایسا مال ہے جس کی وجہ سے انسان کو قید خانہ میں ڈال دیا جاتا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ تنگی اور بل [?] کے مواقع تجارت میں ایک درہم کے ساتھ چشم پوشی نہیں کی جاتی ہے۔ یعنی بائع ثمن ٹھہر جانے کے بعد ایک درہم چھوڑنے کا روادار نہیں ہوتا ہے اور نہ ہی مشتری ایک درہم زائد دینے کا روادار ہوتا ہے۔ بہرحال جب ایسا ہے تو سامان جس میں تجارت کا وقوع کثیر ہے اس میں ایک درہم کو غبن یسیر نہیں سمجھا جائے گا۔ ہاں نصف درہم چونکہ اس درجہ اہم نہیں ہے اسلئے سامان کی تجارت میں نصف درہم غبن یسیر شمار ہوگا اور جانوروں کی تجارت چونکہ سامان کی تجارت کے وقوع سے کم ہے اسلئے جانوروں کی تجارت میں نصف درہم کا دو چند یعنی ایک درہم غبن یسیر شمار ہوگا اور زمین وغیرہ کی تجارت کا وقوع چونکہ جانوروں کی تجارت کے وقوع سے بھی کم ہے اسلئے زمین کی تجارت میں ایک درہم کا دو چند یعنی دو درہم غبن یسیر شمار ہوں گے۔
Translation: And the loss that people do not bear is that which does not fall within the estimation of the valuers. And it was said: in goods, a ten-dirham item (sold) at ten and a half; in animals, a ten-dirham animal at eleven; and in land etc. immovable property, ten at twelve. Because the occurrence of transactions is high in the first, low in the last, and medium in the middle, and the increase of ghaban (loss) is due to the scarcity of transactions. Explanation: The author of Quduri interpreted ghaban fahish from 'la yataghaban al-nasu fihi' (that over which people do not overlook loss) and defined ghaban fahish as a loss that does not enter the estimation of trade experts, i.e., no person among those who own trade would estimate that amount as compensation. In any case, when 'la yataghaban al-nasu fihi' is ghaban fahish, then its opposite 'ma yataghaban al-nasu fihi' is ghaban yasir. And when ghaban fahish is defined as 'ma la yadkhulu tahta taqwimi al-muqawwimin', then ghaban yasir is defined as 'ma yadkhulu tahta taqwimi al-muqawwimin', i.e., a loss that enters the estimation of trade experts, and that is ghaban yasir. The apparent statement of Imam Quduri 'wa qila fi al-urud 'ashara niṣf' etc. indicates that this is an interpretation of ghaban fahish: in goods, ghaban fahish is that a ten-dirham item is (sold) at ten and a half dirhams; in animals, ghaban fahish is that a ten-dirham animal is at eleven dirhams; and in immovable property like land and houses, ghaban fahish is that a ten-dirham land is at twelve dirhams. However, the author of Fath al-Qadir said that in my view the truth is that this is an interpretation of ghaban yasir, because it matches the statement narrated by the majority of jurists and most of the mashayikh. And the author of al-Nihayah also wrote this. So if the ghaban matches the mentioned amount, it is called ghaban yasir, and the purchase contract is binding and effective on the principal; if it exceeds this amount, it is called ghaban fahish, and the purchase contract is binding and effective on the agent.
Proof: The proof that the mentioned amount is ghaban yasir and beyond it is ghaban fahish is that ghaban is greater when a person has little experience, and when experience is great, ghaban is little, and the scarcity and abundance of experience come from scarcity and abundance of transactions. That is, the increase of transactions and occurrence of trade will increase experience, and the decrease of transactions and occurrence of trade will decrease experience. And it is obvious that trade occurs frequently in goods, less frequently in land and other immovable property, and in animals its occurrence is of medium level. Then, since ten dirhams is a nisab for which the hand is cut off for theft, ten dirhams was taken as the basis in interpreting ghaban yasir. And one dirham is property for which a person is imprisoned. For this reason, in the context of hardship and property? (?) in trade, one dirham is not overlooked. That is, the seller, after the price is fixed, is not willing to forgo one dirham, nor is the buyer willing to pay one dirham extra. In any case, when this is so, then in goods, where trade occurrence is abundant, one dirham will not be considered ghaban yasir. Yes, half a dirham, since it is not of such importance, will be considered ghaban yasir in goods trade. And in animal trade, since it is less than the occurrence of goods trade, double of half a dirham, i.e., one dirham, will be considered ghaban yasir. And in land etc. trade, since its occurrence is even less than animal trade, double of one dirham, i.e., two dirhams, will be considered ghaban yasir.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on ghaban (loss/deception) in sales by an agent. It begins by defining ghaban fahish (excessive loss) as a loss that expert valuers would not overlook, and ghaban yasir (minor loss) as a loss they would overlook. The text then presents two interpretations: the apparent view of Imam Quduri (in the matn) that the stated amounts (10.5 for goods, 11 for animals, 12 for land) define ghaban fahish; but the correct view according to Fath al-Qadir and al-Nihayah is that these amounts define ghaban yasir. The practical effect: if the loss is within these amounts (ghaban yasir), the sale is binding on the principal (muwakkil); if it exceeds (ghaban fahish), the sale is binding on the agent (wakil). The text then provides a rational proof: the amount of tolerable loss varies with the frequency of trade transactions. Goods are traded most frequently, so the tolerable loss is smallest (half dirham). Animals are traded less, so the tolerable loss is one dirham. Land is traded least, so the tolerable loss is two dirhams. The basis of ten dirhams is taken because it is the nisab for theft, and one dirham is significant enough to cause imprisonment. This shows the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from custom and rational analysis.

Key Terms
دلیل عقلی (dalil aqli): A rational proof based on logical reasoning and empirical observation, not on scriptural texts.
تصرف (tasarruf): Transaction or occurrence of trade; frequency of dealings in a particular type of property.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount that triggers a legal ruling, here the threshold for theft (hand amputation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rational proof, why is the tolerable loss (ghaban yasir) for land greater than for goods?
A) Because land is more expensive
B) Because land is less frequently traded, so traders have less experience and tolerate larger losses
C) Because land is immovable and harder to valuate
D) Because the nisab for theft is higher for land

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rational proof for ghaban amounts links transaction frequency to tolerance: more frequent trade means smaller acceptable loss, rooted in the inverse relationship between experience and ghaban.

Agent Selling Half a Slave: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial sale by agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on an agent selling half a slave for half the price, and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits an agent to sell half a slave for half the price because it is more beneficial; the Sahibayn forbid it due to customary limits and harm.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the authority of an agent to sell part of a slave. Imam Abu Hanifa held that selling half for half is permissible, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, deemed it invalid. The disagreement hinges on whether the absolute agency covers non-customary sales and on the concept of detriment to the principal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the central question: Is it permissible for an agent, authorized to sell a slave, to sell half the slave for half the price? Then identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa says yes, Sahibayn say no.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's argument
Examine the a fortiori (awla) reasoning: Selling whole slave for half price is permissible (according to Abu Hanifa) and causes greater loss. Since selling half for half is less harmful, it is a fortiori permissible.
The key is comparing degrees of benefit and harm.
3
Examine the objection and response
The objection is that selling half creates co-ownership (ayb al-shirkah), which harms the principal. The response: the harm is greater in the whole-for-half sale, so the lesser harm is permissible.
This is a classic talil (reasoning) based on weighing harms.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's arguments
Sahibayn give two proofs: 1) Absolute agency (tawkil mutlaq) is interpreted according to custom (urf), and selling half is not customary. 2) Selling half causes harm through co-ownership, and the agent cannot cause harm.
They also reject the whole-for-half sale due to ghaban fahish.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if following Abu Hanifa, the sale is valid and binding; if following Sahibayn, it is invalid and the agent is liable for compensation.
The text does not give a tarjih, but the dispute is recorded in zahir al-riwayah.

کیونکہ آدھے غلام کو آدھے ثمن کے عوض بیچنے اور آدھے غلام کو روک لینے میں موکل کا زیادہ نفع ہے۔ یہ نسبت اس کے کہ پورے غلام کو آدھے ثمن کے عوض فروخت کیا جائے۔ اسلئے کہ پہلی صورت میں مؤکل کو نصف ثمن بھی حاصل ہوگا اور آدھا غلام بھی اسکے پاس رہے گا اور دوسری صورت میں نصف ثمن تو حاصل ہو جاتا ہے مگر غلام کا کوئی حصہ اس کے پاس باقی نہیں رہتا۔ لہذا پہلی صورت مؤکل کیلئے زیادہ نفع بخش ہوگی اور دوسری صورت غیر نفع ہوگی۔ پس جب غیر انفع صورت (پورے غلام کو نصف ثمن کے عوض) میں بیع جائز ہے تو انفع صورت (نصف غلام کو نصف ثمن کے عوض) میں بیع بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگی۔

لیکن اگر آپ یہ اعتراض کریں کہ پورے غلام کو نصف ثمن کے عوض بیچنا اسلئے جائز ہے کہ یہ بیع عیب شرکت کو متضمن نہیں ہے اور نصف غلام کو نصف ثمن کے عوض بیچنا اسلئے ناجائز ہے کہ اس میں عیب شرکت ہے یعنی غلام میں موکل اور مشتری دونوں شریک ہو جائیں گے۔ حالانکہ شرکت عیب ہے پس نصف غلام کو نصف ثمن کے عوض بیچنے میں چونکہ عیب شرکت ہے اسلئے یہ بیع وکیل کی طرف سے اپنے موکل کی مخالفت الی الشر ہے اور وکیل کیلئے اپنے مؤکل کی مخالفت الی الشر چونکہ جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے وکیل کی یہ بیع جائز نہ ہوگی اور اس کا نفاذ مؤکل پر نہ ہوگا۔ اور پورے غلام کو نصف ثمن کے عوض بیچنے میں چونکہ عیب شرکت نہیں پایا جاتا اسلئے اس بیع میں مؤکل کی مخالفت الی الشر بھی لازم نہ آئے گی اور جب اس بیع میں موکل کی مخالفت الی الشر لازم نہیں آتی تو یہ بیع بھی جائز ہوگی اور موکل پر نافذ ہوگی۔ ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آدھے غلام کو آدھے ثمن کے عوض فروخت کرنے میں اگرچہ عیب شرکت لازم آتا ہے اور پورے غلام کو آدھے ثمن کے عوض فروخت کرنے میں عیب شرکت لازم نہیں ہے مگر پورے غلام کو نصف ثمن کے عوض بیچنے میں موکل کا نقصان زیادہ ہے اور آدھے غلام کو آدھے ثمن کے عوض بیچنا یعنی زیادہ نقصان برداشت کرنا جائز ہے تو نصف غلام کو نصف ثمن کے عوض بیچنا یعنی کم نقصان برداشت کرنا بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگا۔

یہ خیال رہے کہ پورے غلام کو آدھے ثمن کے عوض بیچنا صرف امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اس وجہ سے یجوز عندہ کہا گیا ہے ورنہ صاحبین کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے کیونکہ پورے غلام کو نصف ثمن کے عوض بیچنے میں غبن فاحش ہے اور غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیچنا صاحبین کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔

صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مؤکل کا اپنے غلام کو فروخت کرنے کا وکیل کرنا مطلق ہے جیسا کہ امام صاحب کی دلیل میں گذرا ہے۔ ان اللفظ مطلق اور مطلق متعارف کی طرف راجح ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی مطلق سے متعارف مراد ہوتا ہے اور آدھے غلام کو فروخت کرنا غیر متعارف ہے۔ بہر حال جب توکیل بیع العبد مطلق ہے اور مطلق سے متعارف مراد ہوتا ہے اور آدھے غلام کو فروخت کرنا غیر متعارف ہے تو یہ توکیل آدھے غلام کے فروخت کرنے کو شامل نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب یہ توکیل آدھے غلام کو فروخت کرنے کو شامل نہیں ہے تو وکیل کا آدھے غلام کو فروخت کرنا مؤکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کرنا ہوگا اور وکیل کا اپنے مؤکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کرنا چونکہ جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے وکیل کا آدھے غلام کو فروخت کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔

دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ آدھا غلام فروخت کرنے کی صورت میں مؤکل اور مشتری چونکہ دونوں غلام میں شریک ہو جائیں گے اور شرکت عیب ہے اسلئے اس شرکت کی وجہ سے مؤکل کو ضرر ہوگا اور وکیل ایسا تصرف کرنے کا ہرگز مجاز نہیں ہوتا جس میں موکل کو ضرر لاحق ہوتا ہو۔ پس جب اس تصرف میں یعنی آدھا غلام فروخت کرنے میں موکل کو ضرر لاحق ہوتا ہے تو وکیل آدھا غلام فروخت کرنے کا
Translation: Because selling half a slave for half the price and retaining half the slave brings more profit to the principal. This is in comparison to selling the whole slave for half the price. Because in the first case, the principal gets half the price and also keeps half the slave; in the second case, he gets half the price but no part of the slave remains with him. Therefore, the first case is more beneficial for the principal, and the second case is less beneficial. So when the less beneficial case (selling the whole slave for half the price) is permissible, then the more beneficial case (selling half the slave for half the price) is permissible a fortiori.

But if you object that selling the whole slave for half the price is permissible because it does not entail the defect of co-ownership, while selling half the slave for half the price is impermissible because it entails the defect of co-ownership, i.e., the principal and the buyer become partners in the slave, and co-ownership is a defect. So since selling half the slave for half the price involves the defect of co-ownership, this sale is an opposition detrimental to the principal on the part of the agent, and since an agent is not permitted to oppose his principal in a detrimental way, this sale is not permissible and will not be binding on the principal. And in selling the whole slave for half the price, since the defect of co-ownership does not exist, this sale does not entail detrimental opposition to the principal, and therefore this sale is permissible and binding on the principal.

Our response is that although selling half a slave for half the price entails the defect of co-ownership, and selling the whole slave for half the price does not entail co-ownership, but selling the whole slave for half the price involves a greater loss to the principal. And bearing a greater loss (by selling half the slave for half the price) is permissible, so bearing a lesser loss (by selling half the slave for half the price) is permissible a fortiori.

Note that selling the whole slave for half the price is permissible only according to Imam Abu Hanifa. For this reason, it is said 'yajuzu 'indahu'. Otherwise, according to the Sahibayn, it is impermissible, because selling the whole slave for half the price involves ghaban fahish, and selling with ghaban fahish is impermissible according to the Sahibayn, as has passed earlier.

The proof of the Sahibayn is that the principal's appointment of the agent to sell the slave is absolute (mutlaq), and an absolute term leans towards the customary meaning. That is, from the absolute, the customary meaning is intended, and selling half a slave is not customary. Therefore, when the appointment to sell the slave is absolute, and absolute intends the customary, and selling half a slave is not customary, then this appointment does not cover selling half the slave. And since the appointment does not cover selling half the slave, the agent's selling half the slave would be opposition to the principal's command, and since an agent's opposition to his principal's command is not permissible, the agent's selling half the slave is also not permissible.

The second proof is that in the case of selling half a slave, the principal and the buyer both become partners in the slave, and partnership is a defect, so due to this partnership, the principal suffers harm. And an agent is never authorized to perform an action that causes harm to the principal. So when this action, i.e., selling half the slave, causes harm to the principal, the agent (selling half the slave is not permissible).
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an agent selling part of a slave. The issue: is it permissible for an agent authorized to sell a slave to sell half the slave for half the price? Imam Abu Hanifa permits it, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) forbid it. The text first gives Abu Hanifa's argument: selling half the slave for half the price is more beneficial than selling the whole for half the price because the principal retains half the slave. Since the latter is permissible, the former is a fortiori. An objection is raised: selling half the slave creates co-ownership (defect), which is harmful, so it is not permissible. The response: the greater harm in selling the whole for half the price outweighs the co-ownership defect; thus the lesser harm is permissible. Then the text notes that even selling the whole for half is only allowed by Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn forbid it due to ghaban fahish. Finally, the Sahibayn present two proofs: (1) the agency is absolute and does not cover non-customary acts like selling half; (2) selling half causes detriment to the principal through co-ownership. The text cuts off during the second proof, but the position is clear.

Key Terms
عیب شرکت (ayb al-shirkah): The defect of co-ownership, meaning that the sold item becomes jointly owned by the seller (or principal) and buyer, which is considered disadvantageous.
توکیل مطلق (tawkil mutlaq): An absolute agency appointment without specifying conditions or limitations.
متعارف (muta'arif): Customary or conventionally known; what people commonly do.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa in this passage, selling half a slave for half the price is permissible because:
A) The agent has absolute authority to sell any part
B) It is more beneficial for the principal than selling the whole for half
C) Co-ownership is not a defect
D) The Sahibayn also permit it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a legitimate disagreement on whether an agent can sell part of a slave, reflecting different prioritizations of benefit, harm, and custom.

The Suspended Purchase: Agent Buying Half a Slave
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the suspension of an agent's partial purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent buying half a slave, explain why it is suspended, and distinguish it from the sale of half a slave using the two key arguments (tuhma and property encounter).

Core Idea
An agent buying half a slave is suspended until the whole is bought; selling half is immediately valid—the difference lies in tuhma and the nature of the command.

In Hanafi agency, the scope of an agent's authority depends on the nature of the transaction. When an agent is commanded to buy a slave and instead buys only half, the purchase is not immediately binding—it is suspended (mawquf). The Hidayah explains why this differs from the rule when an agent sells half a slave, which is valid outright. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the suspension and the important distinction based on tuhma and the encounter with ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the agreement
Start by stating the rule: if an agent appointed to buy a slave buys only half, the purchase is suspended. Note that Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree on this suspension.
The suspension means the purchase is not immediately binding on the principal.
2
Recognize the objection from the sale case
Understand the objection: in the earlier case of selling half a slave, the sale is valid without suspension. Why should buying be different? This is the intra-Hanafi dispute that the Hidayah addresses.
The objection is based on consistency: if selling half is valid, why not buying half?
3
Examine the first distinction: suspicion (tuhma)
In purchase, there is a suspicion that the agent might have bought the half for himself and then attributed it to the principal. To prevent self-dealing, the purchase is suspended. In sale, the agent cannot own the principal's property, so no such suspicion exists.
Tuhma is a key concept in Hanafi fiqh to protect the principal's interests.
4
Examine the second distinction: property encounter and custom (urf)
The command to sell meets the principal's own property, so it is valid and its absoluteness (itlaq) is considered, authorizing any part. The command to purchase meets another's property, so it is not inherently valid; it is only permitted by necessity. Thus, custom (urf) determines that the command is to buy the entire slave, not a part.
This second distinction relies on the Hanafi principle that urf can interpret ambiguous commands.
5
Apply the distinction to determine the practical consequence
If the agent later buys the other half before the principal rescinds, the first half becomes a means to the whole, and the purchase becomes binding. If not, the agent is liable. This differs from sale, where selling half is immediately binding.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the principal is bound or not.

Chapter of Agency. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume Ten. The accusation on what has passed and another: The command to sell encounters his property, so it is valid, and its absolute nature is considered. The command to purchase encountered the property of another, so it is not valid, and restriction and absoluteness are not considered therein. Translation: And if he appointed him as an agent to buy a slave, and the agent bought half a slave, then this purchase is suspended. Then if the agent bought the remaining slave, this purchase becomes binding on the principal, because buying one part of the slave sometimes becomes a means of executing the principal's command, such as when the slave is inherited among a group, then the agent is not in need of buying it piece by piece. So when the agent bought the remaining slave before the principal rescinded the sale, it became apparent that buying the first half was a means. Therefore it is effective on the principal, and this ruling is by agreement. And based on the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, the distinction is that in the case of purchase, suspicion (tuhma) is realized. As has passed. And the second distinction is that the command to sell meets the principal's property, so it is valid, and its absoluteness is considered. And the command to purchase met the property of another, so it is not valid, and restriction and absoluteness are not considered therein. Explanation of the case: A person appointed someone as an agent to buy a slave. The agent bought half a slave. By agreement, this purchase is suspended. That is, if the agent also buys the remaining part, the purchase is binding and effective on the principal; if he does not buy the remaining part, the purchase is not binding on the principal. The proof is that buying one part of the slave sometimes becomes a means of executing the principal's command. For example, if a slave is inherited by several people, they own the slave. Now if the agent wants to buy this slave, he must buy piece by piece from all owners. In any case, when the agent bought the remaining part before the principal rescinded the sale of the first half, it became apparent that buying the first half was a means of executing the principal's command. It has passed that in the case where selling half a slave becomes a means of executing the principal's command, the sale is effective on the principal. So in the case of purchase, when buying the first half becomes a means of executing the principal's command, this purchase is effective on the principal, because it is as if the agent bought the entire slave. The author of Hidayah said: On this matter that the purchase of the first half is suspended, Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) are all agreed. But on Imam Abu Hanifa's statement, there is an objection: Imam Abu Hanifa in the earlier issue of selling half a slave declared the sale valid without suspension. Here in the issue of purchase, he suspends the purchase of half a slave. So what is the reason for the distinction between the two? The author of Hidayah mentioned two aspects of distinction. The first distinction is that in the case of purchase, suspicion (tuhma) is realized in the agent's favor, in that the agent may have bought half the slave for himself, but when he sensed a loss, he attributed the purchase to the principal. Due to this suspicion, the purchase of half a slave is suspended, and it is said that if the agent also bought the remaining slave, then this purchase becomes effective on the principal; if not, it does not become effective. But in the case of sale, this suspicion is not realized. Therefore, selling half a slave can only be for the principal, not for the agent. Based on this distinction, in the case of sale, selling half a slave is declared valid without suspension, and in the case of purchase, buying half a slave is suspended. The second distinction is that in the case of an agent for sale, the principal's command to sell encounters his own property. That is, the principal ordered to sell something he owns. Since the principal has authority over his property, his command to sell is valid. When his command to sell is valid, the absoluteness of the command is considered. When absoluteness is considered, the agent is authorized to sell the entire slave or half the slave. When the agent is authorized to sell half, his selling half is valid. In the case of agency for purchase, the principal's command encounters the property of another. That is, the thing the principal ordered to buy is not his property but the seller's property. Ordering to buy property of another is not a valid contract; it is only permitted out of necessity. So when the command to purchase is not valid, absoluteness or restriction is not considered; rather, custom (urf) is considered. Custom is that the entire slave is bought. Therefore, ordering to buy a slave, in view of custom, is an order to buy the entire slave. When this is the case, whichever way the agent buys the entire slave (whether at once or in parts), since this purchase conforms to the principal's command, it is binding on the principal. When he buys only half, since it does not conform, it is not binding on the principal but binding on the agent.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the ruling when an agent is appointed to buy a slave but only buys half. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Imam Abu Hanifa vs. the two companions) with an explanation of the distinction between sale and purchase. The ruling: If the agent buys half a slave, the purchase is suspended (mawquf). If the agent later buys the other half before the principal rescinds, it becomes binding on the principal; otherwise, it is not. This is agreed upon by Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The objection arises: why is selling half a slave valid without suspension, but buying half is suspended? Two reasons are given: (1) In purchase, there is suspicion (tuhma) that the agent might have bought for himself and then attributed to the principal; in sale, such suspicion does not exist because the agent cannot own the principal's property. (2) In sale, the command encounters the principal's property, so the command is valid and its absoluteness (itlaq) is considered, authorizing the agent to sell any part. In purchase, the command encounters another's property, so the command is not inherently valid and is only permitted by necessity; thus, custom (urf) determines that the command is to buy the entire slave, not a part. Therefore, buying half does not fulfill the command and is not binding on the principal.

Key Terms
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion or accusation; here, the possibility that the agent acted in his own interest rather than the principal's.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a transaction that is not immediately binding but depends on a future condition (here, the purchase of the remaining half).
عرف (urf): Custom; used here to interpret the scope of the agent's authority when the command is ambiguous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hidayah, what is the reason for suspending the purchase of half a slave by an agent?
A) The agent may have bought it for himself (tuhma)
B) The command to purchase is invalid
C) Custom (urf) requires buying the whole slave
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
The key distinction is that in purchase, tuhma and the encounter with another's property lead to custom (urf) interpreting the command as for the whole, whereas in sale, the command is valid and absolute, authorizing any part.

intermediate

Authority of Agent to Take Pledge or Guarantor: Deputy vs Principal
Ruling with talil: distinguishing agent types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a debt-collection agent and a buying agent regarding their authority to take a pledge or guarantor, and determine when the agent becomes personally liable.

Core Idea
A debt-collection agent is a deputy; a buying agent is a principal — only the latter may take security.

This passage examines a critical distinction in Hanafi agency law: the scope of an agent's authority to take collateral or guarantees. It contrasts two common types of agents — one appointed to collect a debt and one appointed to sell goods — and shows that the key factor is whether the agent acts as a mere deputy (na'ib) or as a principal (asil) in the transaction. Understanding this distinction is essential for determining when an agent incurs personal liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of agency
First, recognize that the passage discusses two distinct agency scenarios: agency for debt collection (wakalah fi qabd al-dayn) and agency for sale (wakalah bil-bay').
2
Classify each agent's capacity
For the debt-collection agent, he is a deputy (na'ib) of the principal. For the buying agent, he is considered a principal (asil) in the rights of the sale.
The buying agent acts as if he were the owner in taking possession of the price.
3
Apply the capacity to taking security
Since the debt-collection agent is only a deputy, taking a pledge or guarantor exceeds his authority, making him personally liable if the security is lost or the guarantor fails. The buying agent, as principal, may take such security without exceeding authority.
The buying agent's act is attributed to himself, not as a deputy.
4
Determine the liability outcome
If the debt-collection agent takes a pledge that is destroyed, he must compensate the principal. If the buying agent does so, he is not liable.
The difference hinges on whether the agent acted within the scope of his authority.
5
Understand the underlying reasoning (ta'lil)
The buying agent has the rank of the owner; he takes possession as asil, so the principal cannot prevent him. The debt-collection agent is restricted to receiving the debt; any additional act is transgression.
This reasoning is based on the nature of the agency contract.

صورت میں بھی وکیل پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں شمن ہی کا ہلاک ہونا پایا گیا ہے اور شمن ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں وکیل پر ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر کسی نے اپنا قرضہ وصول کرنے کیلئے کسی کو وکیل کیا اور پھر وکیل نے قرضہ کے عوض قرضدار سے رہن لے لیا تو وکیل کا یہ رہن لینا اور کفیل لینا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگرم بہن وکیل کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہوگی یا کفیل اور مکشول عنہ ( قرضدار ) دونوں مفلس ہو کر مر گئے تو وکیل ضمان سے بری نہ ہو گا۔ بلکہ وکیل پر قرضہ کا ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ کیونکہ قرضہ وصول کرنے کا وکیل میرکل کا نائب ہو کر قرضہ وصول کرتا ہے تو وہ صرف موکل کا قرضہ وصول کرنے کا مجاز ہوگا کیونکہ مؤکل نے اس کو صرف قرضہ وصول کرنے کا نا نب کیا ہے اور کفیل لینے کا اور رہن لینے کا چونکہ اس کو وکیل اور نائب نہیں کیا ہے۔ اسلئے وہ قرضدار سے کفیل لینے اور زہن لینے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ اور وکیل بالمبی چونکہ حقوق بیچ میں اصیل ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے وہ مشن پر اصالتہ قبضہ کرتا ہے۔ نہ کہ نیابتہ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مؤکل اس کو شمن پر قبضہ کرنے سے روکنے کا اختیار نہیں رکھتا ہے نہیں وکیل اس صورت میں مالک کے مرتبہ میں ہوگا اور مالک اگر شمن کے عوض لے لے یا شمن کے واسطے کفیل لے لے تو جائز ہے۔ لہذا وکیل بالربیع بھی رہن لینے اور کفیل لینے کا مجاز ہوگا۔
In this case too, the agent will not be liable. Because in this case, the price itself is found to be destroyed, and when the price is destroyed, the agent is not liable for guarantee. Hence, in this case too, guarantee will not be obligatory. Contrary to this, if someone appointed an agent to collect his debt, and then the agent took a pledge from the debtor in exchange for the debt, then this taking of pledge and taking of guarantor by the agent will not be permissible. Thus, if the pledge is destroyed in the agent's possession, or if both the guarantor and the principal debtor become insolvent and die, the agent will not be absolved of liability. Rather, the agent will be liable for the debt. Because the agent for debt collection acts as a deputy of the principal in collecting the debt, so he is only authorized to collect the principal's debt, since the principal appointed him only as a deputy for collecting the debt, and not for taking a guarantor or pledge. Therefore, he will not be authorized to take a guarantor or pledge from the debtor. And the buying agent (wakil bil-bay'), since he is the principal (asil) in the rights of the sale, takes possession of the price as a principal, not as a deputy. For this reason, the principal does not have the authority to prevent him from taking possession of the price. Rather, in this case, the agent is at the rank of the owner. And if the owner takes the price or takes a guarantor for the price, it is permissible. Hence, the buying agent is also authorized to take a pledge and a guarantor.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability of an agent when he takes a pledge or guarantor beyond his authority. It distinguishes between two types of agency: (1) agency for debt collection (wakalah fi qabd al-dayn) and (2) agency for sale (wakalah bil-bay'). In the first case, the agent is merely a deputy (na'ib) of the principal; he is only authorized to receive the debt. If he takes a pledge or guarantor, he exceeds his authority, and if the pledge is destroyed or the guarantor becomes insolvent, he is personally liable for the debt. In the second case, the buying agent acts as a principal (asil) in the rights of the contract; he takes possession of the price in his own right, not as a deputy. Therefore, he may take a pledge or guarantor just as the owner himself could. The underlying reasoning (ta'lil) is that the buying agent has the authority to act as an owner, and the principal cannot prevent him from taking possession of the price, whereas the debt-collection agent's authority is limited to receiving what is owed.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): An agent appointed to act on behalf of another (muwakkil).
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; here, the agent's liability for the debt if he exceeds authority.
رہن (rahn): Pledge; a security taken for a debt.
کفیل (kafil): Guarantor; a person who guarantees payment of a debt.
اصیل (asil): Principal; the person who acts in his own right, not as a deputy.
نائب (na'ib): Deputy; someone who acts on behalf of another with limited authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An agent appointed to collect a debt takes a personal guarantor from the debtor. The guarantor later becomes insolvent. Who is liable for the debt?
A) The principal, because the guarantor was meant to secure the debt
B) The agent, because he was not authorized to take a guarantor
C) The debtor, because he provided the guarantor
D) No one, because the guarantor's insolvency is unforeseen

Key Takeaway
A debt-collection agent acts as a deputy and cannot take security without liability; a buying agent acts as a principal and may do so.

Two Agents in Matters of Opinion
Rules for joint agency and exceptions for acts not requiring opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for joint agency in Hanafi fiqh and identify its exceptions based on the need for opinion.

Core Idea
Two agents must act jointly in matters requiring discretion; mere expression allows solo action.

When a principal appoints two agents, the default rule is that both must act together unless the matter requires no personal judgment. This lesson from Al-Hidayah explains the reasoning behind this rule and lists the key exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what action is being considered (e.g., sale, khul') and the ruling: two agents must act jointly.
The ruling applies only to actions requiring opinion (ra'y).
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is that the principal consented to both opinions, so acting alone violates that consent.
The dalil is the principal's consent, not a direct textual source.
3
Trace the Objection and Response
Even if the price is specified, joint action is still beneficial because agents can increase the price or choose a better buyer.
Specification does not eliminate the need for joint opinion.
4
Identify the Exceptions
List the cases where one agent can act alone: litigation (khusumah) and acts of mere expression (ta'bir mahd) like divorcing without compensation, freeing a slave, returning a deposit, paying a debt.
Litigation is exceptional due to impracticality; mere expression requires no judgment.
5
Note the Boundary Case
If the principal says 'if you wish' or 'her affair is in your hands', it becomes a tamlik requiring joint action, analogized to joint entry.
This is not a mere expression but a delegation to opinion.

And when he appoints two agents, it is not permissible for one of them to act in that which they were both appointed without the other. And this applies to an action that requires opinion, such as sale and khul' and the like, because the principal consented to their opinion, not the opinion of one of them. And even if the countervalue is specified, specification does not prevent the use of opinion in increasing (the price) and choosing the buyer.
Section: If a person appoints two men as agents, one cannot act in the absence of the other. The text: "And when he appoints two agents..." (as above). Commentary: This rule applies to actions requiring opinion, like sale and khul', so that multiple opinions may concur for strength. The proof is that when the principal appointed two, he consented to both their opinions, not just one. So one agent acting alone would not have the principal's consent. The phrase "Even if the countervalue is specified" answers an objection: if the price is fixed, there is no need for opinion, yet the rule still applies because specification does not prevent increasing the price or choosing a suitable buyer. Joint action is still beneficial. Exceptions: If he appoints them for litigation (khusumah), one can act alone because joint presence is impractical in court and may cause confusion; opinion is needed beforehand to prepare the case. Or if he appoints them for divorcing his wife without compensation, freeing his slave without compensation, returning a deposit, or paying a debt—these do not require opinion, they are mere expression; one agent can do them just like two. The opposite is if he says to them: 'Divorce her if you wish' or 'Her affair is in your hands,' because that is a delegation to their opinion and is a tamlik restricted to the council, and because he suspended divorce on their action, so it is analogized to their joint entry.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage establishes the general rule for joint agency: when a principal appoints two agents for a matter that requires judgment (like sale, khul'), neither may act alone without the other. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the principal consented to both their opinions, not just one. The passage then addresses an objection: what if the price is specified? The response is that even then, joint opinion is beneficial because they can increase the price or choose a better buyer. After stating the rule, exceptions are provided: (1) litigation (khusumah) – because requiring both to be present in court is impractical and would cause confusion; opinion is needed beforehand. (2) Acts that do not require opinion, such as divorcing without compensation, freeing a slave, returning a deposit, or paying a debt – these are mere expressions (ta'bir mahd) and one agent can execute them alone. (3) However, if the principal says 'Divorce her if you wish' or 'Her affair is in your hands,' that is a delegation (tafwid) to their opinion, and both must act together because it is a tamlik (conferral of ownership) restricted to the council and the divorce is suspended on their joint action, analogized to a joint condition.

Key Terms
رأي (ra'y): Opinion or judgment; here, the exercise of discretion in a transaction.
خصومة (khusumah): Litigation; legal dispute in court.
تملیک (tamlik): Conferral of ownership; here, giving the agents authority over the wife's divorce as if they own the right.
تعبیر محض (ta'bir mahd): Mere expression; an action that requires no judgment, only conveying the principal's words.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case can one of two appointed agents act without the other?
A) Selling a house for a fixed price
B) Khul' (divorce by compensation) with a specified amount
C) Returning a deposit to the depositor
D) Buying a specific item for a set price

Key Takeaway
Two agents must act jointly in matters requiring discretion; only in litigation, acts of mere expression, and similar can one act alone.

Exceptions to Joint Agency in Hanafi Fiqh
Explains exceptions to joint agency rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five exceptions where one of two agents may act alone and explain the Hanafi rationale for each exception.

Core Idea
When joint action is impossible or unnecessary, a single agent suffices — litigate, give, free, return, pay.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rule that two agents must act jointly, and the five exceptions where one agent may act alone. The exceptions are based on practical necessity (litigation) or the nature of the act being a mere conveyance (divorce, manumission, returning deposit, paying debt). We also explore the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar regarding litigation and the reasoning behind the joint-action requirement.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule of joint agency
The text establishes that when a principal appoints two agents, they must act together. Acting alone is invalid unless an exception applies. The basis is the principal's consent to both opinions.
This rule is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
List the five exceptions
The passage enumerates five cases where one agent may act alone: (1) litigation in court, (2) divorcing the wife without compensation, (3) freeing a slave without compensation, (4) returning a deposit, (5) paying a debt.
These are considered pure conveyances needing no opinion.
3
Analyze the rationale for each exception
For litigation, joint presence causes disruption; consultation beforehand suffices. For the others, no opinion is required—the acts are mere expressions of the principal's will.
Istihsan overrides strict analogy here.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on litigation
Imam Zufar argued that both agents must appear in court because strengthening the case requires joint opinion. The Hanafi response is that consultation before court is sufficient; joint presence is not needed due to practical impossibility.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) follows the majority.

کی رائے پر اور جب موکل دونوں کی رائے پر راضی ہوا تھا تو ایک وکیل کے تصرف کرنے پر مؤکل راضی نہ ہوگا اور جب مؤکل اس پر راضی نہیں ہے تو صرف ایک وکیل کو تصرف کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ دونوں کی رائے کا اکٹھا ہوناضروری ہے۔ والبدل و ان کان مقدر سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اگر عوض اور بدل متعین ہو جائے مثلا موکل نے ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض غلام بیچنے کا وکیل کیا یا ایک ہزار کے عوض خالع کرنے کا وکیل کیا تو اس میں دونوں وکیلوں کی رائے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے پس جب اس میں رائے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے تو دو نوں وکیلوں میں سے ہر ایک بغیر دوسرے کے اس تصرف کا مجاز ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ حالانکہ آپ کہتے ہیں کہ اس صورت میں بھی دونوں کی رائے جمع ہونا ضروری ہے۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ معوض متعین ہونے کی صورت میں اگر چہ متعینہ عوض میں کم کرنا ملک نہیں ہے لیکن زیادہ کرتا تو من ہے۔ یعنی عوض کی تعیین اگر چہ کم کرنے کیلئے مانع ہے لیکن زیادہ کرنے کیلئے مانع نہیں ہے۔ ہیں دونوں وکیلوں کی رات جمع ہونے سے بسا اوقات شمن میں اضافہ ہو سکتا ہے بہر حال ثابت ہو گیا کہ اس صورت میں بھی دونوں کی رائے کا جمع ہونا مفید اور کارآمد ہے۔ نیز مشیر عملی کبھی ناد ہند ہ ہوتا ہے اس سے شمن وصول کرنا بہت دشوار ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس ایسے مشتری کا انتخاب کرنے میں جو ادائے شن میں نہال معمول تھا کرتا دو رائے مشورہ کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے پس اس سے بھی دونوں وکیلوں کی رائے کی ضرورت ثابت ہوگی اور جب دونوں کا کھیلوں کی رات کی ضرورت ہے تو صرف ایک وکیل کو تصرف کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ اگر دونوں میں سے ہر ایک وکیل خصومت ہو تو ایک دوسرے کی عدم موجودگی میں تصرف کر سکتا ہے قال الا ان يوكلهما بالخصومة لان الاجتماع فيها متعذر للافضاء الى الشعب في مجلس القضاء والرأي يحتاج اليه سابقا لتقويم الخصومة قال أو بطلاق زوجته بغير عوض او بعتق عبده بغير عوض او برد وديعة عبده او قضاء دين عليه لان هذه الاشياء لا يحتاج فيها الى الرأى بل هو تعبير محض وعبارة المشى والي سراء وهذا بخلاف ما اذا قال لهما طلقاها ان شئتما او قال امرها بايديكما لانه تفويض إلى رأيهما الأثرى ملیک مقتصر چند صورتیں ایسی ہیں جہاں دو شخصوں کو وکیل کرنے کے باوجود ایک وکیل کا تصرف کرنا جائز اور کافی ہے۔ ان میں سے ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ کسی شخص نے قاضی کی عدالت میں مقدمہ پیش کرنے کیلئے دو شخصوں کو وکیل کیا۔ لیکن ان میں سے ایک وکیل نے بغیر دوسرے کے مقدمہ پیش کر دیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اور اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقدمہ پیش کرتے وقت مجلس قاضی میں لوگوں کا اجتماع متعذ رہے کیونکہ زیادہ لوگوں کے اکٹھا ہونے سے شور وشغب ہوگا۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ شور و شعب کی وجہ سے مجلس قاضی کی ہیبت ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ حالانکہ اس کا باقی رہنا ضروری ہے۔ پس جب کسی نے مقدمہ پیش کرنے کیلئے دو شخصوں کو وکیل کیا حالانکہ اس کو معلوم ہے کہ ان دونوں کا جمع کرنا مستعد رہے گا گویا وہ ان میں سے ایک کے مقدمہ پیش کرنے پر راضی ہو گیا اور جب مؤکل ایک کے مقدمہ پیش کرنے پر راضی ہو گیا تو ان میں سے صرف ایک وکیل کا عدالت قاضی میں مقدمہ پیش کرنا درست اور کافی ہوگا۔ الراى يحتاج اليه سابقا ہے امام زفر کے قول کی تردید کر نا مقصود ہے۔ امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ صرف ایک وکیل کا مقدمہ پیش کرنا درست اور جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ مقدمہ کو مضبوط کر کے پیش کرنے میں رائے مشورے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے اور موکل ان دونوں کی رائے پر راضی ہوا ہے۔ لہذان میں سے صرف ایک رائے پر اکتفا کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ دونوں کی رائے کا جمع ہونا ضروری ہوگا۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ دونوں کی رائے کا جمع ہونا مقدمہ پیش کرنے سے پہلے ضروری ہے تا کہ مقدمہ کو مضبوطی سے قائم کیا جا سکے اور جب ایسا ہے تو دونوں وکیل مقدمہ پیش کرنے سے صلاح و مشورہ کر کے مقدمہ کو مضبوط کر دیں اور پھر مجلس قاضی میں ایک وکیل جا کر پیش کر دے۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ مجلس قاضی میں مقدمہ پیش کرنے کیلئے ایک وکیل کا ہونا کافی ہے دونوں کا جمع ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ دو شخصوں کو اس بات کا وکیل کرے کہ وہ دونوں بغیر عوض اس کی بیوی کو طلاق دے دیں اس صورت میں بھی ان میں سے تنہا ایک وکیل کو طلاق دینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اگر اپنے غلام کو بغیر عوض آزاد کرنے کا دو شخصوں کو وکیل کیا تو بھی ان میں سے ایک وکیل آزاد کرنے کا مجاز ہے۔ چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کے پاس کسی کی ودیعت ہو اور شخص دو شخصوں کو بس ودیعت کے واپس کرنے کا وکیل کرے تو صرف ایک وکیل اس ودیعت کو واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ پانچویں صورت یہ ہے کہ موکل پر جو قرضہ ہے اس کا ادا کرنے کیلئے موکل نے دو شخصوں کو وکیل کیا تو ان دونوں میں سے صرف ایک وکیل قرضہ ادا کر سکتا ہے۔
[And concerning the opinion: when the principal had agreed to both opinions, then he will not be satisfied with one agent acting; when the principal is not satisfied, a single agent does not have the authority to act; rather, the combination of both opinions is necessary. And 'al-badl wa in kana muqaddaran' is the answer to a question. The question is: if the consideration and the thing given in exchange become specified—e.g., the principal appointed an agent to sell a slave for one thousand rupees, or to divorce for one thousand—then there is no need for the opinion of both agents; when there is no need for opinion, then each of the two agents should be authorized to act without the other, yet you say that even in this case the combination of both opinions is necessary. The answer: when the counter-value is specified, even though reducing the specified amount is not permitted, increasing it is permissible. i.e., specification of the price prevents reduction but does not prevent increase. Sometimes the combination of both opinions may lead to an increase in the price; in any case, it is established that even here, the combination of both opinions is beneficial and useful. Also, the buyer [؟] is sometimes uncommon [؟], making it very difficult to receive the price; so in selecting such a buyer who will pay the price, two opinions and consultation are needed; thus the necessity of both agents' opinions is established; when both opinions are needed, a single agent does not have authority to act. If each of the two agents is for litigation, he can act in the absence of the other: He said 'unless he appoints them jointly for litigation, because joint action in that is impossible due to leading to disturbance in the court; and opinion is needed beforehand to strengthen the case.' He said 'or for divorcing his wife without compensation, or freeing his slave without compensation, or returning a deposit of his slave, or paying a debt owed by him, because these matters do not require opinion; rather they are mere conveyance and the expression of the agent is like the expression of the principal.' And this is different from when he said to them 'divorce her if you wish' or said 'her matter is in your hands', because that is delegation to their opinion; it is a form of possession restricted to the council, and because he suspended the divorce on their action, so it is analogized to their entering. No. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri said: If a person appointed two individuals as agents, then one of them does not have the right to act without the other's opinion, but there are several cases where despite appointing two agents, one agent's action is permissible and sufficient. One such case is if a person appointed two agents to present a case in the Qadi's court; then one agent presented the case without the other—this is permissible. The proof: at the time of presenting the case, the gathering of both in the court is difficult, because the assembly of many people leads to noise and disruption, while the court must be kept free from noise and disruption; this is necessary because the purpose of presenting the case is to manifest the truth, and noise prevents that; the second reason is that noise destroys the dignity of the court, which must be preserved. Since the principal appointed two agents knowing that their joint presence is difficult, it is as if he consented to one of them presenting the case; when the principal consents to one, then only one agent's presenting is valid and sufficient. 'Opinion is needed beforehand' is intended to refute Imam Zufar. Imam Zufar said: one agent's presenting is not valid because strengthening the case requires consultation, and the principal agreed to both opinions; so relying on only one opinion is not correct; both opinions must combine. The answer: the combination of opinions is necessary before presenting, to strengthen the case; when that is done, the two agents consult beforehand and strengthen the case, then one agent goes to the court and presents. In any case, it is established that for presenting in court, one agent is sufficient; joint presence is not necessary. The second case: if he appoints two agents to divorce his wife without compensation, then one of them has the authority to divorce. Third case: if he appoints two agents to free his slave without compensation, one agent may free. Fourth case: if someone has a deposit of another, and the depositor appoints two agents to return it, one agent may return it. Fifth case: if the principal has a debt and appoints two agents to pay it, one agent may pay.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the rule of joint agency. It opens by stating the general principle: when a principal appoints two agents, they must act jointly; one cannot act without the other's opinion. This is because the principal agreed to both opinions. The passage then addresses a potential objection: if the price or consideration is specified (e.g., sell for exactly one thousand), why is joint opinion still necessary? The author explains that even with a fixed price, the agents can increase it (though not decrease), so their collective opinion may yield a better deal. Additionally, the buyer may be difficult to find, requiring consultation. Thus, joint opinion remains beneficial. Then the text lists exceptions where one agent may act alone: (1) for litigation (khushoomah) in court, because gathering both causes disruption; (2) divorcing a wife without compensation; (3) freeing a slave without compensation; (4) returning a deposit; (5) paying a debt. These are mere conveyances (ta'beer mahz) needing no opinion, unlike cases where the principal says 'if you wish' or 'the matter is in your hands,' which delegate discretion. The commentary further elaborates on the litigation exception, rebutting Imam Zufar's objection that both opinions are needed. The answer: consultation before court suffices; joint presence is not required. This passage demonstrates Hanafi istihsan (juristic preference) overriding strict qiyas. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as it is part of al-Hidayah commentary.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakālah): Agency; a contract by which someone appoints another to act on their behalf.
خصومت (khuṣūmat): Litigation; legal dispute in court.
عوض (ʿiwaḍ): Consideration; the price or counter-value in a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is an exception where one of two agents may act alone?
A) Selling a house with a fixed price.
B) Divorcing the wife without compensation.
C) Both are exceptions.
D) Neither is an exception.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes five situations where one agent may act alone: litigation, divorce without compensation, manumission without compensation, returning a deposit, and paying a debt — all based on lack of need for opinion or practical impossibility.

Two Agents for Litigation: One Agent May Act Alone
Ruling with rational proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether one agent may act alone in court litigation and explain the rational proof (istihsan) that supports it.

Core Idea
For court presentation, one agent suffices—practical necessity overrides the need for both.

Al-Quduri laid down the general principle that two agents must act jointly. But the Hanafi school recognizes an exception for court cases: one agent may present the case alone. This lesson unpacks the rational proof based on courtroom dignity and implicit consent, and addresses the objection of Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State al-Quduri's rule: when two agents are appointed, one cannot act without the other's opinion.
2
Recognize the exception
The commentator lists exceptions; the one in focus is court presentation. Understand the practical need for the exception.
3
Explain the rational proof
The proof: gathering both would cause noise and destroy court dignity, hindering truth. Therefore, implicit consent is inferred.
This is istihsan overriding qiyas.
4
Analyze the opposing view
Imam Zufar argued that both must act because consultation strengthens the case. Note his reasoning.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The response: consultation can occur before court; after that, one may present. Thus, the mufta bihi is that one agent suffices.
Note the tarjih: majority view prevails over Zufar.

تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا تھا کہ اگر کسی شخص نے دو شخصوں کو وکیل کیا ہو تو ان میں سے ایک کو بغیر دوسرے کی رائے کے تصرف کا حق حاصل نہیں ہے لیکن چند صورتیں ایسی ہیں جہاں دو شخصوں کو وکیل کرنے کے باوجود ایک وکیل کا تصرف کرنا جائز اور کافی ہے۔ ان میں سے ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ کسی شخص نے قاضی کی عدالت میں مقدمہ پیش کرنے کیلئے دو شخصوں کو وکیل کیا۔ لیکن ان میں سے ایک وکیل نے بغیر دوسرے کے مقدمہ پیش کر دیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اور اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقدمہ پیش کرتے وقت مجلس قاضی میں لوگوں کا اجتماع متعذر ہے کیونکہ زیادہ لوگوں کے اکٹھا ہونے سے شور و شغب ہوگا۔ حالانکہ مجلس قاضی کو شور و شغب سے محفوظ رکھنا ضروری ہے اور مجلس قاضی کو شور و شغب سے محفوظ رکھنا اسلئے ضروری ہے کہ مقدمہ پیش کرنے سے مقصود اظہار حق ہے اور شور و شغب کی وجہ سے یہ مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ شور و شغب کی وجہ سے مجلس قاضی کی ہیبت ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ حالانکہ اس کا باقی رہنا ضروری ہے۔ پس جب کسی نے مقدمہ پیش کرنے کیلئے دو شخصوں کو وکیل کیا حالانکہ اس کو معلوم ہے کہ ان دونوں کا جمع کرنا متعذر ہے گویا وہ ان میں سے ایک کے مقدمہ پیش کرنے پر راضی ہو گیا اور جب موکل ایک کے مقدمہ پیش کرنے پر راضی ہو گیا تو ان میں سے صرف ایک وکیل کا عدالت قاضی میں مقدمہ پیش کرنا درست اور کافی ہوگا۔ الرأى يحتاج إليه سابقاً ہے امام زفر کے قول کی تردید کرنا مقصود ہے۔ امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ صرف ایک وکیل کا مقدمہ پیش کرنا درست اور جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ مقدمہ کو مضبوط کر کے پیش کرنے میں رائے مشورے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے اور موکل ان دونوں کی رائے پر راضی ہوا ہے۔ لہذا ان میں سے صرف ایک رائے پر اکتفا کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ دونوں کی رائے کا جمع ہونا ضروری ہوگا۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ دونوں کی رائے کا جمع ہونا مقدمہ پیش کرنے سے پہلے ضروری ہے تا کہ مقدمہ کو مضبوطی سے قائم کیا جا سکے اور جب ایسا ہے تو دونوں وکیل مقدمہ پیش کرنے سے صلاح و مشورہ کر کے مقدمہ کو مضبوط کر دیں اور پھر مجلس قاضی میں ایک وکیل جا کر پیش کر دے۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ مجلس قاضی میں مقدمہ پیش کرنے کیلئے ایک وکیل کا ہونا کافی ہے دونوں کا جمع ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
Commentary: Sadr al-Shari'ah (al-Quduri) stated: If a person appoints two persons as agents, then none of them has the right to act without the other's opinion. However, there are several cases where despite appointing two, the action of one agent is permissible and sufficient. One such case: a person appointed two agents to present a case in the qadi's court, but one of the agents presented the case without the other; this is permissible. The proof: when presenting the case, gathering people in the qadi's court is difficult because many people gathering causes noise and disturbance, whereas the qadi's court must be kept free from noise and disturbance; this is necessary because the purpose of presenting the case is to manifest the truth, and noise prevents that. Second reason: noise destroys the dignity of the court, which must be preserved. So when one appointed two for court presentation knowing that gathering both is difficult, it is as if he consented to one presenting it. Therefore, presentation by one is valid and sufficient. This is a refutation of Imam Zufar's view. Imam Zufar said: presentation by only one is not correct because presenting a strong case requires consultation, and the principal consented to both their opinions, so acting on one opinion is insufficient; both opinions must be combined. The answer: combining their opinions is necessary before presenting the case to strengthen it; they can consult beforehand, then one goes to court. So it is established that for court presentation, one agent suffices.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The passage begins by stating the general principle from al-Quduri: when two are appointed, one cannot act without the other. Then an exception is given: in litigation before a qadi, one may act alone. The proof is rational (dalil 'aqli): gathering both would cause disruption in court (shor o shaghab), which impedes the purpose of truth and destroys the court's dignity. Therefore, the principal's implicit consent is deduced. The passage then addresses the opposing view of Imam Zufar, who argued that both must act because consultation is needed. The Hanafi response is that consultation can occur before the court session; after that, one may present. Thus, the operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that one agent suffices for court presentation. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas requiring both.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakīl): An agent appointed by another (muwakkil) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
مجلس قاضی (majlis al-qāḍī): The court session where the qadi hears cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling when a person appoints two agents to present a case in court, and one agent presents it alone?
A) It is invalid because both agents must act together.
B) It is valid and sufficient because gathering both would cause disruption in court.
C) It is valid only if the other agent gives permission.
D) It is valid only if the principal explicitly permits one to act alone.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, one agent may present a case in court alone due to implicit consent based on the difficulty of gathering both and the need to preserve court dignity.

Four Cases Where One Agent Suffices in Joint Agency
Listing four additional cases where one agent suffices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four cases where one of two appointed agents may act alone according to the Hanafi school and explain the rationale based on the nature of the act as mere conveyance of speech.

Core Idea
In divorce, manumission, returning a deposit, and paying a debt, one agent suffices because the act is merely conveying the principal's words.

In Hanafi law, when a principal appoints two agents for a task, they must generally act together. However, there are exceptions. This lesson covers four such cases where a single agent can act alone. The common thread is that these acts require no personal judgment—they are mere communication of the principal's speech. Understanding these exceptions helps clarify the boundaries of joint agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Recognize that in most cases, two agents must act jointly. The principal appoints them to act together, implying consultation.
The general rule is not explicitly stated in this passage but is assumed.
2
List the four exceptional acts
Memorize the four cases: divorce without compensation, manumission without compensation, returning a deposit, and paying a debt.
These are all without monetary consideration in the first two.
3
Understand the rationale
In these acts, the agent merely conveys the principal's speech; no deliberation is needed. One person can convey as well as two.
The text says: 'the agent's job is merely to communicate the principal's words.'
4
Contrast with acts requiring consultation
Contrast these four with acts like litigation or sales where joint judgment is necessary.
The passage mentions that in litigation, the first case (not covered here) required both agents to avoid disruption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ دو شخصوں کو اس بات کا وکیل کرے کہ وہ دونوں بغیر عوض اس کی بیوی کو طلاق دے دیں اس صورت میں بھی ان میں سے تنہا ایک وکیل کو طلاق دینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اگر اپنے غلام کو بغیر عوض آزاد کرنے کا دو شخصوں کو وکیل کیا تو بھی ان میں سے ایک وکیل آزاد کرنے کا مجاز ہے۔ چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کے پاس کسی کی ودیعت ہو اور اس شخص نے دو شخصوں کو اس ودیعت کے واپس کرنے کا وکیل کرے تو صرف ایک وکیل اس ودیعت کو واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ پانچویں صورت یہ ہے کہ موکل پر جو قرضہ ہے اس کا ادا کرنے کیلئے موکل نے دو شخصوں کو وکیل کیا تو ان دونوں میں سے صرف ایک وکیل قرضہ ادا کر سکتا ہے۔ آخر کی چاروں صورتوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان چاروں صورتوں میں رائے مشورہ کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں بلکہ توکیل صرف موکل کے کلام کو ادا کرتا ہے۔ یعنی طلاق، عتاق، ادائے ودیعت اور ادائے قرض میں وکیل کا کام صرف اتنا ہے کہ وہ موکل کے کلام کو ادا کر دے اور کلام ادا کرنے میں ایک اور دو دونوں برابر ہیں کیونکہ معنی میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں۔ پس جس طرح دو آدمی موکل کے کلام کی ترجمانی کریں گے۔ اسی طرح ایک آدمی بھی کرے گا۔ ان دونوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔
Second case: a person appoints two agents to divorce his wife without compensation; in this case also, one agent alone has the authority to divorce. Third case: if he appoints two agents to free his slave without compensation, then one agent is authorized to free. Fourth case: if someone has a deposit (wadi'ah) of another, and that person appoints two agents to return the deposit, then only one agent can return it. Fifth case: if the principal has a debt, and he appoints two agents to pay it, then only one agent can pay. The proof for the last four cases is that in these four cases, there is no need for consultation; rather, the agency is only to convey the principal's speech. That is, in divorce, manumission, returning a deposit, and paying a debt, the agent's job is merely to communicate the principal's words, and in conveying speech, one and two are equal because there is no difference in meaning. Just as two persons may interpret the principal's speech, so may one person; there is no difference between them.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement listing four additional exceptions to the general rule that two agents must act together. The commentator enumerates them: (1) divorce without compensation, (2) freeing a slave without compensation, (3) returning a deposit, (4) paying a debt. The reason given is that these acts require no personal judgment; the agent merely conveys the principal's words. Since conveying speech is the same whether done by one or two, one agent suffices. These are distinct from the first case (litigation) where the proof was based on court disruption; here the proof is based on the nature of the act being mere communication. This is a useful categorization for students to memorize.

Key Terms
طلاق بغير عوض (ṭalāq bi-ghayr 'iwaḍ): Divorce pronounced by the husband without any compensation from the wife (i.e., not khul').
عتاق ('itāq): Manumission of a slave, freeing without compensation.
وديعت (wadī'ah): Deposit; an item left with another for safekeeping.
قرض (qarḍ): Debt; money owed by the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The four exceptions to the rule of joint agency are divorce without compensation, manumission without compensation, returning a deposit, and paying a debt—because these are mere conveyances of the principal's speech.
