Agent Cannot Appoint Sub-Agent Unless Authorized
Ruling on an agent delegating to another agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule, exceptions, and legal effects when an agent delegates to another agent in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
An agent cannot delegate without permission; sub-agent becomes principal's agent if valid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a fundamental limitation on an agent's authority: the agent cannot appoint a sub-agent because the principal trusted his specific judgment. However, the principal may permit delegation explicitly or through broad language. Understanding this rule is crucial for commercial and legal agency relationships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Locate the statement 'ليس للوكيل أن يوكل' and understand that it is a prohibition. The agent has no inherent right to delegate.
The rule is based on the principal's consent being specific to the agent's opinion.
2
Recognize the Exceptions
The text provides two exceptions: explicit permission from the principal, or the principal saying 'act on your opinion'. These indicate broader delegation.
The phrase 'اعمل برأيك' is interpreted as a general authorization to use judgment, including delegation.
3
Analyze the Legal Consequences when Delegation is Valid
If delegation is valid, the sub-agent becomes the principal's direct agent. The original agent cannot dismiss the sub-agent, nor does the sub-agent's appointment end with the original agent's death.
Both agents are dismissed only upon the principal's death.
4
Connect to Parallel Rule for Judges
The commentator notes that a similar rule applies to judges delegating authority, as covered in Adab al-Qadi.
This reinforces the principle that delegation of authority requires explicit authorization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وليس للوكيل ان يوكل فيما وكل به لانه فوض اليه التصرف دون التوكيل به وهذا لانه رضى برأيه والناس متفاوتون فى الاراء قال الا ان ياذن له المؤكل لوجود الرضاً أو يقول له اعمل برأيك لاطلاق التفويض الى رايه واذا جاز فى هذا الوجه يكون الثانى وكيلا عن المؤكل حتى لا يملك الاول عزله ولا ينعزل بموته وينعزلان بموت الأول وقد مر نظيره في ادب القاض فی القاضي
He said: It is not permissible for an agent to appoint another agent in the matter for which he was appointed, because he was given authority to act, not to appoint an agent. This is because the principal consented to his judgment, and people differ in opinions. He said: Except if the principal permits him, because then consent exists; or if he says to him 'Act on your opinion', because it is an absolute delegation to his opinion. And when it is permissible in this way, the second is an agent of the principal, so the first cannot dismiss him, nor is he dismissed by the first's death, but both are dismissed by the principal's death. Its parallel has passed in Adab al-Qadi.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn (original text of Hidayah) with brief commentary. The general rule: an agent (wakil) cannot delegate his agency to another (tawkil) because the principal appointed him specifically for his judgment. People's opinions differ, so the principal's consent was particular to him. However, two exceptions: (1) if the principal explicitly permits tawkil; (2) if the principal tells the agent 'act on your opinion' (i'mal bi-ra'yik), which broadly delegates the task to his judgment, including the right to delegate. If the sub-agent is appointed, he becomes the agent of the principal directly: the original agent cannot dismiss him, and the sub-agent is not dismissed by the original agent's death; both are dismissed only by the principal's death. The commentator notes that this rule is similar to what was discussed in Adab al-Qadi regarding judges delegating.

Key Terms
توكيل (tawkīl): Appointing another agent; the act of delegation by the original agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An agent cannot delegate to another agent unless the principal explicitly permits or says 'act on your opinion'; valid delegation makes the sub-agent a direct agent of the principal.

Delegation in Agency: The Rule and Its Exceptions
General ruling on delegation in agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that a wakil cannot appoint a sub-agent without permission and identify the two exceptions that permit delegation.

Core Idea
A wakil cannot delegate without the muwakkil's permission; exceptions require explicit consent or absolute discretion.

This passage from the chapter of Agency (Wakalah) establishes a fundamental principle of agency law: the agent (wakil) acts as a fiduciary and cannot delegate his task to another without the principal's (muwakkil) consent. The reasoning is that the principal's trust is specific to the agent's own judgment. This lesson unpacks the rule and its two exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The wakil cannot appoint another wakil for the same task without permission. This is the default position in Hanafi law.
The passage emphasizes that the muwakkil's consent is specific to the wakil's opinion.
2
Understand the rationale
The muwakkil is satisfied only with the wakil's opinion. Since people's opinions differ, consent to one does not imply consent to another. Appointing a sub-agent without permission violates the muwakkil's command.
This rationale distinguishes personal agency from impersonal tasks.
3
Identify the first exception
If the muwakkil explicitly permits delegation, then the wakil may appoint a sub-agent. The permission makes the delegation valid.
The sub-agent then becomes the agent of the muwakkil, not the first wakil.
4
Identify the second exception
If the muwakkil says to the wakil, 'Act according to your opinion,' this implies absolute discretion and includes the authority to delegate.
This is a form of general mandate (tafwid 'ala al-itlaq).
5
Note the legal effects of valid delegation
When delegation is valid, the second wakil is the agent of the muwakkil. The first wakil cannot dismiss the second, the death of the first does not end the second's agency, but the death of the muwakkil dismisses both.
This ensures the sub-agent's authority is directly tied to the principal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة
ادب القاضی میں گزر چکی ہے
نشرت صور تسمیہ یہ ہے کہ وکیل کو جس کام میں کیا کیا گیا وہ اس کام میں کسی دوسرے کو کیا کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے وکیل کیونکہ متوکل نے وکیل کے سپرد اس کام میں تصرف کیا ہے جس کا اس کو وکیل کیا گیا ہے اور اس تصرف کیلئے کسی دوسرے کو وکیل کرنا اس کے سپرد نہیں کیا گیا تو وہ دوسرے آدمی کو وکیل کرنے کا مجاز بھی نہ ہوگا اور یہ عدم جواز توکیل اسلئے ہے کہ متوکل صرف وکیل کی رائے پر ہی راضی ہوا ہے اور لوگوں کی رائیں مختلف ہوتی ہیں۔ لہذا اس کی رائے پر راضی ہونے سے دوسرے کی رائے پر راضی ہونا لازم نہیں آتا اور جب ایسا ہے تو وکیل کو اپنے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کو اسی کام کیلئے وکیل کرنا مؤکل کے حکم کی خلاف ورزی ہے اور موکل کے حکم کی خلاف ورزی جو خود سے منع ہے۔ دوسرے کو وکیل کرنا بھی نا جائز ہے۔ لیکن اگر مؤکل اپنے وکیل کو اس بات کی اجازت دے دے تو وکیل کے لئے وکیل کرنا جائز ہوگا کیونکہ اس وقت توکیل وکیل پر موکل کی اذن موجود ہے یا موکل اپنے وکیل سے یہ کہے کہ تو اپنی رائے سے عمل کر تو اس صورت میں بھی اس کیلئے وکیل کرنے کی اجازت ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں تفویض علی الاطلاق وکیل کی رائے پر کیا گیا۔ لہذا موکل کی اجازت اور حکم کے تحت وکیل کا اپنے علاوہ کو وکیل کرنا بھی داخل ہو گا تو جب توکیل وکیل موکل کی اجازت سے جائز ہے تو وکیل کا اپنے علاوہ کو وکیل کرنا بھی درست ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ جب مذکورہ دو صورتوں میں توکیل ہوتی ہے تو وکیل ثانی ، متوکل کی طرف سے وکیل ہوگا نہ کہ وکیل اول کی طرف سے چنانچہ وکیل اول ، وکیل ثانی کو معزول کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ اور وکیل اول کی موت سے وکیل ثانی معزول نہ ہوگا۔ البتہ موکل کی موت سے دونوں معزول ہو جائیں
Chapter of Agency. It has passed in Adab al-Qadi. The summary of the ruling is that the wakil has no authority to appoint another person in the task for which he was appointed, because the muwakkil only entrusted the wakil with acting in that task, and he did not entrust him with appointing another for that action. So he will not be authorized to appoint another person. And this lack of authorization for delegation is because the muwakkil is only satisfied with the wakil's opinion, and people's opinions differ. Therefore, being satisfied with his opinion does not necessitate being satisfied with another's opinion. When this is the case, the wakil appointing someone else for the same task is a violation of the muwakkil's command, and violating the muwakkil's command is prohibited. Appointing another is also not permissible. But if the muwakkil gives permission to his wakil for this, then it is permissible for the wakil to appoint another, because then there is the muwakkil's permission for delegation. Or if the muwakkil says to his wakil, 'Act according to your opinion,' then in this case also he has permission to delegate, because in this case delegation is made absolutely to the wakil's opinion. Therefore, under the muwakkil's permission and command, the wakil's appointing another is included. So when delegation by the wakil is valid with the muwakkil's permission, then the wakil appointing another is also valid. The author of Hidayah said: When delegation occurs in these two cases, the second wakil will be an agent of the muwakkil, not of the first wakil. Consequently, the first wakil will not have the authority to dismiss the second wakil. And the death of the first wakil does not dismiss the second wakil. However, the death of the muwakkil dismisses both.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a general ruling statement from the chapter of Agency (Wakalah) in Ashraf Ul Hadaya. It establishes the fundamental principle that a wakil (agent) cannot appoint another wakil (sub-agent) for the same task without the explicit permission of the muwakkil (principal). The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the muwakkil's consent is specific to the wakil's own judgment and opinion. Since people's opinions vary, consent to one does not imply consent to another. Therefore, appointing a sub-agent without permission is a violation of the muwakkil's command and is impermissible (na jaiz). Two exceptions are mentioned: (1) the muwakkil explicitly permits delegation, and (2) the muwakkil tells the wakil to act according to his own opinion (tafwid 'ala al-itlaq), which implicitly includes the authority to delegate. In both exceptions, the second wakil becomes the agent of the muwakkil, not the first wakil, meaning only the muwakkil can dismiss him, and the death of the first wakil does not end the second's agency. This principle is standard in the Hanafi school, as found in Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage also references Adab al-Qadi for further details.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): An agent appointed by the principal (muwakkil) to perform a specific task. In this passage, the wakil is the first agent who may or may not have authority to delegate.
موکل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the wakil. His consent is central to the validity of sub-agency.
توکیل (tawkil): The act of appointing an agent. In this passage, it specifically refers to the wakil appointing a sub-agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, when is a wakil permitted to appoint another wakil (sub-agent) for the same task?
A) Whenever the wakil deems it necessary for the task
B) Only if the muwakkil explicitly gives permission or says 'act according to your opinion'
C) Only if the task is complex
D) Never, as agency is personal

Key Takeaway
A wakil cannot delegate without the muwakkil's permission; valid delegation requires explicit consent or a general mandate, and then the sub-agent is the principal's agent.

6 min
Validity of the Second Wakil's Contract: Presence, Ratification, and Price-Setting
Detailed scenarios of sub-agency validity based on principal's purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for the validity of a sub-agent's contract by analyzing whether the first wakil's opinion (ra'y) is present, either physically or through ratification.

Core Idea
A second wakil's contract is valid only if the first wakil's opinion is present — through presence, ratification, or prior price-setting.

Agency (wakalah) in Hanafi fiqh is built on the principal's trust in the wakil's judgment. When a wakil appoints a second wakil without permission, the validity of the second wakil's contract hinges on whether the first wakil's opinion (ra'y) is effectively present. This lesson unpacks the key scenarios from Al-Hidayah: contracting in the presence or absence of the first wakil, ratification after the fact, and the effect of the first wakil setting the price. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying agency law in transactions where sub-agency arises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
The text asks: when a wakil appoints a second wakil without the principal's permission, under what conditions is the second wakil's contract valid? The answer revolves around the presence of the first wakil's opinion (ra'y).
The principal's purpose (maqsud) is key.
2
Analyze the scenario of presence
If the second wakil contracts in the presence of the first wakil, the contract is valid because the first wakil's opinion is present. This satisfies the principal's purpose.
Scholars differed on whether the rights of the contract revert to the first or second wakil.
3
Analyze the scenario of absence
If the second wakil contracts in the absence of the first wakil, the contract is invalid because the first wakil's opinion is lost. However, if the first wakil later ratifies (by being informed and permitting), the opinion becomes present and the contract becomes valid.
Same rule applies if a stranger (third party) sells and the wakil ratifies.
4
Analyze the exception for price-setting
If the first wakil sets the price for the second wakil, then the second wakil can validly contract in the first wakil's absence because the opinion needed for pricing is already present. The purpose of pricing is fulfilled.
This differs from the case where the principal appoints two wakils and sets the price — there, both must act together.
5
Distinguish the two-wakil case
When the principal appoints two wakils and sets the price, the principal's purpose is the gathering of both opinions for price increase or buyer selection. Thus, both must concur, unlike the single-price-set scenario.
If no price is set and only one wakil is appointed, his opinion suffices for the major matter (price estimation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مؤکل کی اجازت کے بغیر وکیل نے آگے وکیل بنایا وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی موجودگی میں تصرف کیا جائز ہے
بدایتی
قال فان وكل بغير اذن مؤكله فعقد وكيله بحضرته جاز لان المقصود حضور رأى الأول وقد حضر وتكلموا فى حقوقه وان عقد في حال غيبته لم يجزلانه فات رأيه الا ان يبلغه فيجزيه و كذا لو باع غير الوكيل فبلغه فاجازه لانه حضر رأية ولو قدر الاول الثمن للثانى فعقد بغيبته يجوز لان الرأى يحتاج اليه فيه لتقدير الثمن ظاهرا وقد حصل وهذا بخلاف ما اذا وكل وكيلين وقدر الثمن لأنه لما فوض اليهما مع تقدير الثمن ظهران غرضه اجتماع رأيهما فى الزيادة واختيار المشترى على ما بيناه اما اذا لم يقدر الثمن وفوض ى الاول كان غرضه رأيه فى معظم الامر وهو التقدير في الثمن ترجمہ اور اگر وکیل اول نے موکل کی اجازت کے بغیر دوسرا وکیل کیا پس وکیل اول کے وکیل نے وکیل اول کی موجودگی میں معقد کیا تو جائز ہے اسلئے کہ موکل کا مقصود وکیل اول کی رائے کا موجود ہوتا ہے اور وہ یہاں موجود ہے اور علماء نے اس عقد کے حقوق میں کلام کیا ہے۔ اور اگر وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی عدم موجودگی میں عقد کیا تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ وکیل اول کی راے فوت ہوگئی مگر یہ کہ وکیل اول کو خبر پہنچے پھر وہ اس کی اجازت دیدے اسی طرح اگر وکیل ثانی کے علاوہ نے بیچا پھر وکیل اول کو خبر پہنچی اور اس نے اجازت دیدی کیونکہ وکیل اول کی رائے موجود ہوگئی اور اگر وکیل اول نے وکیل ثانی کیلئے شمن کا انداز و بیان کر دیا پھر وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی عدم موجودگی میں منعقد کیا تو جائز ہوگا کیونکہ بظاہر شمن کا انداز کرنے کے لئے عقد میں رائے کی ضرورت ہوتی ہے اور رائے حاصل ہو چکی ہے اور یہ اسکے جب مؤکل نے دو وکیل گئے ہوں اور شمن کا اندازہ بیان کردیا ہو کیونکہ جب کرنے کے باوجود عقد دو کیلوں کے سپرد کیا تو ظاہر ہو گیا کہ موکل کا مقصد شمن بڑھانے اور مشتری پسند کرنے میں دونوں کی رائے کا جمع ہونا ہے چنانچہ ہم نے بیان کیا ہے لیکن جب ثمن کا اندازہ بیان نہیں کیا اور عقد وکیل اول کے سپرد کیا گیا تو موکل کی غرض سب سے بڑی بات یعنی تقدیر شمن میں اس کی رائے طلب کرنا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وکیل نے اپنے مؤکل کی اجازت کے بغیر کسی کو اسی معاملہ میں وکیل کر دیا جس میں خود اس کو وکیل کیا گیا تھا اور وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی موجودگی میں عقد کر لیا تو یہ عقد جائز اور نافذ ہوگا کیونکہ متوکل کا مقصود یہ تھا کہ وکیل اول کی رائے موجود ہو اور مذکورہ صورت میں وکیل اول کی رائے موجود ہوگئی پس جب وکیل اول کی رائے موجود ہو گئی تو موکل کا مقصود حاصل ہو گیا اور جب موکل کا مقصود حاصل ہو گیا تو وکیل ثانی کا منعقد کردہ عقد بھی جائز ہوگا۔ البتہ علماء کا اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ وکیل ثانی کے منعقد کردہ عقد کے حقوق کس کی طرف راجع ہوں گے علماء کے درمیان اس بات میں اختلاف اسلئے پیدا ہوا کہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں اس مسئلہ کا کوئی حکم ذکر نہیں فرمایا ہے بہر حال بعض علماء نے کہا کہ اس عقد کے حقوق وکیل اول کی طرف راجع ہوں گے کیونکہ مؤکل اسی بات پر راضی ہوا ہے کہ ذمہ داریاں اور حقوق عقد وکیل اول کی طرف راجع ہوں۔ اور بعض علماء نے کہا کہ اس عقد کے حقوق وکیل ثانی کی طرف راجع ہوں گے کیونکہ سبب یعنی عقد وکیل ثانی ہی کی طرف سے پایا گیا ہے۔ نہ کہ وکیل اول کی طرف سے اور جس کی طرف سے سبب یعنی عقد موجود ہوتا ہے۔ حقوق اسی کی طرف لوٹتے ہیں اس لئے حقوق وکیل ثانی کی طرف راجع ہوں گے اور اگر وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی عدم موجودگی میں عقد کیا تو یہ عقد جائز اور نافذ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں وکیل اول کی رائے مفقود ہوگئی ہے اور جب وکیل اول کی رائے فوت ہوگئی تو موکل کا مقصود حاصل نہیں ہوا اور جب مؤکل کا مقصود حاصل نہیں ہوا تو عقد بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر وکیل ثانی کے عقد کی خبر وکیل اول کو پہنچ گئی اور وکیل اول نے اس عقد کی اجازت دیدی تو وکیل اول کی رائے کے متحقق ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ عقد جائز اور نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر وکیل کے علاوہ کسی اجنبی آدمی نے عقد کیا اور وکیل اول کو جب اس عقد کی خبر موصول ہوئی تو اس نے اس کی اجازت دیدی پس اس صورت میں بھی یہ عقد جائز ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی وکیل کے اجازت دینے سے اس کی رائے موجود ہوگئی ہے۔ اور اگر وکیل اول نے وکیل ثانی کے سامنے اس چیز کا شمن متعین کر دیا جس چیز کو بیچنے کا وکیل کیا گیا تھا۔ پھر وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی عدم موجودگی میں اس چیز کو اس متعین کردہ شمن کے عوض فروخت کر دیا تو یہ فروخت کرنا یعنی عقد کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بظاہر عقد میں شمن متعین کرنے کیلئے رائے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے اور یہ مقصد یعنی شمن متعین کرنا حاصل ہو چکا ہے اور جب مقصود حاصل ہو چکا تو وکیل اول کا موجود ہونا ضروری نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر کسی شخص نے سامان بیچنے کے لئے دو وکیل مقرر کئے اور موکل نے اس سامان کا شمن بھی متعین کر دیا تو متعینہ شمن کے عوض صرف ایک وکیل کا فروخت کرنا درست نہ ہوگا بلکہ دونوں وکیلوں کی رائے کا جمع ہونا ضروری ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ موکل کا شمن متعین کرنے کے باوجود مذکورہ شی کو فروخت کرنے کیلئے دو وکیلوں کو مقرر کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ موکل کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ دو وکیلوں کی رائے اکٹھا ہونے سے متعین کردہ شمن میں اضافہ ہو جائے ۔ یا دونوں وکیل مل کر ایسا مشتری منتخب کریں جو شمن ادا کرنے میں ٹال مٹول نہ کرے بہر حال جب ثمن متعین کرنے کے باوجود وکیل مقرر کرنے سے مؤکل کا یہ مقصد وابستہ ہے تو صرف ایک وکیل کا فروخت کرنا درست نہ ہوگا بلکہ دونوں کا ملا کر فروخت کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ لیکن جب مؤکل نے شمن متعین نہیں کیا بلکہ عقد بیع وکیل اول کے سپرد کر دیا تو اس صورت میں موکل کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ عقد بیع کے سبب سے اہم معاملہ یعنی شمن متعین
If the wakil appoints another without the principal's permission, and the second wakil contracts in his presence, it is valid because the purpose is the presence of the first's opinion and it is present. They have discussed its rights. If he contracts in his absence, it is not valid because his opinion is lost, unless he is informed and then permits. Similarly, if someone other than the wakil sells and then he is informed and permits, it is valid because his opinion is present. And if the first sets the price for the second and he contracts in his absence, it is valid because the opinion needed for price estimation is apparent and has been obtained. This is different from the case where he appoints two wakils and sets the price, because in that case his purpose is the gathering of both their opinions for increase and choice of buyer, as we have explained. But if he does not set the price and delegates to the first, his purpose is his opinion in the greater matter, i.e., price estimation. Translation: And if the first wakil appointed a second wakil without the principal's permission, and the second wakil contracted in the presence of the first wakil, it is valid because the principal's purpose is the presence of the first wakil's opinion, and it is present. Scholars have discussed the rights of this contract. If the second wakil contracts in the absence of the first wakil, it is not valid because the first wakil's opinion is lost, unless the first wakil is informed and then gives permission. Similarly, if someone other than the second wakil sells, and then the first wakil is informed and permits, it is valid because the first wakil's opinion becomes present. And if the first wakil sets the price for the second wakil, and then the second wakil contracts in the absence of the first wakil, it is valid because apparently the contract needs an opinion for setting the price, and that opinion has been obtained. And this is so when the principal appoints two wakils and sets the price, because when he entrusts the contract to both despite setting the price, it becomes clear that the principal's purpose is the gathering of both their opinions for increasing the price and choosing the buyer, as we have explained. But when the price is not set and the contract is entrusted to the first wakil, the principal's purpose is his opinion in the greatest matter, i.e., price estimation. Explanation: The scenario is that if the wakil, without the principal's permission, appoints someone as wakil in the same matter in which he himself was appointed, and the second wakil contracts in the presence of the first wakil, then this contract is valid and effective, because the principal's purpose was that the first wakil's opinion be present, and in this case the first wakil's opinion is present. Therefore, when the first wakil's opinion is present, the principal's purpose is achieved, and when the principal's purpose is achieved, the contract made by the second wakil is also valid. However, scholars differ as to whom the rights of this contract refer. The difference arose because Imam Muhammad did not mention any ruling on this issue in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Nevertheless, some scholars said that the rights of this contract refer to the first wakil, because the principal consented that the responsibilities and rights refer to the first wakil. And some scholars said that the rights refer to the second wakil, because the cause (i.e., the contract) is found on the part of the second wakil, not the first wakil. Rights revert to the one from whom the cause (contract) originates, so the rights will refer to the second wakil. And if the second wakil contracts in the absence of the first wakil, this contract is not valid or effective, because in that case the first wakil's opinion is missing, and when the first wakil's opinion is lost, the principal's purpose is not achieved, and when the principal's purpose is not achieved, the contract is not valid. Yes, if news of the second wakil's contract reaches the first wakil and he permits it, then due to the realization of the first wakil's opinion, this contract becomes valid and effective. Similarly, if a stranger (not the second wakil) sells, and when news of this contract reaches the first wakil he permits it, then in this case also the contract is valid, because in this case also, due to the wakil's permission, his opinion becomes present. And if the first wakil specifies the price for the second wakil for the item he was appointed to sell, and then the second wakil sells that item for that specified price in the absence of the first wakil, then this sale (i.e., contract) is valid, because apparently in the contract an opinion is needed for setting the price, and this purpose (setting the price) has been achieved. And when the purpose is achieved, the presence of the first wakil is not necessary. But if a person appoints two wakils to sell goods, and the principal also sets the price for those goods, then selling by only one wakil at the set price is not valid; rather, the gathering of both wakils' opinions is necessary. The evidence is that although the principal set the price, appointing two wakils to sell the said item is proof that the principal's purpose is that by gathering the opinions of the two wakils, the set price may be increased, or that both wakils together choose such a buyer who does not procrastinate in paying the price. In any case, when despite setting the price, the principal's purpose is connected to appointing wakils, then selling by only one wakil is not valid; rather, it is necessary that both sell together. But when the principal did not set the price and entrusted the sale contract to the first wakil, then in that case the principal's purpose is that through the contract of sale, the important matter i.e., setting the price
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of a ruling from Al-Hidayah (Bidayah al-Mubtadi) regarding the validity of a sub-agent's contract when the first wakil appointed a second wakil without the principal's permission. The matn (in Arabic) presents several scenarios: (1) If the second wakil contracts in the presence of the first wakil, the contract is valid because the principal's purpose—the presence of the first wakil's opinion—is achieved. Scholars differ on whether the rights of the contract revert to the first or second wakil. (2) If the second wakil contracts in the absence of the first wakil, it is invalid unless the first wakil subsequently ratifies it. (3) If someone other than the second wakil (a stranger) sells and the first wakil later ratifies, it is valid. (4) If the first wakil sets the price for the second wakil, then the second wakil can validly sell in the absence of the first, because the opinion needed for pricing is already present. (5) If the principal appoints two wakils and sets the price, both must act together because the principal's purpose is the gathering of their opinions for price increase or buyer selection. The commentary explains that this ruling is based on understanding the principal's underlying purpose (maqsud). The ikhtilaf among scholars (whether rights revert to first or second wakil) arises because Imam Muhammad did not explicitly address this in al-Jami' al-Saghir; hence later scholars differed. The text then elaborates that ratification by the first wakil cures the defect. The passage concludes with the rule regarding two wakils: if the principal sets the price, both must agree; if not, the first wakil alone can act, because the key matter (price setting) requires his opinion.

Key Terms
وكيل ثاني (wakil thani): The second agent appointed by the first wakil without the principal's permission. His contract's validity depends on the first wakil's presence or ratification.
رأي (ra'y): The opinion or judgment of the wakil. The principal's purpose is the presence of the first wakil's ra'y, which justifies the contract's validity when present.
حقوق (huquq): The rights and obligations arising from the contract made by the second wakil. Scholars differed on whether these revert to the first wakil or the second wakil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the first wakil appoints a second wakil without the principal's permission, and the second wakil contracts in the absence of the first wakil, under which condition does the contract become valid?
A) If the contract is made at a lower price
B) If the first wakil later ratifies the contract
C) If the second wakil is a relative
D) If the principal is informed first

Key Takeaway
The validity of a sub-agent's contract in Hanafi law depends on the presence or subsequent ratification of the first wakil's opinion, reflecting the principal's underlying purpose.

Validity of a Sub-Agent's Contract in Hanafi Wakalah
Conditions for a wakil appointing a sub-wakil and validity of the sub-wakil's contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a sub-agent's contract is valid according to Hanafi fiqh and identify the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the reversion of contractual rights.

Core Idea
A sub-agent's contract is valid if the principal's objective (first agent's opinion) is present, either directly or through later approval.

The Hanafi school has detailed rules for agency (wakala), especially when an agent appoints a sub-agent without the principal's permission. This passage explores the validity of such sub-agency contracts, focusing on the presence of the first agent's opinion or its later confirmation. It also touches on the rights that arise from the contract, where scholars differ. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly applying the law of agency in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic scenario
The passage begins with an agent appointing a sub-agent without permission. Note the key condition: the sub-agent acts in the presence of the first agent. What makes this contract valid? The presence of the first agent's opinion.
2
Analyze the dispute on rights
After validity, the passage discusses to whom the rights of the contract revert. Some scholars say the first agent, others the second. Understand the reasoning: one side focuses on the principal's consent, the other on the cause of the contract.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the effect of the first agent's absence
When the sub-agent acts without the first agent present, the contract is invalid. But later approval can cure it. Also, an approval by the agent of a stranger's contract is similar.
4
Understand the role of price specification
A key nuance: if the first agent specifies the price in the sub-agent's presence, the sub-agent can sell even without the first agent because the need for opinion on price is met.
5
Consider the case of two agents appointed by the principal
If the principal appoints two agents for selling and specifies the price, both must act jointly. This is because the principal's intent is to combine their opinions, possibly to increase the price or find a good buyer.
This is distinct from the single agent scenario.

کی طرف راجع ہوں گے کیونکہ سبب یعنی عقد وکیل ثانی ہی کی طرف سے پایا گیا ہے۔ نہ کہ وکیل اول کی طرف سے اور جس کی طرف سے سبب یعنی عقد موجود ہوتا ہے۔ حقوق اسی کی طرف لوٹتے ہیں اس لئے حقوق وکیل ثانی کی طرف راجع ہوں گے اور اگر وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی عدم موجودگی میں عقد کیا تو یہ عقد جائز اور نافذ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں وکیل اول کی رائے مفقود ہوگئی ہے اور جب وکیل اول کی رائے فوت ہوگئی تو موکل کا مقصود حاصل نہیں ہوا اور جب مؤکل کا مقصود حاصل نہیں ہوا" عقد بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر وکیل ثانی کے عقد کی خبر وکیل اول کو پہنچ گئی اور وکیل اول نے اس عقد کی اجازت دیدی تو وکیل اول کی رائے کے متحقق ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ عقد جائز اور نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر وکیل کے علاوہ کسی اجنبی آدمی نے عقد کیا اور وکیاں کو جب اس عقد کی خبر موصول ہوئی تو اس نے اس کی اجازت دیدی پس جو اس صورت میں بھی یہ عقد جائز ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی وکیل کے اجازت دینے سے اس کی رائے موجود ہوگئی ہے۔ اور اگر وکیل اول نے وکیل ثانی کے سامنے اس چیز کا ثمن متعین کر دیا جس چیز کو بیچنے کا وکیل کیا گیا تھا۔ پھر وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی عدم موجودگی میں اس چیز کو اس متعین کردہ ثمن کے عوض فروخت کر دیا تو اسے فروخت کرنا یعنی عقد کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بظاہر عقد میں ثمن متعین کرنے کیلئے رائے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے اور یہ مقصد یعنی ثمن متعین کرنا حاصل ہو چکا ہے اور جب مقصود حاصل ہو چکا تو وکیل اول کا موجودہ ہونا ضروری نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر کسی شخص نے سامان بیچنے کے لئے دو وکیل مقرر کئے اور موکل نے اس سامان کا ثمن بھی متعین کر دیا تو متعینہ ثمن کے عوض صرف ایک وکیل کا فروخت کرنا درست نہ ہوگا بلکہ دونوں وکیلوں کی رائے کا جمع ہونا ضروری ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ موکل کا ثمن متعین کرنے کے باوجود مذکورہ شی کو فروخت کرنے کیلئے دو وکیلوں کو مقرر کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ موکل کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ دو وکیلوں کی رائے اکٹھا ہونے سے متعین کردہ ثمن میں اضافہ ہو جائے ۔ یا دونوں وکیل مل کر ایسا مشتری منتخب کریں جو ثمن ادا کرنے میں ٹال مٹول نہ کرے بہر حال جب ثمن متعین کرنے کے باوجود وکیل مقرر کرنے سے مؤکل کا یہ مقصد وابستہ ہے تو صرف ایک وکیل کا فروخت کرنا درست نہ ہوگا بلکہ دونوں کا ملا کر فروخت کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ لیکن جب مؤکل نے ثمن متعین نہیں کیا بلکہ عقد بیع وکیل اول کے سپرد کر دیا تو اس صورت میں موکل کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ عقد بیع کے سبب سے اہم معاملہ یعنی ثمن متعین کرنے میں وکیل اول کی رائے موجود ہو پس جب وکیل اول نے بیع کا ثمن متعین کر دیا تو ثمن متعین کرنے میں وکیل کی رائے حاصل ہوگئی اور جب وکیل اول کی رائے حاصل ہو گئی تو اس صورت میں وکیل ثانی کا وکیل اول کی عدم موجودگی میں بیچنا بھی درست ہو گا۔
Despite [the principal] entrusting the contract to two agents, it becomes apparent that the principal's purpose is to combine the opinions of both regarding increasing the price and choosing the buyer as we have explained. But when the price was not specified and the contract was entrusted to the first agent, the principal's greatest objective is to seek his opinion in determining the price. Explanation of the issue: If the agent, without the permission of his principal, appointed another as agent in the same matter in which he himself was appointed, and the second agent concluded the contract in the presence of the first agent, then this contract is valid and enforceable because the principal's intent was that the opinion of the first agent be present, and in this case, the opinion of the first agent was present. So when the opinion of the first agent was present, the principal's objective was achieved, and when the principal's objective was achieved, the contract concluded by the second agent is also valid. However, there is disagreement among scholars about to whom the rights of the contract concluded by the second agent revert. This disagreement arose because Imam Muhammad did not mention any ruling on this issue in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Nevertheless, some scholars said that the rights of this contract revert to the first agent, because the principal agreed that the responsibilities and rights of the contract revert to the first agent. And some scholars said that the rights of this contract revert to the second agent, because the cause, i.e., the contract, occurred on the part of the second agent, not the first agent, and to whose side the cause (the contract) exists, the rights revert to him. Therefore, the rights revert to the second agent. And if the second agent concluded the contract in the absence of the first agent, this contract is not valid and enforceable, because in this case the opinion of the first agent is missing, and when the opinion of the first agent is lost, the principal's objective is not achieved, and when the principal's objective is not achieved, the contract is also not valid. However, if news of the second agent's contract reached the first agent and the first agent gave permission for this contract, then due to the realization of the first agent's opinion, this contract becomes valid and enforceable. Similarly, if a stranger other than the agent concluded the contract and when the agent received news of this contract, he gave permission for it, then in this case also the contract becomes valid, because in this case also, due to the agent's permission, his opinion became present. And if the first agent specified the price of the item he was authorized to sell in the presence of the second agent, then the second agent sold this item for that specified price in the absence of the first agent, then this sale, i.e., the contract, is valid, because apparently, in the contract, the need for opinion is for specifying the price, and this objective, i.e., specifying the price, has been achieved, and when the objective has been achieved, the presence of the first agent is not necessary. But if a person appointed two agents to sell goods and the principal also specified the price of those goods, then selling by only one agent for the specified price is not valid; rather, the combination of both agents' opinions is necessary. The proof is that the principal, despite specifying the price, appointing two agents to sell the aforementioned item indicates that the principal's purpose is that by the combination of the two agents' opinions, the specified price may be increased, or both agents together may select a buyer who does not procrastinate in paying the price. In any case, when with the specification of the price, the principal's purpose is connected to appointing agents, then selling by only one agent is not valid; rather, both must combine to sell. But when the principal did not specify the price but entrusted the contract of sale to the first agent, then in this case the principal's purpose is that the opinion of the first agent be present in the important matter of the sale contract, i.e., specifying the price. So when the first agent specified the price of the sale, the agent's opinion in specifying the price was obtained, and when the first agent's opinion was obtained, then in this case, even selling by the second agent in the absence of the first agent is valid.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from a Hanafi commentary on the book of agency (Wakalah). It discusses the conditions under which a sub-agent's contract is valid. The first scenario: if an agent (wakil) appoints a sub-agent (wakil thani) without the principal's permission, and the sub-agent concludes the contract in the presence of the first agent, the contract is valid because the principal's objective—having the first agent's opinion—is achieved. However, there is a scholarly dispute about to whom the rights of the contract revert. Some say to the first agent, since the principal agreed to his responsibility; others say to the second agent, since he performed the contract. The text follows the latter view, emphasizing the cause of the contract. If the sub-agent acts in the first agent's absence, the contract is invalid unless the first agent later approves it. Similarly, if a stranger acts and the first agent approves, the contract becomes valid. A key nuance: if the first agent specifies the price in the sub-agent's presence, the sub-agent can sell even without the first agent, because the need for opinion on price is met. Conversely, if the principal appoints two agents and specifies the price, both must act jointly, as the principal's intent is to combine their opinions to possibly increase the price or find a reliable buyer. The ruling is based on the principal's presumed intent, not on explicit textual proof, so argument type is none.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakīl): An agent appointed by the principal (muwakkil) to act on his behalf in a specific matter, such as selling goods.
وکیل ثانی (wakīl thānī): A sub-agent appointed by the first wakil, either with or without the principal's permission.
ثمن (thaman): The price or consideration in a sale contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a contract by a sub-agent (wakīl thānī) valid even in the absence of the first agent?
A) When the sub-agent acts without the principal's approval
B) When the first agent has specified the price in the sub-agent's presence
C) When the principal has appointed two agents
D) When the sub-agent is a stranger

Key Takeaway
The validity of a sub-agent's contract hinges on the presence or subsequent realization of the first agent's opinion, with price specification substituting for presence.

beginner

Slave, Mukatab, and Dhimmi Cannot Act for Free Muslim Minor
Ruling on disqualification of certain persons as guardians for a free Muslim minor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that slaves, mukatabs, and dhimmis cannot validly act for a free Muslim minor, and explain the two proofs: severance of wilayah due to slavery/disbelief and the nature of wilayah nazariyyah requiring capability and sympathy.

Core Idea
Slavery and disbelief sever the legal guardianship (wilayah) required to act for a free Muslim minor.

This passage establishes a clear limitation on who can exercise guardianship over a free Muslim minor. The Hanafi school teaches that certain persons, namely slaves (including mukatabs) and dhimmis, lack the necessary legal authority to manage the minor's affairs, such as marriage or property transactions. The reasoning is rooted in both textual evidence (Quran) and the conceptual nature of guardianship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The author states that if a mukatab, slave, or dhimmi marries off his free Muslim minor daughter, or sells or buys for her, the act is not permissible (la yajuz). This applies to any disposal of her wealth. Note the scope: it covers all acts of guardianship, not just marriage.
2
Locate the first proof: severance of wilayah by slavery and disbelief
The author argues that slavery (riqq) and disbelief (kufr) sever wilayah. He supports this by analogy: a slave cannot even marry himself, so how can he marry another? Also, a disbeliever has no wilayah over a Muslim, as evidenced by the rejection of his testimony and the Quranic verse denying disbelievers any way over believers.
The Quranic verse (4:141) is cited: 'And Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers.'
3
Locate the second proof: wilayah nazariyyah requires capability and sympathy
The author introduces a second rationale: this guardianship is 'wilayah nazariyyah' (custodianship founded on care). Therefore, it must be delegated to someone who is both capable (qadir) and sympathetic (mushfiq). Slavery destroys capability (the slave is occupied by his master's service), and disbelief destroys sympathy towards a Muslim.
4
Synthesize the two proofs
Both proofs converge: slaves and mukatabs lack capability, dhimmis lack sympathy. Hence, none of them can validly exercise wilayah over a free Muslim minor, and their transactions are invalid (batil).
This double reasoning strengthens the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا زوج المكاتب او العبد او الذمي ابنته وهي صغيرة حرة مسلمة او باع او اشترى لها لم يجز معناه التصرف في مالها لان الرق والكفر يقطعان الولاية ألا ترى ان المملوك لا يملك انكاح نفسه فكيف يملك انكاح غيره وكذا الكافر لا ولاية له على المسلم حتى لا تقبل شهادته عليه ولان هذه ولاية نظرية فلابد من التفويض الى القادر المشفق ليتحقق معنى النظر والرق يزيل القدرة والكفر يقطع الشفقة على المسلم فلا تفوض اليهما

ترجمہ اور جب مکاتب نے یا غلام نے یا ذمی نے اپنی آزاد مسلمان صغیرہ بیٹی کا نکاح کیا یا اس کیلئے بچا یا خریدا تو جائز نہیں ہے اور اس کے معنی اسکے مال میں تصرف کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ رقیت اور کفر دونوں ولایت کو منقطع کر دیتے ہیں کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ مملوک اپنی ذات کا نکاح نہیں کر سکتا ہے تو غیر کا نکاح کیونکر کر سکے گا اور اسی طرح کافر کو مسلمان پر ولایت نہیں ہے۔ حتی کہ مسلمان کے خلاف کافر کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی ہے اور اس لئے کہ یہ ولایت نظری ہے لہذا قادر مشفق کے سپرد کرنا ضروری ہے تاکہ نظر اور شفقت کے معنی متحقق ہو سکیں۔ اور رقیت قدرت کو زائل کر دیتی ہے اور کفر مسلمان پر شفقت کو زائل کر دیتا ہے لہذا یہ ولایت ان دونوں کے سپرد نہ ہوگی۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مکاتب نے یا غلام نے یا ذمی نے اپنی آزاد مسلمان نابالغ بچی کا نکاح کیا یا اس کیلئے اسکا کوئی سامان فروخت کیا یا اس نے مال کے عوض اس کیلئے کچھ خریدا۔ تو یہ تمام تصرفات ناجائز ہوں گے متن میں بیع اور شراء سے مراد مطلق تصرف ہے یعنی ان حضرات کیلئے مذکورہ صغیرہ کے مال میں کسی طرح کے تصرف کا حق نہیں ہے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ رقیت اور کفر دونوں ولایت کو منقطع کر دیتے ہیں یعنی مذکورہ تصرفات ولایت کے قبیل سے ہیں۔ اور غلام اور مکاتب میں رقیت اور ذمی میں کفر ان کی ولایت کو ختم کر دیتے ہیں چنانچہ جب مملوک کو خود اپنا نکاح کرنے کی ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے۔ تو دوسرے کا نکاح کرنے کی ولایت کیسے حاصل ہوگی کیونکہ دوسرے پر ولایت کا حاصل ہونا اس بات کی فرع ہے کہ خود اس کو اپنی ذات پر بھروسہ حاصل ہو پس جب غلام اور مکاتب کو اپنی ذات پر ولایت حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور یہ سب کس طرح حاصل ہوگی جبکہ کافر کو مسلمان پر ولایت حاصل نہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ کافر کی گواہی مسلمان پر قبول نہیں۔

وَلَنْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ لِلْكَافِرِينَ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ سَبِيلًا تو اسکو مسلمان لڑکی کے نکاح پر ولایت کس طرح حاصل ہوگی۔

دوسری دلیل یہ کہ بچے اور بچیوں کیلئے جو ولایت ثابت ہے اس کا دارومدار نظر اور شفقت پر ہے لہذا صغیر اور صغیرہ پر اسی کو ولایت حاصل ہو گی جو قادر بھی ہو اور مشفق بھی ہو حالانکہ رقیت قدرت کو زائل کر دیتی ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے : ضَرَبَ اللَّهُ مَثَلاً عَبْدًا مَمْلُوكًا لَا يَقْدِرُ عَلَى شَيْءٍ اور کفر مسلمان پر شفقت کو ختم کر دیتا ہے۔

پس جب غلام اور مکاتب میں قدرت مفقود ہے اور ذمی کافر میں شفقت مفقود ہے تو ان کو ولایت بھی حاصل نہ ہوگی اور جب ان کو ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے تو ان کے تصرفات بھی معتبر نہ ہوں گے۔
He said: And when a mukatab, a slave, or a dhimmi marries off his daughter while she is a free Muslim minor, or sells or buys for her, it is not permissible. Its meaning is [that this is] disposal of her wealth, because slavery and disbelief sever legal authority. Do you not see that the enslaved one does not have the authority to marry himself, so how can he have the authority to marry another? Likewise, a disbeliever has no authority over a Muslim, to the extent that his testimony against a Muslim is not accepted. And because this authority is a custodianship (wilayah nazariyyah), so it must be delegated to one who is capable and sympathetic so that the meaning of care is realized. Slavery removes capability, and disbelief severs sympathy towards a Muslim, so it is not delegated to them.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage states a ruling and its proofs. The ruling is that a mukatab (a slave under contract to earn his freedom), an ordinary slave, or a dhimmi (a non-Muslim living under Muslim rule) cannot validly perform any act of guardianship (wilayah) over a free Muslim minor girl—whether marrying her off, selling her property, or buying for her. The author then explains that the word "marries" or "sells" in the text is general, covering all types of disposal of her wealth. The first proof is that slavery and disbelief sever wilayah. The text argues that if a slave cannot even contract his own marriage (because he lacks full capacity), how can he contract for another? Similarly, a disbeliever has no wilayah over a Muslim, as evidenced by the rejection of his testimony against a Muslim, and by the Quranic verse "And Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers" (4:141). The second proof is that this sort of guardianship is 'wilayah nazariyyah'—a custodianship founded on care and sympathy. Therefore, it must be entrusted to someone who is both capable (qadir) and sympathetic (mushfiq). Slavery destroys capability (since a slave is occupied by his master's service), while disbelief destroys sympathy towards a Muslim. Hence, these two groups are disqualified. The commentary then reinforces this with examples and further explanation, concluding that since slaves and mukatabs lack capability and dhimmis lack sympathy, they have no wilayah, and their transactions are invalid.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority or guardianship over another person or property, including the right to act on their behalf.
ولایت نظری (wilayah nazariyyah): Guardianship based on care and consideration (nazar) and sympathy (shafaqah) for the ward's interest.
مشفق (mushfiq): One who has sincere sympathy and compassion for another, essential for valid guardianship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because he is not a relative
B) Because disbelief severs sympathy (shafaqah) towards a Muslim
C) Because he is not mentally capable
D) Because the minor must choose

Key Takeaway
Slavery and disbelief sever the legal guardianship required to act for a free Muslim minor, making any such transaction invalid (batil).

Authority of Apostate and Harbi over Children's Property
Ruling on effectiveness of murtadd's and harbi's transactions regarding their own and children's property (intra-Hanafi dispute)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a murtadd's and harbi's transactions in their own and their child's property, and distinguish the Sahibayn's position from potential intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
An apostate's own property transactions are effective, but his dealings with his child's property are suspended — pending his return to Islam or death in apostasy.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the view of the two great students of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on the legal authority of an apostate (murtadd) and an enemy non-Muslim (harbi). The key distinction is between the apostate's own property and that of his Muslim child. Understanding this ruling requires examining the concept of wilayah nazariyyah (custodianship based on care) and the condition of religious unity between guardian and ward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Note the two types of individuals: murtadd (apostate) and harbi (enemy non-Muslim). Their rulings differ from that of a dhimmi.
2
Distinguish between own and child's property
For the murtadd: his own property transactions are effective (according to Sahibayn); for his child's property, they are suspended (mawquf). For the harbi: he has no authority at all over his Muslim child's property.
The harbi is more distant than the dhimmi, who already lacks authority.
3
Analyze the rationale for suspension
The father's authority over his child is wilayah nazariyyah, founded on care and sympathy. That requires unity of religion (ittihad al-millah). Since the murtadd's religious status is unsettled, the basis for sympathy is uncertain, leading to suspension.
4
Determine the consequence of suspension
If the murtadd returns to Islam, the transaction becomes valid; if he is killed or dies in apostasy, the transaction becomes void (batil).
This is by consensus (bil-ijma') regarding the child's property.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text presents Sahibayn's view. Abu Hanifa reportedly held that the murtadd's own property transactions are also suspended. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
The ikhtilaf is only about own property; child's property suspension is agreed upon.

مرتذ جب اپنی ردت میں قتل کیا گیا تو اس کا تصرف اس کے مال میں نافذ ہے لیکن والد اور ولد کے مال میں موقوف ہے یہی حکم حربی کا ہے

و قال ابويوسف ومحمد المرتد اذا قتل على ردته والحربي كذالك لان الحربي ابعد من الذمى فاولى بسلب الولاية واما المرتد فتصرفه فى ماله ان كان نافذاً عندهما لكنه موقوف على ولده ومال ولده بالاجماع لانها ولاية نظرية وذالك باتفاق الملة وهى مترددة ثم تستقر جهة الانقطاع اذا قتل على الردة سطلع والاسلام يجعل لم يزل كان مسلما

ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے کہا کہ مرتد جب اپنی ردت پر قتل کیا گیا اور حربی اسی طرح کیونکہ حربی ذمی سے بعید تر ہے تو بدرجہ اولی اس کی ولایت سلب ہوگی اور بہر حال مرتد تو صاحبین کے نزدیک اگر چہ اس کا تصرف اس کے مال میں نافذ ہے لیکن اسکا تصرف اسکے ولد اور اس کے والد کے مال پر بالاجماع موقوف ہے کیونکہ یہ ولایت نظری ہے اور نظر و شفقت ملت کے متفق ہونے کی صورت میں ہوتی ہے حالانکہ مرتد کی ملت متردد ہے پھر جب وہ اپنی ردت پر قتل کر دیا گیا تو انقطاع کی جہت مستقر ہوگئی۔ پس اس کا تصرف باطل ہو جائے گا اور اسلام کی وجہ سے ایسا قرار دیا جائے گا گویا وہ برابر مسلمان رہا لہذا اس کا تصرف درست ہوگا۔

تشریح صاحبین نے کہا کہ مرتد جب اپنی ردت پر قتل کیا گیا ہو اور حربی، ان دونوں کا تصرف ان کی مسلمان اولاد پر اور ان کے مال پر جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حربی اگر چہ مستامن ہو ذمی سے بعید تر ہے یعنی ذمی مسلمانوں سے قریب ہے بہ نسبت حربی کے اور پہلے گذر چکا ہے کہ ذمی کو مسلمان پر ولایت نہیں ہوتی لہذا حربی کو بدرجہ اولی مسلمان پر ولایت حاصل نہ ہوگی اور رہا مرتد تو اس کا تصرف اپنے مال میں صاحبین کے نزدیک اگر چہ نافذ ہے لیکن اس کا تصرف اس کی اولاد اور اسکی اولاد کے مال پر بالاجماع موقوف ہے۔ یعنی مرتد اگر مسلمان ہو گیا تو اسکا تصرف جائز ہوگا اور اگر مسلمان نہ ہوا بلکہ قتل کر دیا گیا یا مر گیا یا دارالحرب میں چلا گیا تو اس کا تصرف نافذ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ باپ کی ولایت اولاد اور مال اولاد پر نظری ہے یعنی باپ کو اپنی اولاد اور اولاد کے مال پر ولایت اس لئے حاصل ہوتی ہے کہ باپ اولاد کے حق میں مشفق ہوتا ہے لیکن باپ بیٹے کے درمیان نظر و شفقت اس وقت متحقق ہوتی ہے جبکہ ان دونوں کا مذہب اور ملت ایک ہو حالانکہ یہاں مرتد کی ملت متردد ہے یہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ دوبارہ اسلام قبول کرے اور یہ بھی ہوسکتا ہے کہ اسکو اسلام کی توفیق نہ ہو۔ حال جب مرتد کو بحالت ردت قتل کر دیا گیا تو باپ اور اولاد کے درمیان اتحاد ملت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی ولایت کا منقطع ہونا ہو گیا اور جب اسکی ولایت کا منقطع ہونا محقق ہو گیا تو اس کا تصرف بھی باطل ہو جائے گا اور اگر مرتد نے اسلام قبول کر لیا تو اسلام قبول کرنے کی وجہ سے ایسا ہو گیا گویا وہ برابر مسلمان چلا آرہا ہے اور جب اس صورت میں مسلمان چلا آ رہا ہے تو اتحاد ملت کی وجہ اسکی ولایت منقطع نہ ہوگی اور جب ولایت منقطع نہیں ہوتی تو اس کا تصرف بھی جائز اور نافذ ہوگا۔
When an apostate is killed during his apostasy, his disposal in his own property is effective, but it is suspended regarding the property of his father and son. The same ruling applies to a harbi.

Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The apostate when killed during his apostasy, and the harbi similarly — because the harbi is more distant than the dhimmi, so it is more fitting to strip of authority. As for the apostate, his disposal in his own property is effective according to them, but regarding his son and his son's property it is suspended by consensus, because this is custodianship (wilayah nazariyyah), and that requires agreement in religion, and [his religion] is unsettled. Then the cause of severance becomes established when he is killed during apostasy; and Islam makes it as if he never ceased to be a Muslim.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage presents the view of the two great Hanafi imams, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding the authority (wilayah) of an apostate (murtadd) and a harbi (an enemy non-Muslim from dar al-harb). The ruling has two parts: (1) for a harbi, the ruling is that he has absolutely no authority over his Muslim child or the child's property, because a harbi is even more distant from Muslims than a dhimmi, and dhimmis already lack such authority. (2) For an apostate, his transactions in his own property are effective while he is alive, but concerning his child and the child's property, they are suspended (mawquf) by consensus. The reason is that the father's authority over his child is a custodianship (wilayah nazariyyah) founded on care and sympathy, which in turn requires unity of religion (ittihad al-millah). Since an apostate's religious status is unsettled (mutaraddid)—he might return to Islam or remain in apostasy—the basis for sympathy is uncertain. If the apostate is killed while in apostasy, the suspension becomes permanent and the transaction becomes void (batil). However, if he returns to Islam, it is as if he never left the faith, so his authority is validated, and the transaction becomes effective. The commentary elaborates that the same principle applies if he dies or flees to dar al-harb without returning to Islam.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who renounces Islam (apostate). The passage discusses his legal capacity in relation to his own and his child's property.
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Islam (enemy combatant or citizen of dar al-harb).
ولایت نظری (wilayah nazariyyah): Guardianship based on care and supervision, requiring the guardian to be capable and sympathetic towards the ward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, what is the status of an apostate's transaction regarding his child's property?
A) Completely valid and effective
B) Completely invalid
C) Suspended, becoming valid if he returns to Islam
D) Only valid if the child is also an apostate

Key Takeaway
An apostate's authority over his child's property is suspended due to the uncertainty of religious unity; the transaction's validity hinges on his eventual fate.
